Belief in the Prophet's Basin (Hawd)
Affirmation of the Hawd and its purpose

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that belief in the Hawd is part of Ahl al-Sunnah's creed and that it is established by authentic reports.

Core Idea
The Prophet's basin on Judgment Day is a true gift for his nation.

This lesson affirms a key eschatological belief: the Hawd (basin) of the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ on the Day of Judgment. The author states that it is true, and that it is a provision for the Prophet's nation, repelling the good and fending off the evil. We explore the meaning of this belief and its foundation in prophetic reports.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage affirming the Hawd
Read the Arabic sentence about the Hawd and its translation. Notice the key terms: الحوض, غياث, برده الأخيار, يداد الأشرار.
2
Understand what the Hawd is
The Hawd is a special basin granted to the Prophet on the Day of Judgment. The author says it is 'true' meaning it is a reality we must believe in.
The phrase 'غياثًا لأمته' indicates it is a provision/succor for his nation.
3
Recognize the proof base
Even though this lesson focuses on the belief itself, the author mentions it is established by authentic reports. This prepares us for the next lesson on tawatur ma'nawi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالحَوْضُ الَّذِي أَكْرَمَهُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى بِهِ غِيَانًا لِأُمِّتِهِ حَقٌّ. (و) نقول: (الحوض) لرسول الله (الذي أكرمه الله تعالى به يوم القيامة (غيانًا لأمته) برده الأخيار ويُدَاد (١) عنه الأشرار (حق) ثابت بصحيح الأخبار (٢) التي يبلغ مجموعها التواتر المعنوي. (١) ذاد الراعي إبله عن الماء: منعها. انظر: المصباح المنير (ذود). (٢) هو أن يتواتر معنى في ضمن الفاظ مختلفة ولو كان المعنى المشترك فيه بطريق اللزوم، وذلك إن کثرت الأخبار في الوقائع واختلف فيها لكن كل واحد منها يشتمل على معنى مشترك بينها بجهة التضمن أو الالتزام فيحصل العلم بالقدر المشترك، وذلك كسخاء حاتم وشجاعة علي ؛ فوقائع حاتم فيها يحكي من عطاياه من فرس وإبل وغير ذلك تتضمن جوده فيعلم جوده وإن لم يعلم شيء من تلك القضايا بعينه، وقضايا علي في حروبه من أنه هزم في خيبر كذا وفعل في أحد كذا إلى غير ذلك تدل بالالتزام على شجاعته، وقد تواتر ذلك منه وإن كان شيء من تلك الجزئيات لم يبلغ القطع. انظر شرح الكوكب المنير ص (259 - 260)، الإبهاج شرح المنهاج (1843/5-1844).
And the basin which Allah the Exalted honored him with as a provision for his nation is true. (And) we say: The basin of the Messenger of Allah which Allah the Exalted honored him with on the Day of Judgment as a provision for his nation, repelling the good and fending off the evil ones, is true, established by authentic reports whose total reaches tawatur ma'nawi (massively transmitted meaning). (1) 'Dhada' the shepherd his camels from water: he prevented them. See al-Misbah al-Munir (dhawd). (2) It is that a meaning is transmitted via multiple chains within different wordings, even if the common meaning is by way of necessity (luzum). That is, when reports about events are numerous and differ, but each one includes a common meaning either by inclusion (tadamun) or implication (iltizam), then knowledge of the common element is obtained. For example, the generosity of Hatim and the bravery of Ali: the incidents of Hatim that narrate his gifts of horses, camels, etc. imply his generosity, so his generosity is known even if no single incident is known with certainty. And the incidents of Ali in his battles – that he defeated in Khaybar such and such, did in Uhud such and such, etc. – imply by necessity his bravery. And it has become mutawatir from him even if none of those particulars reach certainty. See Sharh al-Kawkab al-Munir pp. 259-260, al-Ibhaj Sharh al-Minhaj 5/1843-1844.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof. It begins by stating the belief: the Hawd (basin) of the Prophet on the Day of Judgment is true. The author then explains that this belief is established by sound authentic reports that collectively reach the level of tawatur ma'nawi. He defines tawatur ma'nawi as a type of multiple transmission where the same meaning is conveyed through different wordings, and the common meaning is known with certainty even if no single report is certain. He gives examples: the generosity of Hatim and the bravery of Ali are known through many individual reports that imply these qualities. Similarly, the existence of the Hawd is known through many hadiths that mention it. This is the proof.

الحوض
غياث

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) To punish the sinners
B) To provide water for the believers on the Day of Judgment
C) To honor the Prophet and as a provision for his nation
D) To test people's faith

Key Takeaway
The Hawd is a true, literal basin that Allah has granted His Prophet as a provision for his believing community on the Day of Judgment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The Hawd is a mercy for the believers, but it also means accountability. Are you living as if you will be among those who are repelled, or among those who drink? What evidence in your life supports your answer?

The Proof of Tawatur Ma'nawi
Definition and examples of tawatur ma'nawi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the concept of tawatur ma'nawi and how it establishes certainty from multiple varied reports.

Core Idea
Tawatur ma'nawi: many different reports conveying the same meaning yield certain knowledge.

After affirming the Hawd, the author explains the evidential method that underpins this belief: tawatur ma'nawi. This is a kind of multiple transmission where the common meaning, not the exact wording, becomes certain. The lesson clarifies this concept using classic examples of Hatim's generosity and Ali's bravery, showing how it applies to the Hawd.

Guided Path
1
Read the explanation of tawatur ma'nawi
Read the Arabic definition and the examples. Identify the key condition: different wordings sharing a common meaning.
2
Understand the two examples
The passage uses Hatim al-Ta'i (generosity) and Ali ibn Abi Talib (bravery) to illustrate how many individual reports imply a common attribute.
Note the terms: بالتضمن (by inclusion) and بالالتزام (by implication).
3
Apply to the Hawd
Similarly, many hadiths about the Hawd, though varied, all share the common meaning that the Prophet has a basin on Judgment Day. This collective transmission becomes certain.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالحَوْضُ الَّذِي أَكْرَمَهُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى بِهِ غِيَانًا لِأُمِّتِهِ حَقٌّ. (و) نقول: (الحوض) لرسول الله (الذي أكرمه الله تعالى به يوم القيامة (غيانًا لأمته) برده الأخيار ويُدَاد (١) عنه الأشرار (حق) ثابت بصحيح الأخبار (٢) التي يبلغ مجموعها التواتر المعنوي. (١) ذاد الراعي إبله عن الماء: منعها. انظر: المصباح المنير (ذود). (٢) هو أن يتواتر معنى في ضمن الفاظ مختلفة ولو كان المعنى المشترك فيه بطريق اللزوم، وذلك إن کثرت الأخبار في الوقائع واختلف فيها لكن كل واحد منها يشتمل على معنى مشترك بينها بجهة التضمن أو الالتزام فيحصل العلم بالقدر المشترك، وذلك كسخاء حاتم وشجاعة علي ؛ فوقائع حاتم فيها يحكي من عطاياه من فرس وإبل وغير ذلك تتضمن جوده فيعلم جوده وإن لم يعلم شيء من تلك القضايا بعينه، وقضايا علي في حروبه من أنه هزم في خيبر كذا وفعل في أحد كذا إلى غير ذلك تدل بالالتزام على شجاعته، وقد تواتر ذلك منه وإن كان شيء من تلك الجزئيات لم يبلغ القطع. انظر شرح الكوكب المنير ص (259 - 260)، الإبهاج شرح المنهاج (1843/5-1844).
And the basin which Allah the Exalted honored him with as a provision for his nation is true. (And) we say: The basin of the Messenger of Allah which Allah the Exalted honored him with on the Day of Judgment as a provision for his nation, repelling the good and fending off the evil ones, is true, established by authentic reports whose total reaches tawatur ma'nawi (massively transmitted meaning). (1) 'Dhada' the shepherd his camels from water: he prevented them. See al-Misbah al-Munir (dhawd). (2) It is that a meaning is transmitted via multiple chains within different wordings, even if the common meaning is by way of necessity (luzum). That is, when reports about events are numerous and differ, but each one includes a common meaning either by inclusion (tadamun) or implication (iltizam), then knowledge of the common element is obtained. For example, the generosity of Hatim and the bravery of Ali: the incidents of Hatim that narrate his gifts of horses, camels, etc. imply his generosity, so his generosity is known even if no single incident is known with certainty. And the incidents of Ali in his battles – that he defeated in Khaybar such and such, did in Uhud such and such, etc. – imply by necessity his bravery. And it has become mutawatir from him even if none of those particulars reach certainty. See Sharh al-Kawkab al-Munir pp. 259-260, al-Ibhaj Sharh al-Minhaj 5/1843-1844.
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof. It begins by stating the belief: the Hawd (basin) of the Prophet on the Day of Judgment is true. The author then explains that this belief is established by sound authentic reports that collectively reach the level of tawatur ma'nawi. He defines tawatur ma'nawi as a type of multiple transmission where the same meaning is conveyed through different wordings, and the common meaning is known with certainty even if no single report is certain. He gives examples: the generosity of Hatim and the bravery of Ali are known through many individual reports that imply these qualities. Similarly, the existence of the Hawd is known through many hadiths that mention it. This is the proof.

Key Terms
التواتر المعنوي
بالتضمن
بالالتزام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that tawatur requires identical wording across all reports.
Correction: Tawatur ma'nawi shows that even with different wordings, if the reports share a common meaning, they can collectively reach certainty.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how does tawatur ma'nawi produce knowledge?
A) Through a single report with many chains
B) Through many reports with identical wording
C) Through many reports with different wordings that share a common meaning
D) Through rational deduction

Key Takeaway
Tawatur ma'nawi is a method of establishing certainty from multiple varied reports that agree on a common message, applicable to the Hawd and other beliefs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have heard many reports about the Prophet's mercy, patience, and justice. Have you let them converge into certain knowledge that reshapes how you treat others? Or do you brush each account aside as just another story?
?
The many hadith about the Hawd all point to one certain truth: you will face your deeds. Does this certainty make you weep over your sins tonight, or do you live as if it were a distant possibility?
?
Ali's bravery was known through scattered battle reports. You have the entire Quran and sunnah before you. What common message do they all scream that you have been silencing? Will you answer it today?

Hadith Evidence for the Prophet's Basin
Enumeration of hadiths about the Hawd.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific hadith evidence from Bukhari and Muslim that describe the Prophet's basin, including its dimensions, water quality, and cups.

Core Idea
Multiple authentic hadiths describe the Prophet's basin in vivid detail.

The author begins by presenting a collection of hadiths from the most authentic sources, Bukhari and Muslim, that provide detailed descriptions of the Prophet's basin. These narrations, transmitted by several Companions, establish the existence and attributes of the Hawd as a concrete reality. The hadiths emphasize the vast size, the pureness of its water, and the abundance of its drinking vessels.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadiths carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Notice the sensory details: distance, water color, scent, cups.
There are multiple hadiths; each adds a detail.
2
Identify the Companions
Note that these hadiths are narrated by Abdullah ibn Amr, Anas, and Abu Dharr among others. This shows widespread transmission.
The author states the hadiths are 'very many from groups of Companions'.
3
Reflect on the purpose
Ask why these descriptions are given. They assure believers of the Prophet's gift and encourage hope.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ففي صحيح البخاري ومسلم عن عبد الله بن عمرو بن العاص قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «حَوْضِي مَسِيرَةَ شَهْرٍ مَاؤُهُ أَبْيَضُ مِنَ اللَّبَنِ، وَرِيحُهُ أَطْيَبُ مِنَ المِسْكِ وَكِيزَانُهُ كَنُجُومِ السَّمَاءِ مَنْ شَرِبَ مِنْهُ لَا يَظْمَأُ أَبَدًا» (۳), وفي رواية لهما: حَوْضِي مَسِيرةَ شَهْرٍ زَوَايَاهُ سَوَاءٌ وَمَاؤُهُ أَبْيَضُ مِنَ الوَرِقِ)، وحديث أنس عندهما أيضًا: «مَا بَيْنَ نَاحِيَتَي حَوْضِي كَمَا بَيْنَ صَنْعَاءَ وَالمَدِينَةِ»(3), وفي رواية لهما: مِثْلُ مَا بَيْنَ المَدِينَةِ وَعُمان» (١), وفي رواية لمسلم من حديث أبي ذر : عَرْضُهُ مِثلُ طُولِهِ مَا بَيْنَ عُمَان إِلَى أَيْلَةَ ()، والأحاديث في الصحيحين وغيرهما كثيرة جدا من روايات جماعات من الصحابة. تنبیهان. الأول: قد فسر بعضهم الكوثر بالحوض، وهو قول عطاء (1) من المفسرين ويمكن أن يستدل له بحديث الصحيحين عن أنس بينا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بين أظهرنا إذ أغفى إغفاءة في المسجد، ثم رفع رأسه مبتسما؛ فقلنا: ما أضحكك يا رسول الله؟ قال: «أُنزِلَتْ عَلَيَّ أَنها سُورَةٌ، فقرأ: ﴿بِسْمِ اللَّهِ الرَّحْمَنِ الرَّحِيمِ إِنَّا أَعْطَيْنَاكَ الْكَوْثَرَ فَصَلِّ لِرَبِّكَ وَأَكْخَرَ إِنَّ شَائِكَ هُوَ الْأَبْتَر [سورة الكوثر ، ثم قال: «أَتَدْرُونَ مَا الكَوْثَرُ»، قلنا: الله تعالى ورسوله أعلم، قال: «فَإِنَّهُ نَهْرٌ وَعَدَنِيهِ رَبِّ كَ عَلَيْهِ خَيْرٌ كَثِيرٌ هُوَ حَوْضٌ تَرِدُ عَلَيْهِ أُمَّتِي يَومَ القِيَامَةِ آنِيَتُهُ عَدَدُ نُجُومِ السَّمَاءِ» (۲) الحديث، وإنما يتجه الاستدلال إذا جعلنا قوله: «هُوَ حَوْضُ» عائدًا إلى النهر، والظاهر أنه خبر عن الخير الكثير، وأن ذلك الخير الكثير هو الحوض؛ ففي رواية في الصحيحين أن الكوثر نهر في الجنة عليه حوضي ](٣)، ولفظ البخاري بيتها أَنَا أَسِيرُ فِي الجَنَّةِ إِذْ أَنَا بِنَهْرٍ حَافَتَاهُ قِبَابُ الدُّرُ الجَوْفِ قُلْتُ مَا هَذَا يَا جِبْرِيلُ قَالَ هَذَا الكَوثَرُ الَّذِي أَعْطَاكَ رَبُّكَ فَإِذَا طِيهُ - أَوْ طينهُ - مِسْكَ أَذْفَرُه ) . ففي ذلك وغيره من الأحاديث صريح بأنه نهر؛ فمعنى قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم خَيرٌ كَثِيرٌ هُوَ حَوْضُ أن النهر يمد الحوض وأن ماءه منه، وفي رواية لمسلم في صفة الحوض: إنَّ
In Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim from Abdullah ibn Amr ibn al-As said: The Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم said: 'My basin is a month's journey, its water is whiter than milk, its smell is more fragrant than musk, its cups are like the stars of the sky; whoever drinks from it will never thirst forever' (3). And in a narration from both: 'My basin is a month's journey, its sides are equal, its water is whiter than silver.' And the hadith of Anas from both: 'The distance between the two sides of my basin is like between San'a and Medina.' And in a narration from both: 'Like between Medina and Oman.' And in a narration from Muslim from Abu Dharr: 'Its width is like its length, between Oman and Ayla.' And the hadiths in the two Sahihs and other books are very many from narrations of groups of Companions. Two notes. First: Some have interpreted al-Kawthar as the basin, and that is the saying of Ata (1) among the exegetes, and one can adduce for it the hadith in the two Sahihs from Anas: 'While the Messenger of Allah صلى الله عليه وسلم was among us, he dozed a doze in the mosque, then raised his head smiling; we said: What makes you laugh, O Messenger of Allah? He said: A surah was revealed to me, and he recited: In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful: Indeed, We have granted you al-Kawthar. So pray to your Lord and sacrifice. Indeed, your enemy is the one cut off. Then he said: Do you know what al-Kawthar is? We said: Allah and His Messenger know best. He said: It is a river that my Lord promised me; upon it is much good; it is a basin at which my nation will come on the Day of Judgment; its cups are as many as the stars of the sky.' (2) The hadith. And the evidence is valid only if we make his statement 'it is a basin' refer to the river, and the apparent meaning is that it is news of the much good, and that that much good is the basin. For in a narration in the two Sahihs: 'al-Kawthar is a river in Paradise upon which my basin is.' And the wording of Bukhari: 'I was walking in Paradise when suddenly I was at a river whose banks were domes of hollow pearl. I said: What is this, O Jibril? He said: This is al-Kawthar which your Lord gave you. Then its mud, or its clay, was fragrant musk.' So in this and other hadiths it is clear that it is a river. So the meaning of his statement صلى الله عليه وسلم 'much good, it is a basin' is that the river feeds the basin and that its water is from it. And in a narration from Muslim about the description of the basin: 'Indeed...'
Source pages p. 90

Commentary
This passage provides the hadith evidence for the existence of the Prophet's basin. The author quotes several specific hadiths from Bukhari and Muslim detailing dimensions, qualities, and the fact that many Companions narrated these. Then he presents two notes (tanbihan). The first note discusses the interpretation of al-Kawthar (Surah al-Kawthar) as the basin. Some exegetes like Ata interpret it that way. The author cites the hadith where the Prophet explains that al-Kawthar is a river and a basin for his nation. He then analyzes the grammar: the phrase 'huwa hawd' could refer to the river or to the 'much good'. The preferred view is that the river feeds the basin. The passage ends mid-explanation, indicating the discussion continues.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

Interpreting al-Kawthar as the Basin
Discussion of tafsir linking al-Kawthar to the basin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the connection between the river of al-Kawthar and the Prophet's basin, and the reasoning behind interpreting al-Kawthar as the basin.

Core Idea
Al-Kawthar is a river in Paradise that feeds the Prophet's basin.

After citing the hadith evidence for the basin, the author turns to a theological note: the interpretation of the Quranic term 'al-Kawthar'. Some exegetes, like Ata, considered al-Kawthar to be the basin itself. However, other hadiths indicate that al-Kawthar is a river from which the basin is filled. The author analyzes the relevant hadith to clarify the relationship, explaining that the river feeds the basin.

Guided Path
1
Read the interpretation and proof
Read the passage about the first note: some interpret al-Kawthar as the basin, citing Ata. Then read the hadith from Anas that connects al-Kawthar to a river and a basin.
The hadith is from the two Sahihs.
2
Analyze the grammar
Notice the phrase 'huwa hawd' in the hadith. The author discusses whether 'huwa' refers to the river or to 'khayr kathir'. Understand the reasoning.
The author leans that it refers to the 'much good', which is the basin.
3
Understand the final relationship
From other hadiths, it is clear that al-Kawthar is a river in Paradise, and the basin is fed from it. This resolves the apparent contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ففي صحيح البخاري ومسلم عن عبد الله بن عمرو بن العاص قال : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «حَوْضِي مَسِيرَةَ شَهْرٍ مَاؤُهُ أَبْيَضُ مِنَ اللَّبَنِ، وَرِيحُهُ أَطْيَبُ مِنَ المِسْكِ وَكِيزَانُهُ كَنُجُومِ السَّمَاءِ مَنْ شَرِبَ مِنْهُ لَا يَظْمَأُ أَبَدًا» (۳), وفي رواية لهما: حَوْضِي مَسِيرةَ شَهْرٍ زَوَايَاهُ سَوَاءٌ وَمَاؤُهُ أَبْيَضُ مِنَ الوَرِقِ)، وحديث أنس عندهما أيضًا: «مَا بَيْنَ نَاحِيَتَي حَوْضِي كَمَا بَيْنَ صَنْعَاءَ وَالمَدِينَةِ»(3), وفي رواية لهما: مِثْلُ مَا بَيْنَ المَدِينَةِ وَعُمان» (١), وفي رواية لمسلم من حديث أبي ذر : عَرْضُهُ مِثلُ طُولِهِ مَا بَيْنَ عُمَان إِلَى أَيْلَةَ ()، والأحاديث في الصحيحين وغيرهما كثيرة جدا من روايات جماعات من الصحابة. تنبیهان. الأول: قد فسر بعضهم الكوثر بالحوض، وهو قول عطاء (1) من المفسرين ويمكن أن يستدل له بحديث الصحيحين عن أنس بينا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بين أظهرنا إذ أغفى إغفاءة في المسجد، ثم رفع رأسه مبتسما؛ فقلنا: ما أضحكك يا رسول الله؟ قال: «أُنزِلَتْ عَلَيَّ أَنها سُورَةٌ، فقرأ: ﴿بِسْمِ اللَّهِ الرَّحْمَنِ الرَّحِيمِ إِنَّا أَعْطَيْنَاكَ الْكَوْثَرَ فَصَلِّ لِرَبِّكَ وَأَكْخَرَ إِنَّ شَائِكَ هُوَ الْأَبْتَر [سورة الكوثر ، ثم قال: «أَتَدْرُونَ مَا الكَوْثَرُ»، قلنا: الله تعالى ورسوله أعلم، قال: «فَإِنَّهُ نَهْرٌ وَعَدَنِيهِ رَبِّ كَ عَلَيْهِ خَيْرٌ كَثِيرٌ هُوَ حَوْضٌ تَرِدُ عَلَيْهِ أُمَّتِي يَومَ القِيَامَةِ آنِيَتُهُ عَدَدُ نُجُومِ السَّمَاءِ» (۲) الحديث، وإنما يتجه الاستدلال إذا جعلنا قوله: «هُوَ حَوْضُ» عائدًا إلى النهر، والظاهر أنه خبر عن الخير الكثير، وأن ذلك الخير الكثير هو الحوض؛ ففي رواية في الصحيحين أن الكوثر نهر في الجنة عليه حوضي ](٣)، ولفظ البخاري بيتها أَنَا أَسِيرُ فِي الجَنَّةِ إِذْ أَنَا بِنَهْرٍ حَافَتَاهُ قِبَابُ الدُّرُ الجَوْفِ قُلْتُ مَا هَذَا يَا جِبْرِيلُ قَالَ هَذَا الكَوثَرُ الَّذِي أَعْطَاكَ رَبُّكَ فَإِذَا طِيهُ - أَوْ طينهُ - مِسْكَ أَذْفَرُه ) . ففي ذلك وغيره من الأحاديث صريح بأنه نهر؛ فمعنى قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم خَيرٌ كَثِيرٌ هُوَ حَوْضُ أن النهر يمد الحوض وأن ماءه منه، وفي رواية لمسلم في صفة الحوض: إنَّ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think al-Kawthar and the basin are one and the same thing.

What is the relationship between al-Kawthar and the basin according to the author?
A) They are the same thing.

D) The basin is larger than the river.

Key Takeaway
Al-Kawthar is a river in Paradise that supplies the Prophet's basin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that the Prophet's basin has cups as numerous as the stars, do you truly believe you will be among those who drink from it? What in your life today reflects that hope?
?
The Prophet smiled when told about al-Kawthar. Does your heart ever smile at the thought of the gifts Allah has prepared for you? Or has worldly worry stolen that joy?
?
If you were asked today, 'Do you know what al-Kawthar is?', would you be able to answer with the same certainty as the Prophet's companions? What steps will you take to make the unseen realities more real to you?

First Warning: Interpreting al-Kawthar as the Basin
The author presents and supports the interpretation of al-Kawthar as the basin (hawd).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Qur'anic term 'al-Kawthar' refers to both a river in Paradise and the basin (al-ḥawḍ) from which the Prophet's community will drink on the Day of Resurrection, and how scriptural evidence reconciles these descriptions.

Core Idea
Al-Kawthar is both a river and a basin, the river feeding the basin with its water.

This lesson explores the first warning (tanbīh) in the commentary, which addresses a specific interpretation of al-Kawthar. Some exegetes, like ‘Aṭā’, understood al-Kawthar to be the basin (al-ḥawḍ) reserved for the Prophet’s community on the Day of Judgment. However, other hadiths describe al-Kawthar as a river in Paradise. The author presents key evidence to reconcile these views, showing that al-Kawthar is both a river and a basin, with the river supplying the basin.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal English translation. Pay attention to the flow of the argument and the key terms.
The passage includes a full hadith from the two Ṣaḥīḥs.
2
Identify the main claim
Notice that the author starts by stating that some interpreters (like ‘Aṭā’) have interpreted al-Kawthar as the basin. This is the claim under discussion.
3
Understand the hadith evidence
The author then brings a hadith to support this interpretation. Read the hadith carefully, noting the Prophet's words: 'It is a river... it is a basin.'
The inference depends on interpreting the pronoun 'huwa' in 'huwa ḥawḍ' as referring back to the river.
4
Grasp the relationship between river and basin
The author explains that the phrase 'abundant good' refers to the basin, and that the river supplies the basin. Study the additional narrations from Bukhārī and Muslim that clarify this relationship.
The key point is that the basin receives its water from the river, so they are not separate entities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأول: قد فسر بعضهم الكوثر بالحوض، وهو قول عطاء من المفسرين ويمكن أن يستدل له بحديث الصحيحين عن أنس بينا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بين أظهرنا إذ أغفى إغفاءة في المسجد، ثم رفع رأسه مبتسما؛ فقلنا: ما أضحكك يا رسول الله؟ قال: «أُنزِلَتْ عَلَيَّ أَنها سُورَةٌ، فقرأ: ﴿بِسْمِ اللَّهِ الرَّحْمَنِ الرَّحِيمِ إِنَّا أَعْطَيْنَاكَ الْكَوْثَرَ فَصَلِّ لِرَبِّكَ وَأَكْخَرَ إِنَّ شَائِكَ هُوَ الْأَبْتَر [سورة الكوثر ، ثم قال: «أَتَدْرُونَ مَا الكَوْثَرُ»، قلنا: الله تعالى ورسوله أعلم، قال: «فَإِنَّهُ نَهْرٌ وَعَدَنِيهِ رَبِّ كَ عَلَيْهِ خَيْرٌ كَثِيرٌ هُوَ حَوْضٌ تَرِدُ عَلَيْهِ أُمَّتِي يَومَ القِيَامَةِ آنِيَتُهُ عَدَدُ نُجُومِ السَّمَاءِ» الحديث، وإنما يتجه الاستدلال إذا جعلنا قوله: «هُوَ حَوْضُ» عائدًا إلى النهر، والظاهر أنه خبر عن الخير الكثير، وأن ذلك الخير الكثير هو الحوض؛ ففي رواية في الصحيحين أن الكوثر نهر في الجنة عليه حوضي، ولفظ البخاري أنا أسير في الجنة إذ أنا بنهر حافتاه قباب الدر الجوف قلت ما هذا يا جبريل قال هذا الكوثر الذي أعطاك ربك فإذا طينه - أو طينه - مسك أذفر. ففي ذلك وغيره من الأحاديث صريح بأنه نهر؛ فمعنى قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم خَيرٌ كَثِيرٌ هُوَ حَوْضُ أن النهر يمد الحوض وأن ماءه منه، وفي رواية لمسلم في صفة الحوض: إنَّ مَاءَهُ أَشَدُّ بَيَاضًا مِنَ اللَّبَنِ وَأَحْلَى مِنَ العَسَلِ يَغُتُ فِيهِ مِيزَابَانِ يَمُدَّانِهِ مِنَ الجَنَّةِ أَحَدُهُمَا مِنْ ذَهَبِ وَالآخَرُ مِنْ وَرِقٍ؛ يقال : غت الماء - بغين معجمة فمثناة فوقية - يغْتُ -بالضم - إذا جرى جريا متتابعا له صوت وتدفق.
The first: Some interpreters have interpreted al-Kawthar as the basin (al-hawḍ), and it is the saying of ‘Aṭā’ among the exegetes. It can be supported by the ḥadīth of the two Ṣaḥīḥs from Anas: While the Messenger of Allah ﷺ was among us, he dozed a doze in the mosque, then he raised his head smiling; so we said: What makes you laugh, O Messenger of Allah? He said: 'A sūrah has been revealed to me,' and he recited: 'In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Indeed, We have granted you al-Kawthar. So pray to your Lord and sacrifice. Indeed, your enemy is the one cut off.' [Sūrat al-Kawthar], then he said: 'Do you know what al-Kawthar is?' We said: Allah and His Messenger know best. He said: 'Indeed, it is a river that my Lord has promised me, upon it is abundant good. It is a basin (ḥawḍ) upon which my community will come on the Day of Resurrection; its vessels are as numerous as the stars of the sky.' The inference is valid only if we take his saying 'it is a basin' as referring to the river, and apparently it is a predicate of 'abundant good', and that abundant good is the basin. For in a narration in the two Ṣaḥīḥs that al-Kawthar is a river in Paradise upon which is my basin, and the wording of al-Bukhārī: 'I was walking in Paradise when suddenly I came to a river whose banks were domes of hollowed pearl. I said: What is this, O Gabriel? He said: This is al-Kawthar which your Lord has given you. Its clay – or its mud – was fragrant musk.' So in this and other ḥadīths it is explicit that it is a river. Thus the meaning of his ﷺ saying 'abundant good, it is a basin' is that the river supplies the basin and that its water is from it. And in a narration of Muslim describing the basin: 'Its water is whiter than milk and sweeter than honey. Two spouts pour into it, supplying it from Paradise, one of gold and the other of silver.' It is said: ghatta al-mā’ (with ghayn and tā’) yaghuttu (with ḍamma) if it flows continuously with sound and gushing.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is the first of two warnings (tanbīhāt) within the commentary on the creed regarding al-Kawthar. The author begins by stating that some exegetes—specifically ‘Aṭā’—interpreted al-Kawthar as the basin (ḥawḍ). He then provides a ḥadīth from the two Ṣaḥīḥs (Bukhārī and Muslim) via Anas ibn Mālik to support this interpretation. In the ḥadīth, the Prophet ﷺ defines al-Kawthar as a river promised to him, on which is abundant good, and he says 'it is a basin' (huwa ḥawḍ). The author notes that the proof depends on taking the pronoun 'huwa' (it) to refer back to the river, which is the apparent meaning. He clarifies that the phrase 'abundant good' is actually the predicate of the basin, i.e., the abundant good is the basin itself. He then cites another narration from Bukhārī that describes al-Kawthar as a river in Paradise with domes of pearls and its clay as musk. This confirms that al-Kawthar is a river. Therefore, the Prophet's ﷺ statement 'abundant good, it is a basin' means that the river feeds the basin and its water originates from the river. Finally, he quotes Muslim's description of the basin: its water is extremely white and sweet, and it is supplied by two spouts from Paradise, one of gold and one of silver. He concludes by explaining the rare word 'yaghuttu' (غت) meaning continuous flowing with sound. This passage thus establishes the identity of al-Kawthar as both a river and a basin, reconciling the scriptural references.

Key Terms
الكوثر
الحوض
النهر
الغت

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think al-Kawthar is only the basin or only the river, treating them as separate entities without connection.
Correction: The author clarifies that al-Kawthar is both a river and a basin, with the river feeding the basin. They are not separate; the basin receives its water from the river.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relationship between the river (al-Kawthar) and the basin (al-ḥawḍ)?
A) They are completely separate entities.
B) The basin is the river, and the river is the basin—they are identical.
C) The river supplies the basin, and its water originates from the river.
D) The basin is only a metaphor for the river.

Key Takeaway
Al-Kawthar refers to both a river in Paradise and the basin (ḥawḍ) from which the Prophet's community will drink; the river supplies the basin with its water.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just learned that the Prophet ﷺ was promised al-Kawthar, a river and basin for his community. On that Day, will you be among those who rush to his basin? What in your life right now shows that you are preparing for that encounter?
?
The water of the basin is whiter than milk and sweeter than honey, yet it is only for those who follow the Prophet sincerely. Are you quenching your spiritual thirst with anything that will leave you barred from that drink? What attachment must you sever today to ensure you are not turned away?
?
The Prophet's basin is fed by a river from Paradise, a gift from Allah to him. When you think of the blessings Allah has given you, do you recognize them as gifts to draw you closer to Him, or do you take them for granted? What is one blessing you have neglected to thank Him for, that could become a means of reaching the basin?

Reconciling Reports on the Basin's Size
The author reconciles differing reports about the size of the basin and adds a conclusion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how apparent contradictions in hadith about the basin's size are resolved by recognizing the intent to convey vastness rather than exact measurement, and learn about the two basins mentioned by al-Qurṭubī.

Core Idea
The basin's reported dimensions teach us about its vastness, not its exact size.

The scholars of Ahl al-Sunnah approach apparent contradictions in sacred texts with respect and a sincere effort to reconcile. In this passage, the commentator addresses differing reports about the size of the Prophet's basin (al-Ḥawḍ). He explains that the variations are not contradictions but rather different ways of describing its unimaginable vastness, tailored to the understanding of each audience. This lesson will walk you through that reconciliation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
The passage has two parts: the reconciliation and an appendix from al-Qurṭubī.
2
Identify the problem being addressed
Notice that the author mentions disagreement (اختلاف) in the reports about the basin's size. Ask yourself: why would different narrations give different measurements?
This is the second warning (تنبيه) in the commentary.
3
Understand the reconciliation principle
The author says the intent is not precise estimation but rather to inform of the basin's extreme vastness. Observe how he explains that the Prophet ﷺ described it to different groups in terms they understood.
Some reports mention distance, others mention time (a month's journey).
4
Consider the two-basin solution
Al-Qurṭubī is cited to mention that the Prophet ﷺ has two basins, both called al-Kawthar: one before the Ṣirāṭ and one in Paradise. This resolves location differences.
This is an appendix (تتمة) to the main reconciliation.
5
Reflect on the broader lesson
Think about how this reconciliation teaches us to approach similar textual issues: look for the intended meaning rather than insisting on literal uniformity.
This principle is key in Islamic creedal methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني: قد اختلف في تقدير الحوض كما مر ويجمع بينها بأنه ليس القصد تقدير تحديد إنها القصد الإعلام بسعة الحوض جدا وأنه ليس كحياض الدنيا، وقد تكرر منه وصفه بذلك فخاطب في وصفه لكل فريق بما يعرفه من مسافة بعيدة ومنهم من قدر له المسافة بالزمان لا بالمكان فقال: «مسيرة شهر من غير قصد تحديد كما قدمناه. تتمة: ذكر القرطبي في التذكرة أن النبي لحوضين كلاهما يسمى الكوثر أحدهما قبل الصراط والثاني في الجنة.
The second: There has been disagreement concerning the estimation of the basin as has passed. And a reconciliation between them is that the intent is not estimation and delimitation; rather the intent is to inform of the extreme vastness of the basin and that it is not like the basins of this world. And his description of it has been repeated thus; so he addressed, in his description of it, each group with what they know of a distant distance. And among them are those who estimated the distance by time rather than by place, so he said: 'a month's journey' without intending delimitation, as we have mentioned previously. Appendix: al-Qurṭubī mentioned in al-Tadhkirah that the Prophet ﷺ has two basins, both called al-Kawthar: one before the Ṣirāṭ and the second in Paradise.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is the second warning (tanbīh) of the commentary. The author addresses the fact that there are varying reports about the precise size of the basin (ḥawḍ). He states that the correct reconciliation is that the different estimates are not meant to give an exact measurement; rather they are intended to convey the immense vastness of the basin, which is unlike any earthly basin. The Prophet ﷺ described it to different groups in terms they understood—some in terms of distance (e.g., a journey of a month) and others in terms of time (e.g., a month's journey), without intending a precise delimitation. The author then adds a supplementary note (tatimma) from al-Qurṭubī's book al-Tadhkirah, which mentions that the Prophet ﷺ actually has two basins, both called al-Kawthar: one before the Ṣirāṭ (the bridge over Hell) and the second inside Paradise. This reconciles reports that seem to place the basin in different locations. The passage thus resolves apparent contradictions in the ḥadīth literature about the basin's size and location by emphasizing the underlying intent of describing its vastness and by distinguishing two separate basins.

Key Terms
تقدير الحوض
السعة
المسافة
الصراط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The varying measurements of the basin contradict each other, indicating uncertainty or error.
Correction: The reports are not contradictory because they serve to describe the basin's vastness, not to give precise dimensions. The Prophet ﷺ tailored descriptions to his audience.

Checkpoint
How does the author reconcile different reports about the size of the basin?
A) He declares some reports weak and relies on a single authentic narration.
B) He says the Prophet ﷺ described it differently to different people to suit their understanding, without intending exact measurement.
C) He suggests the basin changes size.
D) He argues that the reports refer to two different basins.

Key Takeaway
The varying reports about the basin's size are reconciled by understanding that they describe its immense vastness, not its exact measurement.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read descriptions of Paradise and the Basin in the Quran and Sunnah, do you sometimes dismiss them as mere metaphors, or do you truly believe they are real but beyond our full comprehension? How does your answer affect your longing for the Hereafter?
?
The Prophet ﷺ described the basin differently to different people to suit their understanding. Are you actively seeking to understand the descriptions of the unseen according to your capacity, or do you rely on vague, comfortable notions?
?
Al-Qurtubi mentions two basins, one before the Sirat and one in Paradise. Have you ever considered that your deeds may determine which basin you reach? What are you doing today to ensure you drink from the basin before the Sirat and not be denied?

The Description of the Prophet's Basin (Hawd)
Imam Maydani describes the Hawd's water and reconciles differing size estimates.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the descriptions of the Hawd's water, the significance of its size estimates, and the mention of two basins called al-Kawthar.

Core Idea
The Hawd's descriptions emphasize its supernatural vastness and purity.

Imam Maydani presents key details about the Prophet's Basin (Hawd) from the hadith tradition. He describes its water's qualities, the two spouts from Paradise, and then addresses the apparent contradictions in the narrations about its size. This lesson unpacks these descriptions and explains how scholars reconcile them.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith description
Read the passage that describes the water's whiteness and sweetness, and the two spouts from Paradise. Notice the vivid imagery.
The spouts are made of gold and silver.
2
Understand 'ghatta'
The passage explains the meaning of the word 'ghatta' as flowing water with sound. This adds sensory detail.
3
Examine size estimates
The passage mentions differing reports about the basin's size. The author reconciles them by saying the intent is to show extreme vastness, not precise measurement.
One estimate is a month's journey.
4
Learn about two basins
The supplement notes that the Prophet has two basins called al-Kawthar: one before the Sirat and one in Paradise.
This comes from al-Qurtubi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مَاءَهُ أَشَدُّ بَيَاضًا مِنَ اللَّبَنِ وَأَحْلَى مِنَ العَسَلِ يَغُتُ فِيهِ مِيزَابَانِ يَمُدَّانِهِ مِنَ الجَنَّةِ أَحَدُهُمَا مِنْ ذَهَبِ وَالآخَرُ مِنْ وَرِقٍ (۱) اهـ ؛ يقال : غت الماء - بغين معجمة فمثناة فوقية - يغْتُ -بالضم - إذا جرى جريا متتابعا له صوت وتدفق.
الثاني: قد اختلف في تقدير الحوض كما مر ويجمع بينها بأنه ليس القصد تقدير تحديد إنها القصد الإعلام بسعة الحوض جدا وأنه ليس كحياض الدنيا، وقد تكرر منه وصفه بذلك فخاطب في وصفه لكل فريق بما يعرفه من مسافة بعيدة ومنهم من قدر له المسافة بالزمان لا بالمكان فقال: «مسيرة شهر من غير قصد تحديد كما قدمناه (۲). تتمة: ذكر القرطبي في التذكرة أن النبي لو حوضين كلاهما يسمى الكوثر أحدهما قبل الصراط والثاني في الجنة (۳)، كذا في شرح المسايرة (1)
Its water is whiter than milk and sweeter than honey. Two spouts flow into it extending from Paradise, one of gold and the other of silver (1). End. It is said: ghatta al-ma'a – with a ghayn, then a tā' maftūḥa – yaghtu (with damm) – meaning it flows in a continuous stream with a sound and a gush.
Second: There is a difference of opinion regarding the estimate of the basin as mentioned, and it is reconciled that the intention is not to determine a precise measurement; rather, the intention is to inform of the extreme vastness of the basin and that it is not like the basins of this world. He repeatedly described it in such a way, so he addressed each group in its description with what it knew of a great distance. Among them are those who estimated its distance by time not by place, saying: 'A month's journey' without intending a precise determination as we have presented (2).
Supplement: al-Qurtubī mentioned in al-Tadhkira that the Prophet has two basins, each called al-Kawthar: one before the Ṣirāṭ and the second in Paradise (3); likewise in Sharḥ al-Musāyara (1).
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the description of the Prophet's basin (Hawd). It begins by quoting a hadith describing the water's qualities: whiter than milk, sweeter than honey, and fed by two spouts from Paradise, one of gold and one of silver. Then it explains the word 'ghatta' as a verb for flowing water with sound. The second part addresses the differing reports about the basin's size. These are not contradictory but intended to emphasize its immense size by using distances familiar to each audience. Some reports estimate it as a month's journey, not as a spatial measurement but to convey vastness. The supplement notes al-Qurtubi's mention that the Prophet has two basins, both called al-Kawthar: one before the Bridge (Sirat) and the other in Paradise, citing Sharh al-Musayara.

Key Terms
الحوض
الكوثر
الصراط
غت الماء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The differing size estimates of the Hawd contradict each other.
Correction: The estimates are not contradictory; they are rhetorical devices to convey its immense vastness, each tailored to the audience's understanding.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the purpose of the varying estimates of the basin's size?
A) To create confusion among the listeners
B) To show that the basin is not measurable
C) To inform of its extreme vastness in a way each group understands
D) To prioritize spatial over temporal estimates

Key Takeaway
The Hawd is a vast, pure basin provided by Allah for the Prophet's community, with descriptions emphasizing its otherworldly nature.

?

The Prophet's Great Intercession on the Day of Judgment
Imam Maydani explains the great intercession reserved for the Prophet to relieve the people on the Day of Judgment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature and purpose of the Prophet's great intercession (الشفاعة العظمى) and its connection to the Praised Station (المقام المحمود).

Core Idea
The Prophet's great intercession relieves all creation from the terror of the Day of Judgment.

In this passage, Imam Maydani explains the great intercession (الشفاعة العظمى) that Allah has reserved for the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). This intercession is for all people on the Day of Judgment to relieve them from the lengthy and distressful standing and to hasten the reckoning. The passage establishes this intercession as a unique gift to the Prophet and identifies it with the Praised Station (المقام المحمود) mentioned in the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to understand the core meaning.
2
Identify the purpose of the intercession
Look for phrases that describe what the intercession does: 'to relieve them from the standing' and 'to hasten the account'.
3
Note the hadith evidence
Find the two hadiths cited: one about every prophet having a supplication, and the other about being the first intercessor.
These hadiths are from authentic sources.
4
Understand the connection to the Praised Station
The passage explicitly links the great intercession to the Maqam Mahmud mentioned in Surah al-Isra.
5
Consider the exclusivity
Note that the passage says it is exclusive to the Prophet and not denied by anyone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالشَّفَاعَةُ الَّتِي ادَّخَرَهَا اللَّهُ هُمْ كَمَا رُوِي فِي الْأَخْبَارِ.
(و) نقول: (الشفاعة العظمى لرسول الله يوم القيامة في كافة الخلق لإراحتهم من الموقف، وهي التي ادخرها الله لهم بسؤاله ذلك من ربه كما روي) ذلك (في) صحيح (الأخبار)؛ ففي الجامع الصغير رامزاً للطبراني عن ابن مسعود : «إِنَّ لِكُلِّ نَبِيٌّ دَعْوَةً وَإِنِّي اخْتَبَاتُ دَعْوَنِ شَفَاعَةٌ لِأُمَّتِي يَوْمَ القِيَامَةِ ) .
قال ابن قاضي عجلون (۲) في شرح الشيبانية: إن مما خص الله تعالى به نبينا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم الشفاعة في الحشر ؛ كما روي في الصحيحين من طرق: «أَنَا أَوَّلُ شَافِعِ وَأَوَّلُ مُشَفّع » (۳)، وهذه الشفاعة لأهل الجمع في تعجيل الحساب والإراحة من طول الوقوف والغم، وهي الشفاعة العظمى في فصل القضاء يوم القيامة، وهي مختصة بنبينا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم ولم ينكرها أحد، وهي المقام المحمود في قوله تعالى عَسَى أَن يَبْعَثَكَ رَبُّكَ مَقَامًا محمُودًا ) (سورة الإسراء آية: ٧٩]، وهي المقام
(۱) متفق عليه أخرجه البخاري في كتاب الدعوات، باب لكل نبي دعوة مستجابة حديث رقم (٦٣٠٤) ، ومسلم في كتاب الإيمان، باب اختباء التي دعوة الشفاعة، حديث رقم (۱۹۸)، عن أبي هريرة له.
.
وما جاء في المتن من أن السيوطي أخرجه في الجامع الصغير رامزاً للطبراني عن ابن مسعود فلعله سبق نظر؛ لأن السيوطي أورد هذا الحديث وأورد قبله حديثاً غيره أخرجه الطبراني عن ابن مسعود، أما هذا الحديث فقد أخرجه السيوطي في الجامع الصغير عن أنس رامزا له بأحمد والبيهقي. انظر: الجامع الصغير وزوائده (۳۷۷/۲) (۲) محمد بن عبدالله بن عبدالرحمن الدمشقي الشافعي، أبو عبد الله نجم الدين المعروف بابن قاضي عجلون تفقه بأبيه وبالتقي بن قاضي شهبة وغيرهما وأخذ عن علماء عصره، وكان إماما علامة متقناً حجة من تصانيفه بديع المعاني في شرح عقيدة الشيباني والتاج في زوائد الروضة على المنهاج وغير ذلك، توفي بالقاهرة سنة ٨٧٦هـ.
انظر ترجمته في الضوء اللامع (٩٦/٨-٩٧)، معجم المؤلفين (۲۲۳/۱۰) . (۳) أخرجه مسلم في كتاب الفضائل، باب تفضيل نبينا على جميع الخلائق، حديث رقم (۲۲۷۸)، عن أبي هريرة .
And the intercession which Allah has reserved for them as narrated in the reports.
(And) we say: The great intercession of the Messenger of Allah on the Day of Resurrection is for all creation to relieve them from the standing, and it is that which Allah has reserved for them by his request from his Lord as narrated in authentic reports. For in al-Jami' al-Saghir, referencing al-Tabarani from Ibn Mas'ud: 'Every prophet has a supplication, and I have reserved my supplication as intercession for my Ummah on the Day of Resurrection.'
Ibn Qadi 'Ajlun (2) said in Sharh al-Shibaniyya: Indeed, among the things Allah specially gave our Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) is intercession at the Gathering; as narrated in the two Sahihs through multiple chains: 'I am the first intercessor and the first whose intercession is accepted' (3). And this intercession is for the people of the assembly to hasten the account and to relieve them from the long standing and distress. It is the great intercession in the final judgment on the Day of Resurrection, and it is exclusive to our Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) and no one has denied it. It is the praised station (Maqam Mahmud) in His statement: 'It may be that your Lord will raise you to a praised station' (Surah al-Isra, verse 79), and it is the station
(1) Agreed upon: al-Bukhari in Book of Supplications, chapter: 'Every prophet has an answered supplication' hadith no. 6304, and Muslim in Book of Faith, chapter: 'The reserved supplication of intercession' hadith no. 198, from Abu Huraira.
.
And what is mentioned in the text that al-Suyuti recorded it in al-Jami' al-Saghir referencing al-Tabarani from Ibn Mas'ud is probably a mistake; because al-Suyuti recorded this hadith and before it a different hadith from al-Tabarani from Ibn Mas'ud. As for this hadith, al-Suyuti recorded it in al-Jami' al-Saghir from Anas, referencing Ahmad and al-Bayhaqi. See: al-Jami' al-Saghir and its appendices (2/377).
(2) Muhammad ibn Abdullah ibn Abd al-Rahman al-Dimashqi al-Shafi'i, Abu Abdullah Najm al-Din known as Ibn Qadi 'Ajlun, studied with his father and with al-Taqi ibn Qadi Shahba and others, and took from scholars of his time. He was an imam, a scholar, precise, a proof. Among his works: Badi' al-Ma'ani in Sharh 'Aqidat al-Shibani and al-Taj in Zawa'id al-Rawda 'ala al-Minhaj etc. He died in Cairo in 876 AH. See his biography in al-Daw' al-Lami' (8/96-97), Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin (10/223).
(3) Narrated by Muslim in Book of Virtues, chapter: 'The excellence of our Prophet over all creation', hadith no. 2278, from Abu Huraira.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the intercession (shafa'a) of the Prophet. It begins by quoting the matn of the Tahawiyyah: 'And the intercession which Allah has reserved for them as narrated in the reports.' The commentator then explains that this refers to the great intercession for all creation to relieve them from the terror of the standing on the Day of Judgment. He supports this with a hadith from al-Jami' al-Saghir quoting Ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet reserved his supplication for intercession for his Ummah. He then cites Ibn Qadi 'Ajlun who states that intercession at the Gathering is a special gift to the Prophet, as proven by the hadith 'I am the first intercessor...' This intercession is for the people of the assembly to hasten the account and relieve their distress. It is the great intercession, exclusive to the Prophet, and no one has denied it. It is identified with the praised station (Maqam Mahmud) mentioned in the Qur'an. The passage also includes a textual note clarifying the correct chain of the hadith.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the great intercession is for specific individuals or for entering Paradise.
Correction: The passage clarifies that the great intercession is for all creation to relieve them from the standing and to hasten the account, not for specific individuals or for entering Paradise.

Checkpoint

A) To enter all believers into Paradise

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet reserved his one special supplication for his Ummah. Are you living in a way that makes you truly deserving of that intercession? What specific changes can you make today to ensure you are counted among those he intercedes for?
?
On the Day of Judgment, when the standing is long and unbearable, you will desperately long for relief. Do you regularly remember that day and prepare for it, or do you let worldly distractions make you forget? What practical step will you take this week to increase your awareness of the Hereafter?
?
The great intercession is a gift that the Prophet sought for all creation. Do you feel gratitude for this immense mercy? How can you show your thankfulness to Allah and His Messenger for this gift through your actions?

The Great Intercession of the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ
Definition of great intercession with proofs from hadith and consensus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition, proofs, and significance of the great intercession (al-shafa'ah al-uzma) of the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ on the Day of Judgment.

Core Idea
The great intercession is the Prophet's exclusive privilege to relieve all creation from the distress of the Day of Judgment.

In this lesson, we explore one of the most profound honors granted to the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ: the great intercession. This is not the intercession for sinners, but a unique role to bring relief to all of humanity during the most intense moment of the Hereafter. The passage from the Tahawiyyah commentary establishes this doctrine with clear textual evidence and scholarly consensus.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text carefully, noting the key terms like الشفاعة العظمى and المقام المحمود.
Pay attention to the structure: definition, then evidence, then connection to the Quran.
2
Understand the definition
Notice how the author defines the great intercession as specifically for relieving the standing on the Day of Judgment, not for removing sinners from Hell.
This intercession is for all of creation, not just Muslims.
3
Examine the proofs
Identify the hadith evidence cited, including the hadith from Ibn Mas'ud and the mutawatir hadith 'I am the first intercessor'.
These proofs are from authentic sources like al-Tabarani and the two Sahihs.
4
Connect to al-Maqam al-Mahmud
See how the commentary links this intercession to the Praiseworthy Station mentioned in Surah al-Isra, and the wisdom in asking for it after the adhan.
This station is unique to the Prophet and will be praised by all creation.
5
Reflect on the consensus
The passage concludes that this belief is obligatory due to tawatur and ijma'. Consider why this matters for your faith.
The consensus of scholars confirms this as a core Sunni belief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالشَّفَاعَةُ الَّتِي ادَّخَرَهَا اللَّهُ هُمْ كَمَا رُوِي فِي الْأَخْبَارِ. (و) نقول: (الشفاعة العظمى لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يوم القيامة في كافة الخلق لإراحتهم من الموقف، وهي التي ادخرها الله لهم بسؤاله ذلك من ربه كما روي ذلك في صحيح الأخبار؛ ففي الجامع الصغير رامزاً للطبراني عن ابن مسعود : «إِنَّ لِكُلِّ نَبِيٍّ دَعْوَةً وَإِنِّي اخْتَبَأْتُ دَعْوَتِي شَفَاعَةً لِأُمَّتِي يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ». قال ابن قاضي عجلون في شرح الشيبانية: إن مما خص الله تعالى به نبينا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم الشفاعة في الحشر؛ كما روي في الصحيحين من طرق: «أَنَا أَوَّلُ شَافِعٍ وَأَوَّلُ مُشَفَّعٍ»، وهذه الشفاعة لأهل الجمع في تعجيل الحساب والإراحة من طول الوقوف والغم، وهي الشفاعة العظمى في فصل القضاء يوم القيامة، وهي مختصة بنبينا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم ولم ينكرها أحد، وهي المقام المحمود في قوله تعالى: {عَسَى أَن يَبْعَثَكَ رَبُّكَ مَقَامًا مَّحْمُودًا} [الإسراء: 79]، وهي المقام الذي يحمده فيه الأولون والآخرون، وقد ورد في الحديث الصحيح الأمر بأن ندعو بذلك عقيب الأذان، والحكمة في سؤال ذلك مع كونه واجب الوقوع بوعد الله تعالى إظهار شرفه وعظيم منزلته. وفي شرح الجزائرية للسنوسي رحمه الله: «لا شك أن مما يجب الإيمان به لتواتره ووقوع الإجماع عليه ثبوت الشفاعة لسيدنا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم في إراحة الناس من الموقف، واختصاصها به أمر مستفيض مشهور في الصحاح.
And the intercession which Allah has stored for them as has been narrated in the reports. And we say: The great intercession for the Messenger of Allah ﷺ on the Day of Judgment concerning all of creation to give them relief from the standing; it is that which Allah stored for them by his asking that from his Lord as has been narrated in authentic reports. For in al-Jami' al-Saghir, indicating al-Tabarani, from Ibn Mas'ud: 'Indeed, every prophet has a supplication, and I have reserved my supplication as intercession for my nation on the Day of Judgment.' Ibn Qadi 'Ajlun said in his commentary on al-Shaybaniyya: Indeed, from what Allah ﷻ has specially honored our Prophet Muhammad ﷺ with is intercession on the Day of Gathering, as narrated in the two Sahihs through multiple chains: 'I am the first intercessor and the first whose intercession is accepted.' And this intercession is for the people of the assembly to hasten the reckoning and give relief from the length of standing and distress. It is the great intercession in the decisive judgment on the Day of Judgment, and it is exclusive to our Prophet Muhammad ﷺ; no one has denied it. It is the Praiseworthy Station (al-Maqam al-Mahmud) in His ﷻ saying: 'It may be that your Lord will raise you to a Praiseworthy Station' [al-Isra' 17:79]. It is the station in which the first and the last will praise him. And it has been reported in the authentic hadith the command to supplicate for that immediately after the call to prayer. The wisdom in asking for that, despite its being necessarily occurring by Allah's promise, is to manifest his honor and the greatness of his rank. And in the commentary on al-Jaza'iriyya by al-Sanusi, may Allah have mercy on him: 'There is no doubt that from what must be believed due to its tawatur and the occurrence of consensus upon it is the establishment of intercession for our master Muhammad ﷺ in giving people relief from the standing, and its exclusivity to him is a widespread and famous matter in the authentic books.'
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage defines and establishes the doctrine of the great intercession (al-shafa'ah al-uzma) of the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ on the Day of Judgment. It begins by referencing the original text of the Tahawiyyah, which states that Allah has reserved an intercession as reported in the traditions. The commentary then explains that this is the great intercession granted to the Prophet for all of creation to relieve them from the lengthy and distressful standing on the Day of Judgment. It is called 'great' because it encompasses all people, and it is the one for which the Prophet asked his Lord. Evidence is provided from the hadith narrated by Ibn Mas'ud in which the Prophet says he reserved his special supplication to be intercession for his nation. Ibn Qadi 'Ajlun's explanation adds that this intercession is an exclusive honor for the Prophet, supported by the mutawatir hadith from al-Bukhari and Muslim: 'I am the first intercessor and the first whose intercession is accepted.' This intercession is specifically for the people of the assembly to hasten the accounting and relieve them from the agony of waiting. The passage identifies this great intercession with the Praiseworthy Station (al-Maqam al-Mahmud) mentioned in the Quran [17:79], where all creatures—first and last—will praise the Prophet. It notes the wisdom in commanding Muslims to pray for this station after the adhan despite it being guaranteed to occur, which is to manifest the Prophet's exalted rank. Finally, al-Sanusi's commentary confirms that belief in this intercession is obligatory due to its massive transmission (tawatur) and scholarly consensus (ijma'), and that its exclusivity to the Prophet is well-established in the authentic hadith collections.

C) To intercede for the Prophet's family and companions.

Key Takeaway
The great intercession is a unique honor for the Prophet Muhammad ﷺ, proven by authentic hadith and consensus, to relieve all creation from the distress of the Day of Judgment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just learned that the Prophet ﷺ reserved his supplication for the intercession of his nation, and that this intercession is guaranteed by Allah's promise. Yet, the Prophet commanded us to ask for al-Maqam al-Mahmud after the adhan to manifest his rank. Do you regularly say this du'a? If not, what does your neglect say about your gratitude for his sacrifice and your longing for his intercession? Make a firm intention tonight to begin this practice, and reflect: what is holding you back from asking for something that will benefit you and honor him?
?
The great intercession is not about removing sinners from Hell—it is for relieving all creation from the immense distress of the standing. You will be among that creation. How does the reality of that terrifying stand change the way you view your current distractions and sins? What are you doing today to prepare for that moment when you will look for the Prophet’s intercession? Write down one concrete action you will take this week to increase your love and following of him, so that when that day comes, you may be among those he intercedes for.
?
The lesson states that asking for the intercession after the adhan is to manifest the Prophet’s honor, even though it is already promised. How often do you make this du'a with real presence of heart, recognizing his exalted rank? If you rarely do, then ask yourself: Do you truly believe in his great station? What would it take for you to feel the urgency and gratitude that should accompany this supplication? Commit to saying it with attention every time you hear the adhan for the next week, and notice the change in your connection to him.

The Obligation to Believe in the Prophet's Intercession
Al-Maydani explains the wisdom of asking for wasilah and affirms the certainty of intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why belief in the Prophet's intercession is obligatory based on tawatur and ijma', and the wisdom behind asking for al-wasilah after the adhan.

Core Idea
The Prophet's intercession is established by mass transmission and consensus, making it a required belief.

Before describing the types of intercession, Imam al-Maydani establishes the certainty of intercession itself. He cites al-Sanusi to affirm that it is an obligation to believe in the Prophet's intercession, due to its mass transmission (tawatur) and the consensus (ijma') of the scholars. He also explains the wisdom of asking for al-wasilah in the supplication after the adhan, which highlights the Prophet's honor.

Guided Path
1
Read the wisdom of asking for wasilah
Read the first sentence about the wisdom of asking for al-wasilah after the adhan. Reflect on why we ask for something already guaranteed by Allah.
The wisdom is to manifest the Prophet's honor.
2
Understand the certainty of intercession
Read al-Sanusi's statement that belief in intercession is obligatory due to tawatur and ijma'. Note that it is for relief from the standing (al-mawqif) and is specific to the Prophet.
This is a well-known matter in the authentic collections.
3
Distinguish types of evidence
Recognize that the author uses tawatur and ijma' as the basis for obligatory belief. These are the strongest forms of evidence in Islamic theology.
Tawatur means it has been reported by so many that it is impossible to be false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الذي يحمده فيه الأولون والآخرون، وقد ورد في الحديث الصحيح الأمر بأن ندعو بذلك عقيب الأذان، والحكمة في سؤال ذلك مع كونه واجب الوقوع بوعد الله تعالى إظهار شرفه وعظيم منزلته. وفي شرح الجزائرية للسنوسي رحمه الله: «لا شك أن مما يجب الإيمان به لتواتره ووقوع الإجماع عليه ثبوت الشفاعة لسيدنا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم في إراحة الناس من الموقف، واختصاصها به أمر مستفيض مشهور في الصحاح.» وفي شرح الجوهرة للمصنف: وله شفاعات؛ ذكر القاضي والنووي منها خمسا: أحدها - وهي أعظمها وأعمها شفاعته عليه الصلاة والسلام بعد أن يكلم الناس الأنبياء حين يعاينون من شدائد الموقف وأهواله وطول القيام فيه لرب العالمين وزيادة القلق وتصاعد العرق ما يذيب الأكباد وينسي الأولاد مدة ثلاثة آلاف سنة؛ فيترادُّونها من آدم إلى عيسى في خمسة آلاف سنة أيضًا؛ إذ بين سؤال كل نبي وآخر ألف سنة - كما قال ابن حجر والقرطبي وغيرهما - فإذا انتهوا إليه صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «أَنَا هَا أَنَا لَهَا أُمَّتِي أُمني، وكل من قبله لا يقول إلا: نفسي، نفسي اذهبوا إلى غيري»، وهذه مختصة به وتسمى الشفاعة العظمى، وهذه مجمع عليها لم ينكرها أحد ممن يقول بالحشر؛ إذ هي للإراحة من طول الوقوف حين يتمنون الانصراف من موقفهم ولو إلى النار. وثانيها: في إدخال قوم الجنة بغير حساب، وهذه أيضًا خاصة به على ما قاله.
Whom the first and last praise, and it has been reported in the authentic hadith the command that we supplicate with that after the call to prayer, and the wisdom in asking for that, despite it being necessarily occurring by the promise of Allah the Exalted, is to manifest his honor and great rank. And in the commentary of al-Jaza'iriyya by al-Sanusi (may Allah have mercy on him): 'There is no doubt that among what must be believed, due to its tawatur (mass transmission) and the occurrence of consensus upon it, is the establishment of the intercession of our master Muhammad (peace and blessings upon him) for giving relief to the people from the standing, and its being specific to him is a widespread, well-known matter in the authentic collections.' And in the commentary of al-Jawhara by the author: And he has intercessions; al-Qadi and al-Nawawi mentioned among them five: The first – and it is the greatest and most general of them – is his intercession (peace and prayer upon him) after the people speak to the prophets when they witness from the hardships of the standing and its terrors and the length of standing therein for the Lord of the worlds and the increase of anxiety and the rising of sweat what melts livers and makes children forget for a period of three thousand years; so they pass it on from Adam to Jesus over five thousand years as well; for between the request of each prophet and the next is a thousand years – as Ibn Hajar and al-Qurtubi and others said – and when they end with him (peace and prayer upon him) he says: 'I am here, I am for it, my community, my community' ('أُمَّتِي أُمني'), and everyone before him says only 'myself, myself, go to other than me.' And this is specific to him and is called the Great Intercession, and this is agreed upon, no one who affirms the resurrection denies it; for it is for relief from the length of the standing when they wish to depart from their standing even to the Fire. And the second: is for entering a people into Paradise without reckoning, and this also is specific to him, according to what he said.
Source pages p. 94

Commentary
This passage is a continuous explanation about the intercession (shafa'ah) of the Prophet Muhammad (SAW). It begins by citing the wisdom behind asking for al-wasilah in the du'a after the adhan, even though it is guaranteed by Allah's promise, namely to manifest the Prophet's honor and rank. Then it quotes al-Sanusi's statement from his commentary on al-Jaza'iriyya that belief in the intercession is obligatory due to its tawatur (mass transmission) and ijma' (consensus), and that it is well-known in the authentic hadith collections. The intercession is specifically for relieving the people from the terrors of the standing (al-mawqif). The author then transitions to his own Sharh al-Jawhara, where he enumerates five types of shafa'ah as reported by Qadi Iyad and al-Nawawi. The first and greatest type is the Prophet's intercession when the people, after experiencing extreme hardships during the standing of three thousand years, approach the prophets one by one from Adam to Jesus, each declining, until they come to Muhammad (SAW) who says 'I am for it, my community' while others say 'myself, myself.' This intercession is called the Great Intercession (al-shafa'ah al-'uzma) and is agreed upon by all who affirm the resurrection; its purpose is relief from the lengthy standing. The second type is intercession for admitting a group of people into Paradise without reckoning, and this is also specific to him, though the author does not elaborate further in this passage.

Key Terms

تواتر
إجماع
موقف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think intercession is not established or is not obligatory to believe in.
Correction: The passage affirms that intercession is established by tawatur and ijma', making it obligatory to believe.

Checkpoint
According to al-Sanusi, what is the basis for the obligatory belief in the Prophet's intercession?
A) A single hadith
B) Reason and logic
C) Tawatur and ijma'
D) The opinion of a single scholar

Key Takeaway
Belief in the Prophet's intercession is obligatory because it is established by mass transmission (tawatur) and consensus (ijma').

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The Prophet's intercession is for relief from the terrors of the standing. Have you ever reflected on the reality of that standing and your own need for intercession? What steps will you take today to prepare for that moment?
?
Asking for al-wasilah after the adhan manifests the Prophet's honor, yet how often do you rush through the adhan without pondering this du'a? Will you commit to saying it with presence of heart from today?

The Great Intercession and Intercession for Entering Paradise without Reckoning
Al-Maydani describes the first two types of the Prophet's intercession.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first and greatest type of intercession (the Great Intercession) and the second type of intercession specific to the Prophet.

Core Idea
The Prophet's Great Intercession relieves the nations from the terrors of the standing, and his second intercession admits some into Paradise without reckoning.

After establishing the certainty of intercession, Imam al-Maydani details its types. Drawing from al-Qadi and al-Nawawi, he enumerates five types, focusing here on the first two. The first and greatest is the intercession for relief from the long and terrifying standing on the Day of Resurrection. The second is for admitting a people into Paradise without any prior reckoning. Both are exclusive to the Prophet Muhammad (SAW).

Guided Path
1
Read the narrative of the Great Intercession
Read the detailed description of how the people approach the prophets one by one, from Adam to Jesus, each declining, until they come to Muhammad (SAW) who accepts.
Notice the emphasis on the extreme hardships of the standing lasting thousands of years.
2
Identify the first type
The Great Intercession is for relief from the standing. The text says it is agreed upon by all who affirm the resurrection.
This intercession is the most general and greatest.
3
Identify the second type
The second intercession is for entering a group of people into Paradise without any prior reckoning. The text notes it is also specific to the Prophet.

الذي يحمده فيه الأولون والآخرون، وقد ورد في الحديث الصحيح الأمر بأن ندعو بذلك عقيب الأذان، والحكمة في سؤال ذلك مع كونه واجب الوقوع بوعد الله تعالى إظهار شرفه وعظيم منزلته. وفي شرح الجزائرية للسنوسي رحمه الله: «لا شك أن مما يجب الإيمان به لتواتره ووقوع الإجماع عليه ثبوت الشفاعة لسيدنا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم في إراحة الناس من الموقف، واختصاصها به أمر مستفيض مشهور في الصحاح.» وفي شرح الجوهرة للمصنف: وله شفاعات؛ ذكر القاضي والنووي منها خمسا: أحدها - وهي أعظمها وأعمها شفاعته عليه الصلاة والسلام بعد أن يكلم الناس الأنبياء حين يعاينون من شدائد الموقف وأهواله وطول القيام فيه لرب العالمين وزيادة القلق وتصاعد العرق ما يذيب الأكباد وينسي الأولاد مدة ثلاثة آلاف سنة؛ فيترادُّونها من آدم إلى عيسى في خمسة آلاف سنة أيضًا؛ إذ بين سؤال كل نبي وآخر ألف سنة - كما قال ابن حجر والقرطبي وغيرهما - فإذا انتهوا إليه صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «أَنَا هَا أَنَا لَهَا أُمَّتِي أُمني، وكل من قبله لا يقول إلا: نفسي، نفسي اذهبوا إلى غيري»، وهذه مختصة به وتسمى الشفاعة العظمى، وهذه مجمع عليها لم ينكرها أحد ممن يقول بالحشر؛ إذ هي للإراحة من طول الوقوف حين يتمنون الانصراف من موقفهم ولو إلى النار. وثانيها: في إدخال قوم الجنة بغير حساب، وهذه أيضًا خاصة به على ما قاله.
Whom the first and last praise, and it has been reported in the authentic hadith the command that we supplicate with that after the call to prayer, and the wisdom in asking for that, despite it being necessarily occurring by the promise of Allah the Exalted, is to manifest his honor and great rank. And in the commentary of al-Jaza'iriyya by al-Sanusi (may Allah have mercy on him): 'There is no doubt that among what must be believed, due to its tawatur (mass transmission) and the occurrence of consensus upon it, is the establishment of the intercession of our master Muhammad (peace and blessings upon him) for giving relief to the people from the standing, and its being specific to him is a widespread, well-known matter in the authentic collections.' And in the commentary of al-Jawhara by the author: And he has intercessions; al-Qadi and al-Nawawi mentioned among them five: The first – and it is the greatest and most general of them – is his intercession (peace and prayer upon him) after the people speak to the prophets when they witness from the hardships of the standing and its terrors and the length of standing therein for the Lord of the worlds and the increase of anxiety and the rising of sweat what melts livers and makes children forget for a period of three thousand years; so they pass it on from Adam to Jesus over five thousand years as well; for between the request of each prophet and the next is a thousand years – as Ibn Hajar and al-Qurtubi and others said – and when they end with him (peace and prayer upon him) he says: 'I am here, I am for it, my community, my community' ('أُمَّتِي أُمني'), and everyone before him says only 'myself, myself, go to other than me.' And this is specific to him and is called the Great Intercession, and this is agreed upon, no one who affirms the resurrection denies it; for it is for relief from the length of the standing when they wish to depart from their standing even to the Fire. And the second: is for entering a people into Paradise without reckoning, and this also is specific to him, according to what he said.

Commentary
This passage is a continuous explanation about the intercession (shafa'ah) of the Prophet Muhammad (SAW). It begins by citing the wisdom behind asking for al-wasilah in the du'a after the adhan, even though it is guaranteed by Allah's promise, namely to manifest the Prophet's honor and rank. Then it quotes al-Sanusi's statement from his commentary on al-Jaza'iriyya that belief in the intercession is obligatory due to its tawatur (mass transmission) and ijma' (consensus), and that it is well-known in the authentic hadith collections. The intercession is specifically for relieving the people from the terrors of the standing (al-mawqif). The author then transitions to his own Sharh al-Jawhara, where he enumerates five types of shafa'ah as reported by Qadi Iyad and al-Nawawi. This intercession is called the Great Intercession (al-shafa'ah al-'uzma) and is agreed upon by all who affirm the resurrection; its purpose is relief from the lengthy standing. The second type is intercession for admitting a group of people into Paradise without reckoning, and this is also specific to him, though the author does not elaborate further in this passage.
