And Allah's favor upon you is great. And if He wills, He punishes them in the Fire prepared for purifying sins according to their crimes and their injustice to themselves, and that is by His justice and wisdom. Then He brings them out of it by His mercy which encompasses everything of His creation, and by the intercession of the intercessors from among His obedient people, like His prophets, messengers, angels, and those who know Him; and that is by His permission and will. For there are many hadiths with mutawatir meaning: among them is the hadith of Abu Sa'id in the two Sahihs that some people said, 'O Messenger of Allah, will we see our Lord on the Day of Resurrection?...' the complete hadith, and in it: 'Allah the Exalted says: The angels interceded, the prophets interceded, and the believers interceded, and nothing remains except the Most Merciful of the merciful.' And among them is the hadith of al-Tirmidhi, Ibn Majah, Ibn Hibban, and others: 'Indeed, more than the tribe of Ghameem will enter Paradise through the intercession of a man from my Ummah.' Then He resurrects them to His Garden, the abode of His honor; and that is because Allah is the Protector, i.e. Helper, of the people of His knowledge in this world and the Hereafter, and He does not make them in both abodes like the people of His denial, the deniers of His oneness and power, who failed to be guided to His knowledge and did not attain from His guardianship what would guide them to His oneness and worship. O Allah, O Protector of Islam and its people, make us firm in Islam until we meet You with it, pleased with us on the Day of Gathering and its terror; for You are the Guide to it and the Bestower of it.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal statement about the fate of sinful believers. It begins by affirming that if Allah wills, He punishes them in Hellfire according to their sins, by His justice and wisdom. Then, through His immense mercy and the intercession (shafa'ah) of prophets, messengers, angels, and the righteous, He brings them out. This is supported by mutawatir hadiths, such as the famous hadith of Abu Sa'id where Allah says that after all intercessors, the Most Merciful remains. Another hadith promises that many will enter Paradise through the intercession of a single man from the Ummah. After purification, Allah resurrects them to Paradise, distinguishing them from the deniers who rejected His oneness and power. The passage concludes with a supplication asking Allah to keep the author and readers firm in Islam and to be pleased with them on the Day of Gathering, affirming that Allah is the Guide and Bestower of Islam.

Key Terms
شفاعة (intercession)
رحمة (mercy)
عدل (justice)
عذاب (punishment)
جنة (Paradise)
نار (Hell)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Intercession contradicts divine justice by letting sinners off without punishment.
Correction: Intercession occurs only after just punishment has been carried out. It does not override justice but complements it with mercy.

Checkpoint
What role does intercession play according to this passage?
A) It replaces punishment entirely.
B) It occurs after punishment by justice, bringing believers out of Hell.
C) It only applies to prophets.
D) It is automatic without need for permission.

Key Takeaway
Sinful believers who enter Hell are purified by justice and then saved by mercy and intercession, never remaining eternally.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you silently assume Allah's mercy will save you without facing the purifying fire of His justice? How does this passage force you to reconcile hope in mercy with fear of justice? Will you change anything today because of this?
?
If intercession only comes after punishment, are you actively seeking repentance and purification now, or are you passively relying on the Prophet's ﷺ intercession later? What specific sin will you repent from right now?
?
The passage ends with a supplication to be kept firm in Islam until meeting Allah. Do you truly desire to meet Allah with Islam, even knowing it requires accountability? What is one habit you will abandon starting today to prepare for that meeting?

The Duty of Obedience to Rulers Even When Unjust
Tahawi states the duty to obey rulers and avoid rebellion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the obligation to obey Muslim rulers, even if they are unjust, as long as they do not command sin, and the prohibition of rebellion and division.

Core Idea
Obedience to rulers is part of obedience to Allah, except in sin.

Imam Tahawi presents the classical Sunni view on political authority: Muslims must obey their rulers, supplicate for them, and avoid rebellion, even if the rulers are unjust. This lesson explains the boundaries of this obligation and the importance of unity, as derived from the Quran and Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then the English translation. Note the strong language of obligation and prohibition.
2
Identify the core obligations

3
Reflect on the wisdom

This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text

في الإمامة ولا نرى السيف على أحد من أمة محمد إلا من وجب عليه السيف. ولا نرى الخروج على أئمتنا وولاة أمورنا وإن جاروا، ولا ندعو على أحد منهم، ولا ننزع يدا من طاعتهم، ونرى طاعتهم من طاعة الله عز وجل فريضة ما لم يأمروا بمعصية، وندعوهم بالصلاح والنجاح والمعافاة. ونتبع السنة والجماعة ونجتنب الشذوذ والخلاف والفرقة، ونحب أهل العدل والأمانة ونبغض أهل الجور والخيانة. ولا نرى السيف أي سفك الدم واجبا على أحد من أمة نبينا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم إلا على من وجب عليه السيف أي سفك الدم بالنص القاطع؛ كالقاتل والزاني المحصن والمرتد ففي البخاري ومسلم عن ابن مسعود عن النبي : لا يَحِلُّ دَمُ امْرِئٍ مُسْلِمٍ إِلَّا بِإِحْدَى ثَلَاثَ الثَّيِّبُ الزَّانِي وَالنَّفْسُ بِالنَّفْسِ وَالتَّارِكُ لِدِينِهِ الْمُفَارِقُ لِلْجَمَاعَةِ.

The Three Capital Offenses in Islam
Tahawi explains the hadith specifying three capital offenses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will know the three specific crimes for which a Muslim's blood can lawfully be shed according to the hadith cited by Imam Tahawi.

Core Idea
A Muslim's blood is sacred except by three: murder, adultery after marriage, and apostasy.

Imam Tahawi clarifies the earlier statement about using the sword by citing a well-known hadith from the Prophet (ﷺ) that specifies the only three grounds on which a Muslim may be executed. This lesson examines those grounds and the importance of definitive textual evidence (nass qati').

Creed on Obedience to Rulers and Avoiding Rebellion
Tahawiyyah states the creed on capital punishment and obedience to rulers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni creed regarding capital punishment and obedience to rulers, including the limits of obedience.

Core Idea
Obedience to rulers is obligatory unless they command sin, and rebellion is forbidden.

This passage from the Tahawiyyah Creed outlines key principles of Sunni political theology. It addresses two sensitive issues: capital punishment and obedience to rulers. The creed takes a moderate stance—neither allowing arbitrary violence nor endorsing rebellion, even against unjust rulers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the three main sections: capital punishment, obedience to rulers, and following the community.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Understand the condition on obedience
The passage says obedience is obligatory 'as long as they do not command disobedience.' Reflect on what this condition implies for situations where rulers command sin.
This is the key balance in Sunni political thought.
3
Connect to broader Sunni principles
Notice how the passage links obedience to rulers with following the Sunnah and community, and with loving the just and hating the unjust. Think about how these principles work together.
The creed promotes unity and discourages division.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا نَرَى السَّيْفَ عَلَى أَحَدٍ مِنْ أُمَّةِ مُحَمَّدٍ إِلَّا مَنْ وَجَبَ عَلَيْهِ السَّيْفُ. وَلَا نَرَى الْخُرُوجَ عَلَى أَئِمَّتِنَا وَوُلَاةِ أُمُورِنَا وَإِنْ جَارُوا، وَلَا نَدْعُو عَلَى أَحَدٍ مِنْهُمْ، وَلَا تَنْزِعُ يَدًا مِنْ طَاعَتِهِمْ، وَنَرَى طَاعَتَهُمْ مِنْ طَاعَةِ اللهِ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ فَرِيضَةً مَا لَمْ يَأْمُرُوا بِمَعْصِيَةٍ، وَنَدْعُوهُمْ بِالصَّلَاحِ وَالنَّجَاحِ وَالْمُعَافَاةِ. وَنَتَّبِعُ السُّنَّةَ وَالجَمَاعَةَ وَنَجْتَنِبُ الشُّذُونَ وَالخِلَافَ وَالفُرْقَةَ، وَنُحِبُّ أَهْلَ العَدْلِ وَالأَمَانَةِ وَنَبْغَضُ أَهْلَ الجَوْرِ وَالخِيَانَةِ.
And we do not see the sword [to be used] against anyone from the community of Muhammad except one upon whom the sword is obligatory. And we do not see rebellion against our imams and those in authority over us, even if they are unjust, nor do we supplicate against any of them, nor do we withdraw a hand from obedience to them; and we see obedience to them as part of obedience to Allah, the Mighty and Majestic, an obligation as long as they do not command disobedience; and we supplicate for their well-being, success, and safety. And we follow the Sunnah and the community, and we avoid aberrations, dissent, and division; and we love the people of justice and trustworthiness, and we detest the people of injustice and treachery.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage from the Tahawiyyah creed sets forth the Sunni position on capital punishment and political authority.  1. The first sentence restricts the use of capital punishment ("the sword") to those who legally deserve it, implying that killing is not permissible arbitrarily. 2. The second sentence establishes the duty of obedience to rulers and forbids rebellion even if the rulers are unjust, but adds a condition: obedience is obligatory as long as they do not command sin. 3. It also prohibits supplication against them or withdrawing obedience. 4. The next part commands following the Sunnah and community, avoiding schisms, and loving those who are just and trustworthy while hating those who are unjust and treacherous. The tone is moderate: it neither endorses rebellion nor unconditional acceptance of tyranny.

Key Terms
السيف
الخروج على الأئمة
الجماعة
أهل العدل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe the creed permits rebellion against unjust rulers.
Correction: The creed explicitly forbids rebellion, stating that obedience is required even if rulers are unjust, as long as they do not command disobedience to Allah.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the ruling on obedience to rulers?
A) Obedience is always obligatory
B) Obedience is obligatory unless they command disobedience to Allah
C) Obedience is never obligatory if they are unjust
D) Obedience is optional

Key Takeaway
The Sunni position on rulers is to obey them unless they command sin, and to avoid rebellion while praying for their righteousness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Do you find that detesting injustice leads you to harbor hatred in your heart that conflicts with the command to pray for rulers? The Three Capital Offenses in Islamic Law
Commentator explains the hadith limiting capital punishment to three cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three specific offenses for which Islamic law permits capital punishment, as derived from the hadith and the commentary of Imam Tahawi.

Core Idea
Capital punishment in Islam is strictly limited to three specific crimes.

In this passage, the commentator clarifies a crucial principle: the sword (capital punishment) is not to be applied arbitrarily to any Muslim. Rather, it is strictly confined to three offenses for which definitive textual evidence exists. This lesson examines each offense and the prophetic hadith that establishes them.

Guided Path
1
Understand the opening statement
Read the commentary's explanation of 'sword' and what it means for bloodshed to be obligatory only by definitive text.
The commentator equates 'sword' with 'shedding blood' (safk al-dam).
2
Identify the three capital offenses
The passage lists three examples: the murderer, the married adulterer, and the apostate. Note that these correspond to the hadith's categories.
3
Study the cited hadith
Read the hadith from Ibn Mas'ud in Bukhari and Muslim, which explicitly states the three lawful grounds for taking a Muslim's life.
The hadith uses slightly different phrasing: 'the married adulterer, life for life, and the one who abandons his religion.'
4
Reflect on the principle
Consider why the Imam emphasizes that the sword is not to be used except in these cases. This shows the sanctity of human life in Islam.
This principle protects Muslims from arbitrary execution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا نرى السيف) أي سفك الدم واجبًا (على أحد من أمة ) نبينا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم إلا) على (من وجب عليه السيف) أي سفك الدم بالنص القاطع؛ كالقاتل والزاني المحصن والمرتد ففي البخاري ومسلم عن ابن مسعود عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: لا يَحِلُّ دَمُ امْرِئٍ مُسْلِمٍ إِلَّا بِإِحْدَى ثَلَاثَ: الشَّيْبُ الزَّانِ وَالنَّفْسُ بِالنَّفْسِ وَالنَّارِكُ لِدِينِهِ المَفَارِقُ لِلجَمَاعَةِ.
And we do not see the sword: i.e., bloodshed is not obligatory on anyone from the community of our Prophet Muhammad, peace and blessings be upon him, except on one upon whom the sword is obligatory, i.e., bloodshed by definitive text; such as the killer, the married adulterer, and the apostate. For in al-Bukhari and Muslim, from Ibn Mas'ud, from the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him: The blood of a Muslim is not lawful except by one of three: the married adulterer, life for life, and the one who abandons his religion, separating from the community.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory gloss on the first phrase of the Tahawiyyah text: "ولا نرى السيف على أحد من أمة محمد إلا من وجب عليه السيف." The commentator clarifies that "sword" means shedding blood, and it is not obligatory (i.e., permissible only) on any Muslim except those for whom definitive textual evidence makes bloodshed mandatory. He gives three examples: the murderer (liable for qisas), the married adulterer (muhsan, liable for stoning), and the apostate (who leaves Islam and separates from the community). He then cites the well-known hadith from Ibn Mas'ud recorded in Bukhari and Muslim, which lists exactly these three categories as the only lawful grounds for taking a Muslim's life. The narration is slightly paraphrased: "the married adulterer, life for life, and the one who abandons his religion, separating from the congregation." The passage thus restricts capital punishment to these offenses.

Key Terms
سيف
سفك الدم
قاتل
زاني محصن
مرتد
النص القاطع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that capital punishment can be applied for any major sin in Islam.
Correction: The hadith explicitly limits lawful execution to only three specific offenses: murder, married adultery, and apostasy.

Checkpoint
What are the three categories for which a Muslim's blood is lawful according to the hadith cited?
A) Adultery, theft, and drinking alcohol
B) Murder, apostasy, and adultery after muhsan
C) Rebellion, apostasy, and murder
D) Slander, theft, and murder

Key Takeaway
Islamic law permits capital punishment only in three specific cases: murder, married adultery, and apostasy, as established by prophetic hadith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear about crimes like murder, adultery, or apostasy, do you find yourself thinking that the perpetrators 'deserve' death? How does this hadith's limitation of capital punishment to only these three cases challenge any desire for vengeance outside the law?
?
Reflect on the statement 'the blood of a Muslim is not lawful except by one of three.' Have you ever wished harm or death upon someone for a lesser sin? What does that reveal about your understanding of the sanctity of a Muslim's life?
?
If you were part of a community that had to implement this law, would you trust the legal system to administer justice only in these three cases, or would you be tempted to take matters into your own hands? How can you cultivate a deep reliance on Islamic legal procedures and avoid vigilantism?

Evidence for Forbidding Rebellion Against Unjust Rulers
Commentator cites evidence from hadith and Salaf practice for not rebelling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the evidence from hadith and the reasoning of the Salaf for forbidding rebellion against unjust rulers, and why patience is required.

Core Idea
Rebellion against unjust rulers leads to chaos; patience is commanded.

The commentator explains the Tahawiyyah phrase forbidding rebellion by citing the practice of the Salaf and several hadiths that emphasize obedience and patience even when rulers are unjust. This passage provides the textual and rational basis for this important creedal position.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal English translation to understand the basic meaning.
Notice the structure: a rational reason followed by three hadith citations.
2
Understand the rational argument
The commentator argues that infallibility is not a condition for imamate at the outset, so if a ruler becomes unjust, his imamate does not automatically dissolve. Therefore, rebellion is not justified.
This is a critical point: the initial validity of the imam's authority does not depend on sinlessness.
3
Examine each hadith
Three hadiths are cited: (1) from Abu Dawud about detested tax collectors, (2) from Bukhari and Muslim about patience, (3) from Muslim about hating sin but not rebelling. Note the specific lessons each gives.
The hadiths reinforce the obligation of obedience and patience even under unjust rulers.
4
Reflect on the lesson's implication
Consider how this teaching applies today. The commentator emphasizes that rebellion leads to greater harm, as warned in the hadith about dying a death of ignorance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد أشار المصنف إلى بعض أحكامه بقوله : ( ولا نرى الخروج على أئمتنا و) لا (ولاة أمورنا وإن جاروا بالظلم علينا؛ لأنه قد ظهر الفسق وانتشر الجور من الأئمة والأمراء بعد الخلفاء الراشدين والسلف كانوا ينقادون لهم ويقيمون الجمع والأعياد بإذنهم ولا يرون الخروج عليهم، ولأن العصمة ليست بشرط الإمامة ابتداء؛ فبقاء أولى. كذا في شرح العقائد (۳). وفي سنن أبي داود مرفوعا: «سَيَأْتِيكُم رُكَيَبٌ مَبْخُوضُونَ يَطلُبُونَ مِنْكُم مَا لَمْ يَجِبْ عَلَيكُم فَإِذَا سَأَلُوكُم ذَلِكَ فَأَعْطُوهُم وَلَا تَسبُوهُم وَلَتُونُوا لهم (۳)، وفي الصحيحين: مَنْ كَرِهَ مِنْ أَمِيرِهِ شَيْئًا فَلْيَصْبِرْ فَإِنَّهُ مَنْ خَرَجَ مِنَ السُّلْطَانِ شِيرًا مَاتَ مِينَةَ جاهله ()، وفي مسلم: «مَنْ ولي عَلَيْهِ وَالٍ فَرَاهُ يَأْتِي شَيْئًا مِنْ مَعْصِيَةِ اللَّهِ فَلْيَكْرَهُ مَا يَأْتِيهِ
And the author referred to some of its rulings by his saying: (And we do not see rebellion against our imams and) not (the rulers of our affairs, even if they are unjust with oppression upon us); because corruption appeared and injustice spread among the imams and rulers after the Rightly Guided Caliphs, and the Salaf (early Muslims) used to submit to them and hold Friday and Eid prayers with their permission and did not see rebellion against them; and because infallibility is not a condition for imamate initially; so continuity is more appropriate. This is in Sharh al-'Aqa'id. And in Sunan Abi Dawud as a marfu' hadith: 'There will come to you mounted [collectors] whom you detest, asking from you what is not obligatory upon you; when they ask you for that, give it to them, and do not revile them, and be obedient to them.' And in the two Sahihs: 'Whoever dislikes something from his ruler, let him be patient, for whoever separates from the authority by a span will die a death of ignorance.' And in Muslim: 'Whoever is appointed over him a ruler and sees him committing something of disobedience to Allah, let him hate what he commits...'
Source pages p. 147

Commentary
This passage is the commentator's explanation of the Tahawiyyah phrase forbidding rebellion. It argues that after the rightly-guided caliphs, corruption and injustice appeared among rulers, yet the early Muslims (Salaf) did not rebel; they obeyed them and performed religious duties with their permission. The reason given is that infallibility is not a condition for imamate at the outset; thus, if an imam becomes unjust, he is not removed simply because he lacked something that was not required anyway. The commentator then cites three hadiths to support the obligation of obedience and patience: (1) from Abu Dawud: when tax collectors come demanding what is not due, still give and do not revile them; (2) from Bukhari and Muslim: whoever separates from the ruler by even a span dies a death of ignorance (i.e., rebellion is akin to jahiliyya); (3) from Muslim: if one sees his ruler committing a sin, he should hate the sin but not rebel (the rest of the hadith in the original continues 'and he should not withdraw a hand from obedience'). The lesson emphasizes that even with unjust rulers, patience and obedience in worldly matters are required, provided the ruler does not command direct disobedience to Allah.

Key Terms
الخروج
الأئمة
الخلفاء الراشدين
السلف
العصمة
الصبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think rebellion is permissible if the ruler is corrupt.
Correction: The hadiths confirm the opposite, commanding patience and forbidding rebellion, even if the ruler is unjust.

Checkpoint
What does the hadith in the two Sahihs say about someone who separates from the authority by a span?
A) He becomes a martyr
B) He dies a death of ignorance
C) He is still a Muslim
D) He is forgiven

Key Takeaway
Even under unjust rulers, rebellion is forbidden; patience and obedience in worldly matters are required, as taught by the Salaf and confirmed by multiple hadiths.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever felt justified in disobeying or opposing someone in authority (a parent, teacher, or leader) because you believed they were unfair? How does the hadith about 'separating from the authority by a span' challenge that feeling, and what concrete step can you take to practice patience while still hating the wrong?
?
The hadith commands you to hate the sin of the ruler but not the ruler himself. Think of a person in authority whose actions you dislike. Is your emotional response more about hating the act or the person? Humbly examine your heart: is there any trace of rebellion or resentment that would lead to a 'death of ignorance'?
?
The Salaf prayed behind unjust rulers. When was the last time you prioritized communal worship over personal grievance? If your leader were to do something you consider sinful, would your first impulse be to leave the mosque or to stay and pray? What does your impulse reveal about your understanding of this lesson?

Wiping over Khuffs as a Sunni Creedal Practice
Affirmation of wiping over khuffs as a Sunni creedal tenet with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the permissibility of wiping over khuffs in wudu is a firmly established Sunni doctrine based on mass-transmitted evidence and is considered a marker of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuffs is a foundational practice of Ahl al-Sunnah, backed by mass transmission.

The author of the Tahawiyyah now turns from purely theological matters to a practical ritual ruling that nonetheless has creedal weight. Wiping over leather socks (khuffs) during wudu was a point of contention between early sects. This passage establishes that acceptance of this practice is not just a juristic preference but a defining feature of Sunni identity, supported by overwhelming prophetic evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to absorb its rhythm, then read the full translation. Notice how multiple authorities are cited in rapid succession to build a cumulative case.
2
Identify the authorities and their claims
The passage names al-Hasan al-Basri, Imam Ahmad, al-Karkhi, and Abu Hanifah. For each, note what piece of evidence they bring and how strong they consider it.
Al-Karkhi and Abu Hanifah give especially strong warnings about rejecting this practice.
3
Connect to the definition of Ahl al-Sunnah
The final statement from Abu Hanifah lists three core Sunni beliefs, including wiping over khuffs. Ask yourself why a secondary fiqh ruling would be included in a creedal definition.
This shows that the practice was a distinguishing mark of early Sunni identity against opponents.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونرى المسح على الخفين) جائزا (في السفر والحضر كما جاء فعل الشارع لـه (في الأثر)؛ روي عن الحسن البصري أنه قال: حدثني سبعون رجلا من أصحاب النبي أنه مسح على الخفين، وعن الإمام أحمد: ليس في قلبي من المسح شيء، فيه أربعون حديثًا عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ما رفعوا وما وقفوا، وقال الكرخي: أخاف الكفر على من لم ير المسح على الخفين؛ لأن الآثار جاءت فيه في حيز التواتر»، وعن أبي حنيفة: ما قلت حتى جاءني فيه مثل ضوء النهار، «ما وروي عنه أنه سئل عن مذهب أهل السنة والجماعة فقال: هو أن تفضل الشيخين وأن تحب الختنين وأن ترى المسح على الخفين».
And we consider wiping over the khuffs permissible during travel and residence, as the action of the Lawgiver came regarding it in the transmitted report. It is narrated from al-Hasan al-Basri that he said: Seventy men from the companions of the Prophet narrated to me that he wiped over the khuffs. And from Imam Ahmad: There is nothing in my heart against wiping; there are forty hadiths from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, about it, whether they are elevated or stopped. And al-Karkhi said: I fear disbelief for one who does not consider wiping over the khuffs permissible, because the reports about it have reached the level of tawatur. And from Abu Hanifah: I did not say it until it came to me like the light of day. And it is narrated that he was asked about the madhhab of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, and he said: It is that you prefer the two shaykhs (Abu Bakr and 'Umar), that you love the two sons-in-law (Uthman and 'Ali), and that you consider wiping over the khuffs permissible.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage presents the evidence for the Sunni doctrine of wiping over khuffs during wudu. The commentary first states the ruling: it is permissible in both travel and residence, based on the practice of the Prophet. It then cites multiple authorities to demonstrate the strength of this position. Al-Hasan al-Basri reports from seventy Companions that the Prophet did it. Imam Ahmad notes that forty hadiths exist on the topic. Al-Karkhi warns that rejecting it may lead to disbelief because the narrations are mutawatir. Abu Hanifah emphasizes the clarity of the evidence. Finally, Abu Hanifah lists three core elements of Ahl al-Sunnah: preference for Abu Bakr and 'Umar, love for 'Uthman and 'Ali, and acceptance of wiping over khuffs. This firmly establishes the practice as a distinctive Sunni belief.

Key Terms
المسح على الخفين (wiping over khuffs)
التواتر (tawatur/mass transmission)
الشيخين (the two shaykhs/Abu Bakr and Umar)
الختنين (the two sons-in-law/Uthman and Ali)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Wiping over khuffs is a permissible but optional practice that can be rejected without creedal consequence.
Correction: Classical Sunni imams, as cited here, consider it a mass-transmitted (mutawatir) practice; rejecting it after knowing the evidence can lead to disbelief.

Checkpoint
What did al-Karkhi say about someone who does not consider wiping over khuffs permissible?
A) He is a sinner
B) He fears disbelief for him
C) He is excused due to ignorance
D) He should be asked to repent

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of wiping over khuffs is a mass-transmitted practice and a defining belief of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
After reading that this practice is established by mass transmission from the Prophet and Companions, ask yourself: Have I ever treated any sunna as optional or insignificant? Is there a sunna I have been neglecting because it seemed minor? Commit today to reviving one sunna you have overlooked, starting with this one if applicable.
?
Al-Karkhi feared kufr for rejecting a mass-transmitted matter. Do I have this level of reverence for the established teachings of the Prophet? Are there any beliefs or practices of the Salaf that I have doubted or dismissed? Resolve to study them with a heart open to certainty.
?
Abu Hanifah said the evidence for wiping over khuffs was as clear as daylight. Is my faith in the core tenets of Ahl al-Sunnah similarly clear and unwavering? What would it take for me to reach that level of conviction? Write down one step you will take this week to strengthen your certainty in a matter you have been unsure about.

Hajj and Jihad: Ongoing Obligations with All Rulers
Imam Tahawi states that Hajj and Jihad are ongoing obligations with all Muslim rulers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Hajj and Jihad remain obligatory regardless of the ruler's moral character, and how this is supported by consensus and prophetic hadith.

Core Idea
Hajj and Jihad are obligations that do not depend on the ruler's justice.

Imam Tahawi states that Hajj and Jihad are ongoing duties that must be performed with the Muslim rulers, regardless of whether they are righteous or sinful. This might seem surprising, as one might think that only a just ruler can lead such acts. In this lesson, we will read his statement and the commentary that supports it with evidence from the Salaf and the Prophet, peace be upon him.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the key terms 'فرضان ماضيان' and 'مع أولي الأمر برهم وفاجرهم'. Understand the core assertion.
2
Understand the consensus argument
The commentary mentions that the Salaf performed Hajj and Jihad with all rulers without disapproval, forming consensus. Reflect on why this is a strong proof.
Consensus (إجماع) is a primary source in Sunni law.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
The passage cites several hadith: from Bukhari about horses, and from Abu Dawud explicitly stating Jihad with every ruler. Consider how these support the obligation.
4
Analyze the commentary's logic
Al-Qastalani's commentary explains that the hadith about horses implies Jihad's reward is not conditional on the leader's justice. Follow this reasoning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالَحَجُ وَالجِهَادُ فَرْضَانِ مَاضِيَانِ مَعَ أُولِي الأَمْرِ مِنْ أَئِمَّةِ المُسْلِمِينَ بَرِّهِمْ وَفَاجِرِهِمْ لَا يُبْطِلُهُمَا شَيْءٌ وَلَا يَنْقُضُهُمَا . (و) نقول: (الحج والجهاد في سبيل الله تعالى (فرضان ثابتان (ماضیان) مع الصحة (مع أولي الأمر من أئمة المسلمين برهم) أي عادلهم (وفاجرهم) أي ظالمهم (لا يبطلهما شيء من ذلك الظلم (ولا ينقضها)؛ لأن بر الإمام ليس بشرط لصحتها، وقد كان السلف من الصحابة والتابعين يحجون ويجاهدون مع كل إمام بر أو فاجر من غير نكير؛ فكان ذلك إجماعا، وفي صحيح البخاري في باب الجهاد ماضي مع البر والفاجر لقول النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم «الخَيْلُ مَعْقُودٌ بِنَوَاصِيها الخَيْرُ إِلَى يَومِ القِيَامَةِ» . قال القسطلان: وذكر بقاء الخير في نواصي الخيل إلى يوم القيامة وفرة بالأجر، والمغنم المقترن بالأجر إنما يكون بالجهاد، ولم يقيد ذلك بما إذا كان الإمام عادلا؛ فدل على أنه لا فرق في حصول هذا الفضل بين أن يكون الغزو مع الإمام العادل أو الجائر، وأن الإسلام باقي وأهله إلى يوم القيامة؛ لأن من لازم بقاء الجهاد بقاء المجاهدين وهم المسلمون. وفي حديث أبي داود عن مكحول عن أبي هريرة مرفوعا: «الجِهَادُ وَاجِبٌ عَلَيْكُمْ مَعَ كُلِّ أَمِيرِ بَرًّا كَانَ أَوْ فَاجِرًا وَإِنْ عَمِلَ الكَبَائِرَ» . وإسناده لا بأس به؛ إلا أن مكحولا لم يسمع أبا هريرة، وفي حديث أنس عنده أيضًا مرفوعا: «وَالجِهَادُ مَاضٍ مُذْ بَعَثَنِي اللَّهُ إِلَى أَنْ يُقَاتِلَ أَخِرُ أُمَّتِي الدَّجَّالَ لَا يُبْطِلُهُ جَوْرُ جَائِرِ وَلَا عَدْلُ عَادِلٍ» .
And Hajj and Jihad are two ongoing obligations with those in authority from the leaders of the Muslims, their righteous and their sinful; nothing invalidates them and nothing nullifies them. (And) we say: (Hajj and Jihad in the path of Allah Almighty are two established obligations, ongoing, with soundness, with those in authority from the leaders of the Muslims, their righteous) meaning their just, (and their sinful) meaning their oppressor; (nothing of that oppression invalidates them, and nothing nullifies them) because the righteousness of the leader is not a condition for their validity. And indeed the Salaf from the Companions and the Followers performed Hajj and Jihad with every leader, righteous or sinful, without disapproval; so that was a consensus. And in Sahih al-Bukhari, in the chapter of Jihad ongoing with the righteous and the sinful, due to the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'Horses have goodness tied to their forelocks until the Day of Resurrection.' Al-Qastalani said: And his mention of the continuation of goodness in the forelocks of horses until the Day of Resurrection is an abundance of reward, and the spoil coupled with reward is only attained through Jihad, and he did not restrict that to when the leader is just; so it indicates that there is no difference in obtaining this merit between whether the expedition is with a just leader or an unjust one, and that Islam and its people remain until the Day of Resurrection; because from the necessary concomitants of the continuation of Jihad is the continuation of the mujahideen, and they are the Muslims. And in the hadith of Abu Dawud from Mak-hul from Abu Hurairah, raised to the Prophet: 'Jihad is obligatory upon you with every ruler, whether righteous or sinful, even if he commits major sins.' And its chain is not problematic, except that Mak-hul did not hear from Abu Hurairah. And in the hadith of Anas with him also, raised: 'And Jihad is ongoing from the time Allah sent me until the last of my community fights the Dajjal; it is not invalidated by the oppression of an oppressor nor by the justice of a just person.'
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage is a statement from Imam Tahawi followed by a commentary that defends the obligation of Hajj and Jihad with all Muslim rulers, regardless of their moral state. The author begins by affirming that Hajj and Jihad are two continuous obligations (فرضان ماضيان) that must be performed under the authority of the Muslim leaders, both the righteous (بر) and the sinful (فاجر). Nothing can invalidate or nullify these duties. The commentary explains that the righteousness of the Imam is not a prerequisite for the validity of these acts. This is supported by the practice of the Salaf—the Companions and Followers—who performed Hajj and Jihad with every leader without objection, forming a consensus (إجماع). The author then cites a hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari where the Prophet said that goodness is tied to horses' forelocks until the Day of Resurrection. Al-Qastalani's interpretation is quoted: the hadith promises reward and spoil through Jihad without restricting it to just rulers, indicating that the merit remains regardless of the leader's justice. Furthermore, the continuation of Jihad implies the continuation of Muslims. Additional evidence is provided from Abu Dawud's hadiths: one via Mak-hul (with a minor chain issue) stating Jihad is obligatory with every ruler, even the sinful; and another from Anas stating that Jihad is ongoing from the Prophet's time until the end times, not invalidated by any ruler's justice or injustice. The overall argument is that Hajj and Jihad are perpetual communal obligations that do not depend on the moral character of the ruler.

Key Terms
الحج
الجهاد
فرضان ماضيان
أولي الأمر
بر
فاجر
إجماع
الخيل معقود بنواصيها الخير

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that Hajj and Jihad are only valid under a just ruler.
Correction: The passage clarifies that they are obligatory regardless of the ruler's justice, and the Salaf practiced them with all rulers.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling regarding performing Hajj and Jihad with a sinful ruler?
A) It is not permissible because the ruler is sinful.
B) It is permissible but disliked.
C) It is obligatory and valid, and nothing invalidates it.
D) It is only valid if the ruler is just.

Key Takeaway
Hajj and Jihad are perpetual obligations that remain valid with all Muslim rulers, ensuring continuity of worship and community.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever hesitated to perform a religious duty because you disapproved of the leader's character? What does this lesson say to that hesitation?
?
If you knew your ruler was unjust, would you still support Jihad under his command? How does the Salaf's example challenge your comfort zone?
?
What would it cost you personally to obey this teaching and perform Hajj or support Jihad with a ruler you consider sinful? Are you willing to pay that cost?

Hadith Proof for Jihad Under All Rulers
The author cites two Prophetic hadiths proving jihad's obligation under all rulers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that jihad remains obligatory under any ruler, even unjust ones, based on two hadiths from Sunan Abi Dawud.

Core Idea
Jihad is obligatory with every ruler, regardless of their righteousness, and it continues until the end of time.

The author of the commentary now provides direct hadith evidence to support the doctrine of jihad under all rulers. These two narrations from Abu Dawud make clear that the duty of jihad does not depend on the ruler's moral character. As you read, notice how the author also addresses the slight chain issue in the first hadith.

Guided Path
1
Read the two hadiths carefully
Examine the Arabic text and translation. The first hadith emphasizes obligation under any ruler; the second emphasizes continuity until the Dajjal.
Note the chain remark by the author.
2
Identify the key phrases
Spot phrases like 'مع كل أمير برا كان أو فاجرا' and 'لا يبطله جور جائر ولا عدل عادل'.
3
Reflect on the implication
Ask: Why is it important that jihad is not invalidated by injustice? How does this relate to the broader creedal position?
This connects to the Sunni view of obedience to rulers in religious duties.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي حديث أبي داود عن مكحول عن أبي هريرة مرفوعا: «الجِهَادُ وَاجِبٌ عَلَيْكُمْ مَعَ كُلِّ أَمِيرِ بَرًّا كَانَ أَوْ فَاجِرًا وَإِنْ عَمِلَ الكَبَائِرَ»، وإسناده لا بأس به؛ إلا أن مكحولا لم يسمع أبا هريرة، وفي حديث أنس عنده أيضًا مرفوعا: وَالجِهَادُ مَاضٍ مُذْ بَعَثَنِي اللَّهُ إِلَى أَنْ يُقَاتِلَ أَخِرُ أُمَّتِي الدَّجَّالَ لَا يُبْطِلُهُ جَوْرُ جَاثِرِ [؟] وَلَا عَدْلُ عَادِلٍ اهـ.
And in the hadith of Abu Dawud from Makhul from Abu Hurairah, raised (to the Prophet): 'Jihad is obligatory upon you with every amir, whether he is righteous or wicked, even if he commits major sins.' And its chain is acceptable, except that Makhul did not hear from Abu Hurairah. And in the hadith of Anas (also) from him, raised: 'And jihad is ongoing from the time Allah sent me until the last of my community fights the Dajjal; it is not invalidated by the injustice of an unjust person nor by the justice of a just person.' End.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage presents a hadith-based proof for the obligation of jihad under all leaders, regardless of their moral character. The author begins by citing a hadith from Abu Dawud narrated by Makhul from Abu Hurairah, in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) declares that jihad is obligatory with every amir (ruler), whether he is righteous (barr) or wicked (fajir), even if he commits major sins. The author then comments on the chain: it is acceptable except that Makhul did not directly hear from Abu Hurairah, implying a slight weakness but not severe. Then the author cites a second hadith from Anas, also in Abu Dawud, where the Prophet states that jihad continues from the time of his mission until the end times when the last of his community fights the Dajjal (Antichrist). This jihad is not nullified by the injustice of an unjust ruler (jawr jā'ir) nor by the justice of a just ruler. The phrase 'لا يُبْطِلُهُ جَوْرُ جَائِرٍ وَلَا عَدْلُ عَادِلٍ' emphasizes that no human action can abrogate the obligation of jihad; it remains a perpetual duty. Together, these hadiths affirm that the legitimacy of jihad does not depend on the ruler's piety, and that the duty continues despite political or moral conditions.

Key Terms
الجهاد
أمير
الكبائر
الدجال
جور
عدل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Jihad is only valid under a just ruler.
Correction: These hadiths affirm jihad is obligatory even with unjust rulers who commit major sins.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited, what does the Prophet say about jihad with a wicked ruler?
A) It is not valid because the ruler is sinful.
B) It is obligatory even if the ruler commits major sins.
C) It is recommended but not obligatory.
D) It depends on the ruler's repentance.

Key Takeaway
Jihad is a perpetual duty that does not depend on the ruler's piety and continues until the end of time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider that jihad is obligatory even under an unjust ruler, does that challenge your willingness to participate in any form of collective struggle for Islam? What holds you back?
?
The hadith says jihad continues until the Dajjal. Do you live with a sense of ongoing responsibility, or do you think jihad is a past duty? How does this affect your daily priorities?
?
The Prophet said jihad is not invalidated by injustice. Are you quick to excuse yourself from supporting Islamic causes because the leaders are imperfect? What would it take for you to commit to the duty regardless?

Comprehensive Recording by the Noble Scribes
Commentary on the comprehensiveness of the recording angels.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the recording angels record all deeds, including unintentional utterances and sighs, and that this includes disbelievers.

Core Idea
Not even a sigh is missed by the scribes.

This lesson examines the Tahawiyyah's belief in the noble scribes. We see that their recording is comprehensive, covering every action and utterance, intentional or not, and that this applies to all people, believers and disbelievers alike.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on scribes
Read the Arabic and translation carefully to understand the author's description of the angels as 'preservers' who neglect nothing.
Notice the phrase 'لا يهملون من شأنهم شيئاً'.
2
Identify Imam Malik's argument
See how Imam Malik uses the generality of verse 50:18 to conclude that even a groan is recorded.
The verse: 'ما يلفظ من قول إلا لديه رقيب عتيد'.
3
Recognize inclusion of disbelievers
The passage states that the disbeliever is included because his breaths and deeds are recorded for or against him.
This shows the recording is universal.
4
Reflect on implications
Consider how this knowledge affects one's awareness of accountability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونؤمن بالملائكة الكرام الكاتبين، وأن الله قد جعلهم لأفعال العباد مما لهم وعليهم حافظين؛ أي لا يهملون من شأنهم شيئاً فعلوه قصداً أو ذهولاً أو نسياناً صحةً أو مرضاً؛ قال الإمام مالك: يكتبون على العبد كل شيء حتى أنينه في مرضه؛ محتجاً بإفادة الآية العموم، وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿ما يلفظ من قول إلا لديه رقيب عتيد﴾ [سورة ق آية 18]؛ وحينئذ يدخل في العبد الكافر لأنه تضبط أنفاسه وأعماله له أو عليه؛ قال النووي: والصواب الذي عليه المحققون، بل نقل فيه بعضهم الإجماع، أن الكافر إذا فعل أفعالاً جميلة كالصدقة وصلة الرحم ثم أسلم ومات على الإسلام أن ثواب عمله يكتب له، أما دعوى مخالفته للقواعد فغير مسلمة. قلت: وضابطه كما قاله بعضهم: إذا كانت لا تتوقف على نية. وذكر بعضهم أن المعقبات في قوله تعالى: ﴿له معقبات من بين يديه ومن خلفه يحفظونه من أمر الله﴾ [سورة الرعد آية 11] غير الكاتبين بلا خلاف، وعن عثمان أنه سأل النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كم ملكاً على الإنسان فذكر عشرين ملكاً. قال المهدوي: وذكر الآبي أنه يحفظ لابن عطية أن كل آدمي يوكل به من حين وقوعه نطفة في الرحم إلى موته أربعمائة ملك. كذا ذكره اللقاني. وعلى ذلك ففي كلام المصنف مسألتان، وظاهر الآثار أن الكتب حقيقي وعلم الآلة مفوض إلى الله تعالى.
We believe in the angels, the noble scribes, and that Allah has made them preservers of the deeds of the servants, both what is for them and what is against them; meaning they do not neglect anything of their affairs that they have done intentionally, inadvertently, or forgetfully, in health or sickness. Imam Malik said: They write down everything from the servant, even his groaning in his sickness; arguing from the generality of the verse, which is His statement: 'He does not utter a word except that there is a watcher ready' [Surah Qaf verse 18]; and then this includes the disbelieving servant because his breaths and deeds are recorded for him or against him. Al-Nawawi said: The correct view upon which the verifiers agree, nay, some have transmitted consensus on it, is that if a disbeliever does beautiful actions like charity and maintaining family ties, then becomes Muslim and dies upon Islam, the reward for his action is written for him. As for the claim that it contradicts the principles, it is not accepted. I said: And its criterion is as some have said: if it does not depend on intention. And some mentioned that the 'mu'aqqibat' (guardian angels) in His statement: 'For him are angels succeeding before him and behind him, guarding him by the command of Allah' [Surah Ra'd verse 11] are other than the scribes, without dispute. And it is narrated from Uthman that he asked the Prophet, peace be upon him, how many angels are over a human, and he mentioned twenty angels. Al-Mahdawi said: And al-Abi mentioned that it is preserved from Ibn Atiyya that every human is entrusted from the time he becomes a drop in the womb until his death with four hundred angels. Thus mentioned by al-Laqqani. And upon this, in the words of the author there are two issues, and the apparent meaning of the reports is that the recording is real, and the knowledge of the instrument is referred to Allah the Exalted.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is a continuous commentary on the Tahawiyyah's statement of belief in the noble scribes (al-kirām al-kātibīn). The author explains that these angels are made 'preservers' (hāfiẓīn) of human deeds, meaning they neglect nothing—whether done intentionally, inadvertently, forgetfully, in health or illness. He then cites Imam Mālik, who argued from the Qur'anic verse (50:18) that even a groan in sickness is recorded, because the verse states that every utterance has a watcher. This generality includes the disbeliever, whose breaths and deeds are recorded for or against him. Next, al-Nawawī is quoted to address a specific ruling: if a disbeliever performs good deeds sincerely prior to Islam and then converts and dies as a Muslim, the reward for those deeds is written for him. The author (al-Maydānī) interjects with 'qultu' and provides a criterion: the deed must not require intention (niyya) to be valid, as good deeds like charity are intrinsically rewarded. He then addresses a separate point: the 'mu'aqqibāt' (guardian angels) mentioned in Surah Ra'd (13:11) are distinct from the recording scribes, as they guard by Allah's command, not record. Finally, a report from 'Uthmān states the Prophet mentioned twenty angels over a human, but al-Mahdawī relates through al-Ābī and Ibn 'Aṭiyya that each human is assigned 400 angels from the time of being a drop in the womb until death. The lesson concludes by noting that the author's words contain two issues, and the apparent meaning of the transmitted reports is that the recording is real (ḥaqīqī), while the exact nature of the instrument ('ilm al-āla) is known to Allah.

Key Terms
الملائكة الكرام الكاتبين
الحفظة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only major deeds are recorded
Correction: The passage states that even a groan in sickness is recorded, so no deed is too small.

Checkpoint
According to Imam Malik, what is included in what the recording angels write down?
A) Only major sins and good deeds
B) Everything, including even the groan of a sick person
C) Only spoken words
D) Only intentional acts

Key Takeaway
The recording angels leave nothing out, not even a sigh, and this applies to all people.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You know that every word you speak is recorded, including even a sigh of complaint. When you are alone in your room and you murmur in frustration, does that moment seem trivial? How does knowing that the noble scribes write it change the way you will speak in private?
?
The lesson says even your groaning in sickness is written. Have you ever considered that your suffering is not unnoticed by Allah? Does this knowledge make you more mindful of your patience or more afraid of your impatience?
?
It is said that the recording includes disbelievers. If you have a non-Muslim friend or relative, do you ever think about the fact that their every word is recorded? How might that affect your urgency in conveying the truth to them?

Additional Rulings on Recording Angels
Commentary on rulings related to recording angels and their numbers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that good deeds performed before Islam are rewarded upon conversion, that the guardian angels are distinct from the scribes, and that the recording is real.

Core Idea
Good deeds before Islam are not wasted; angels guard and record.

The commentary continues with several important details. Al-Nawawi clarifies that a disbeliever who does good deeds and later converts will be rewarded for those deeds. Then we learn that the guardian angels (mu'aqqibat) are different from the scribes. Finally, reports about the number of angels per person and the reality of recording are discussed.

Guided Path
1
Read the second half of the passage
Focus on al-Nawawi's ruling and the subsequent points.
2
Understand al-Nawawi's ruling on pre-Islam good deeds
Note that the correct view is that such deeds are rewarded after conversion, provided they do not depend on intention.
The criterion: actions like charity and family ties.
3
Distinguish between scribes and guardian angels
The mu'aqqibat are not the recording angels; they guard by command of Allah.
Surah Ra'd 13:11.
4
Consider the number of angels
There are different reports: 20 angels according to Uthman, and 400 according to another narration.
These numbers may indicate different categories or functions.
5
Conclude on the reality of recording
The recording is real (haqiqi), but its exact mechanism is known only to Allah.

Belief in the Four Hundred Angels and the Reality of the Books of Deeds
Commentator explains a hadith about four hundred angels and deduces two issues concerning the books of deeds

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the hadith about four hundred angels affirms the reality of the books of deeds and that only Allah knows the exact nature of the recording instrument.

Core Idea
The books of deeds are real, and their exact nature is known only to Allah.

In this passage, the commentator cites a hadith about four hundred angels appointed over every person. From this, he draws two important theological conclusions: that the books recording our deeds are real (haqiqi) and that the knowledge of how they are written (the instrument) belongs solely to Allah. This affirms the reality of divine recording while humbly acknowledging our limited understanding.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and the commentator's explanation
The hadith says four hundred angels are appointed from conception to death. Understand that this is a specific number mentioned in tradition.
Note the source: al-Laqqani is cited.
2
Identify the two issues
The commentator says there are two issues in the author's speech. What are they? Look for the phrase 'مسألتان'.
3
Reflect on the reality of the books
The books are real, not metaphorical. What does this mean for our belief in divine recording?
This affirms that every deed is recorded truly.
4
Understand the delegation of knowledge
Only Allah knows the instrument (the means). This humbles our intellect and reminds us of Allah's exclusive knowledge.
The exact mechanism is beyond human grasp.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يوكل به من حين وقوعه نطفة في الرحم إلى موته أربعمائة ملك. كذا ذكره اللقاني). وعلى ذلك ففي كلام المصنف مسألتان، وظاهر الآثار أن الكتب حقيقي وعلم الآلة مفوض إلى الله تعالى.
He is entrusted, from the time he becomes a drop in the womb until his death, with four hundred angels. Thus mentioned by al-Laqqani). And based on that, in the author's speech there are two issues, and the apparent meaning of the hadith reports is that the books are real and the knowledge of the instrument is delegated to Allah.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage cites a hadith stating that four hundred angels are appointed over a person from conception to death. The commentator, citing al-Laqqani, then notes that this hadith gives rise to two issues in the author's (al-Tahawi's) words. The apparent sense of the transmitted reports is that the books (of deeds) are real (haqiqi) and that the knowledge of the instrument (al-alah, likely the pen or the means of recording) is consigned to Allah alone. This affirms the reality of the written records of deeds and emphasizes that only Allah knows their exact nature.

Correction: The commentator explicitly states that the apparent meaning is that the books are real (haqiqi).

Key Takeaway
The hadith of the four hundred angels affirms the reality of the books of deeds and that only Allah knows the instrument of recording.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
Imagine standing before the book of your deeds tomorrow. Would you be eager to see it or terrified to open it? Commit one specific action you will take today to ensure that book speaks of mercy and truth.

The Angel of Death and the Meaning of 'Alamin
Defines Angel of Death and explains 'alamin with rational proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the role of the Angel of Death and the comprehensive meaning of 'alamin in Islamic theology.

Core Idea
'Alamin is everything besides Allah, pointing to His existence.

This lesson begins with an affirmation of faith in the Angel of Death, who is appointed by Allah to take souls at their appointed times. Then the commentator explains the term 'alamin, which is often misunderstood as merely 'worlds'. He defines it as everything other than Allah and provides a rational argument that all contingent beings point to the Necessarily Existent.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the two parts: first the belief in the Angel of Death, then the definition of 'alamin and its proof.
The passage links faith in the unseen with a rational argument about creation.
2
Understand the Angel of Death's role
Identify who the Angel of Death is and what his specific task is according to the text. He is appointed by Allah to take souls of all the 'worlds' at the end of their terms.
3
Analyze the term 'alamin
The commentator defines 'alamin as a plural of 'alam, meaning a sign or instrument by which one knows. Here it refers to everything that indicates the Maker, i.e., everything besides Allah.
This includes both substances (jawahir) and accidents (a'rad).
4
Reflect on the rational proof
The passage provides a rational argument: all possible things (mumkin) need an effectant that is self-necessarily existent (wajib li-dhatihi). This shows that the existence of creation points to Allah.
This is a classic kalam argument for the existence of God.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإيمان بملك الموت وعذاب القبر والسؤال فيه ونؤمن بملك الموت الموكل من الله تعالى بقبض أرواح العالمين) عند انتهاء آجالها، والعالمين: جمع عالم، وهو اسم لما يُعلم به كالخاتم غُلب فيما يُعلم به الصانع، وهو كل ما سواه من الجواهر والأعراض؛ فإنها لإمكانها وافتقارها إلى مؤثر واجب لذاته تدل على وجوده
Faith in the Angel of Death and the Punishment of the Grave and the Questioning in It. And we believe in the Angel of Death appointed by Allah to take the souls of the worlds at the end of their terms. And 'alamin: plural of 'alam, which is a noun for that by which one knows, like a seal, predominantly used for that by which the Maker is known. And it is everything other than Him from substances and accidents; for their contingency and need for an effectant necessarily self-existent indicate His existence.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage begins with the heading affirming belief in the Angel of Death, grave punishment, and questioning. The commentator then explains the belief in the Angel of Death (malak al-mawt) who is appointed specifically by Allah to take the souls of all the worlds (al-'alamin) when their terms end. The term 'alamin is then defined: it is the plural of 'alam, which originally means a sign or instrument by which one knows, like a seal. Here it is predominantly used for that by which the Maker (al-Sani') is known. Thus, 'alamin includes everything other than Allah from substances (jawahir) and accidents (a'rad). The commentator gives a rational argument: because these entities are possible (mumkin) and in need of an effectant, and that effectant must be self-necessarily existent (wajib li-dhatihi), they indicate His existence.

Key Terms
ملك الموت
قبض
أرواح
عالمين
جوهر
عرض
ممكن
واجب لذاته

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think 'alamin refers only to humans or limited groups of creatures.
Correction: The commentator clearly states that 'alamin includes everything besides Allah, encompassing all substances and accidents.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what does the term 'alamin refer to?
A) Only humans.
B) Everything that exists besides Allah including substances and accidents.
C) The known worlds like earth and heavens.
D) The angels and jinn only.

Key Takeaway
The Angel of Death takes souls of all creation, and 'alamin means everything other than Allah, whose contingency points to His necessary existence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You are part of 'alamin—contingent and in need of the Necessary Being. Do you live each day with that awareness, or do you act as if you are self-sufficient? What will you do today to consciously depend on Allah?
?
The Angel of Death will take your soul at its appointed term. If your term ended tonight, would you be ready? What is one thing you need to change before that moment, and when will you start?
?
When you look at your own existence—your body, your possessions, your abilities—do you see them as signs of the Maker, or do you take them for granted? Name one specific thing you will use today to remind yourself of Allah's existence.

The Disagreement on How the Angel of Death Takes Souls
Disagreement on direct or assisted soul-taking.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly disagreement on whether the Angel of Death takes souls directly or through assistants.

Core Idea
The Angel of Death may take souls directly or through helpers.

Scholars differ on how the Angel of Death, Azrael, carries out his task of taking souls. Some hold that he takes them directly from their place, while others believe he employs assistant angels for extraction. This lesson presents the main views.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the disagreement.
2
Identify the two views
Note the two positions: direct taking from the soul's abode vs. taking from the hands of his assistants.
3
Consider the scope
Reflect on the list of creatures mentioned: from fleas to angels, showing the universality of death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واختلف هل القبض من مقرها أو من يد أعوانه المعالجين لنزعها من برغوث وبعوض وبشر وملك وجن برا وبحرا، حتى روح نفسه كما قيل وقيل : يقبضها الله تعالى كما قيل إنه يقبض أرواح شهداء البحر، وروي أنه سئل الإمام مالك: أيقبض أرواح البراغيث؟ فقال: ألها أنفس؟ قيل: نعم، قال: يقبضها.
And they differed: is the taking from their place or from the hands of his assistants who are occupied with extracting them, from flea, mosquito, human, angel, and jinn, on land and sea, even his own soul, as is said. And it is said: Allah takes them, as it is said that He takes the souls of martyrs of the sea. And it is narrated that Imam Malik was asked: Does he take the souls of fleas? He said: Do they have souls? He was told: Yes. He said: He takes them.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage discusses a point of scholarly disagreement regarding the mode of soul-taking. The Angel of Death is generally entrusted with taking souls, but there is debate. Some say he takes them directly from their abode (the body), others say he takes them through the hands of his assistant angels who are tasked with extracting them from every kind of creature: flea, mosquito, human, angel, jinn, on land and sea, even his own soul (the Angel's own soul at his death). Another view is that Allah Himself takes some souls, specifically those of martyrs at sea. The commentator then relates a well-known incident: Imam Malik was asked if the Angel of Death takes the souls of fleas. Malik replied by asking whether fleas have souls. Upon being told they do, he affirmed that the Angel takes them as well, thus indicating that no creature is excluded.

Key Terms
قبض
أعوان
معالجين
روح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is one of the views on how the Angel of Death takes souls?
A) He sends diseases.
B) He takes them directly from their place.
C) He only takes souls of believers.
D) He waits for the Hour.

Key Takeaway
The Angel of Death takes souls of all creatures, possibly directly or through assistants.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the Angel of Death may take your soul directly, without any intermediary, does that make the moment of death more immediate and personal for you? How does that change the urgency of preparing for that encounter today?
?
The passage mentions that even the Angel of Death's own soul will be taken. Are you living as if your own soul will be taken at an unknown moment? What specific act of obedience can you commit to today to ensure that when your soul is taken, it is in a state pleasing to Allah?

The Nature of the Soul According to Ahl al-Sunna
Definition of the soul as a subtle body with supporting authorities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the position of Ahl al-Sunna that the soul is a subtle body permeating the body, and how this view is supported by scholars and analogies.

Core Idea
The soul is a subtle body interwoven with the body, not a purely spiritual entity.

In this passage, the commentator presents the Sunni consensus on the nature of the soul. While there is disagreement on its reality, the established view of Ahl al-Sunna is that the soul is a subtle body (jism latif) that permeates the body. This understanding unites theologians, hadith scholars, jurists, and Sufis. Read on to see how this position is articulated and supported by authorities like Imam al-Nawawi and Ibn Arafa.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage slowly, then its literal translation. Notice the vocabulary for 'subtle body' (jism latif) and 'intertwined' (mushtabik).
The passage also includes a biographical note on Ibn Arafa.
2
Identify the key claim
The passage states that Ahl al-Sunna holds the soul to be a subtle body that permeates the physical body, and life departs when it leaves.
3
Analyze the analogy
Some scholars describe the soul's relation to the body like water in a green branch – inseparable and permeating. Reflect on how this clarifies the subtle body concept.
This analogy emphasizes organic unity.
4
Recognize scholarly support
Imam al-Nawawi affirmed this view, and the passage includes a biographical note on Ibn Arafa al-Maliki, showing the wide acceptance among scholars.
Ibn Arafa was a prominent Maliki scholar.
5
Consider the implications
Think about how this view of the soul as a subtle body differs from purely spiritual conceptions. How does it affect understanding of life, death, and resurrection?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واختلف في حقيقة الروح، ومذهب أهل السنة من المتكلمين والمحدثين والفقهاء والصوفية أنها جسم لطيف متخلل في البدن تذهب الحياة بذهابها، وعبارة بعض المحققين هي جسم لطيف مشتبك بالبدن اشتباك الماء بالعود الأخضر، وبه جزم النووي ونقل تصحيحه عن أصحابهم، وابن عرفة المالكي (1) محمد بن محمد بن محمد بن عرفة، أبو عبدالله الورغمي التونسي المالكي، إمام علامة، سمع من الوادي آشي وابن سلمة وغيرهما، برع في الأصول والفروع والعربية والحساب وكان حافظا للمذهب ضابطاً لقواعده إليه الرحلة في الفتوى، وكان رأسًا في العبادة والزهد، من مصنفاته: المبسوط في المذهب ومختصر الحوفي في الفرائض، توفي سنة ٧٤٨هـا وقيل غير ذلك.
And they differed regarding the reality of the soul, and the madhhab of Ahl al-Sunna from the mutakallimun, hadith scholars, jurists, and Sufis is that it is a subtle body permeating the body; life departs with its departure. The expression of some investigators is: it is a subtle body intertwined with the body like the interweaving of water with a green branch. An-Nawawi affirmed this and transmitted its authentication from his companions. And Ibn Arafa al-Maliki (1) Muhammad bin Muhammad bin Muhammad bin Arafa, Abu Abdullah al-Warghami al-Tunisi al-Maliki, an imam and scholar, heard from al-Wadi Ashi and Ibn Salama and others, excelled in usul and furu', Arabic and mathematics, was a preserver of the madhhab, a master of its principles, the destination for fatwa, and a leader in worship and asceticism. Among his works: al-Mabsut in the madhhab and Mukhtasar al-Hawfi in inheritance. He died in the year 748 H, and it is also said otherwise.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage addresses the nature of the soul (ruh). The commentator notes that there is disagreement on its reality, but then presents the position of Ahl al-Sunna (the Sunni consensus) comprising theologians (mutakallimun), hadith scholars (muhaddithun), jurists (fuqaha'), and Sufis (sufiyya). Their view is that the soul is a subtle body (jism latif) that permeates the body (mutakhalil fi al-badan). Life ceases when the soul departs. Some scholars express it as the soul being intertwined with the body like water in a green branch, inseparable. The commentator then reports that Imam al-Nawawi affirmed this view and transmitted its authentication from his teachers. Finally, a detailed biographical note on Ibn Arafa al-Maliki is given, listing his full name, teachers, expertise, works, and death date.

Key Terms
روح
جسم لطيف
متخلل
مشتبك

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The soul is a purely non-physical spirit with no connection to the body.
Correction: According to Ahl al-Sunna, the soul is a subtle body that permeates and intertwines with the physical body, not a disembodied spirit.

Checkpoint

A) A non-physical spirit.
B) A subtle body that permeates the body.
C) The blood.
D) The mind.

Key Takeaway
Ahl al-Sunna holds the soul to be a subtle body permeating the body, whose departure causes death.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the soul is a subtle body that departs at death, are you living today as if that departure could happen at any moment? What would change if you truly believed your soul could leave your body before sunset?
?
The soul is intertwined with your body like water in a green branch. Is your soul being nourished by obedience and remembrance, or is it drying up from neglect? What one action can you take today to strengthen that connection?
?
Knowing that the scholars of Ahl al-Sunna—mutakallimun, muhaddithun, fuqaha', and Sufis—agree on the soul being a subtle body, do you submit to their consensus even if it challenges modern notions of a purely immaterial soul? Are you willing to let their understanding shape your belief, or do you cling to your own assumptions?

Belief in the Questioning by Munkar and Nakir
Maydani explains the questioning of the dead by Munkar and Nakir, their names, and number.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic belief in the questioning of the deceased by Munkar and Nakir, including the significance of their names and the differing views on their number.

Core Idea
The angels Munkar and Nakir question the dead; their names are titles, not insults.

Imam Maydani continues his explanation of the sam‘iyyat (matters known through revelation) by addressing the reality of the grave questioning. The Prophet ﷺ taught that every deceased person is questioned about his Lord, religion, and prophet. Maydani clarifies the names of the two angels, Munkar and Nakir, and addresses a common misconception about their names implying disapproval. He also notes variant reports about their number.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the original Arabic and the translation to grasp the author's phrasing.
2
Identify the core belief
The passage asserts belief in the questioning by Munkar and Nakir absolutely. Note the conditional opinion mentioned.
Some scholars said it's only for disbelievers.
3
Understand the significance of the names
The names Munkar and Nakir are not pejorative; they are titles. The author explains that names are not inherently good or bad.
4
Note the variations in number
The standard view is two angels, but a report from Hilyat Abi Nu‘aym mentions three. Also, al-‘Iraqi narrated that for believers, the angels are bringers of good news.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) نؤمن بسؤال ( الملكين (منكر ونكير للميت) مطلقا، وقيل: للكافر فقط، وتسميتهما بمنكر ونكير ليست على جهة الذم وإنما هي لقب، وليس في الأسماء والذوات قبيح ولا حسن للذات والمتعارف أنهما اثنان، وفي حلية أبي نعيم ثلاثة: منكر ونكير وناكور (1) ، وحكى العراقي (٧) أن ملكي المؤمن مبشر ...
And we believe in the questioning of the two angels (Munkar and Nakir for the deceased) absolutely. And it is said: only for the disbeliever. Their naming as Munkar and Nakir is not in the way of blame; rather, it is a title. There is no ugliness or beauty in names and essences in themselves. And the well-known is that they are two. In Hilyat Abi Nu‘aym, there are three: Munkar, Nakir, and Nakur. And al-‘Iraqi narrated that the two angels of the believer are bringers of good news...
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage addresses the belief in the questioning of the deceased by two angels, Munkar and Nakir. The author affirms this belief absolutely (mutlaqan), but notes an opinion that it applies only to the disbeliever. He clarifies that the names Munkar and Nakir do not imply disapproval (dhamm); they are simply titles (laqab). The author states that names and essences (dhat) are not inherently good or evil—it is the actions and rulings that determine that. Then he mentions the standard view that there are two angels. However, he cites a report from Hilyat al-Awliya' by Abu Nu‘aym that mentions three: Munkar, Nakir, and Nakur. He also references al-‘Iraqi's narration that the two angels for the believer are bringers of glad tidings (mubashshir). This shows that the same angels appear differently based on the person's faith. The passage aims to establish the reality of the grave questioning and address minor variations in the naming and number of the angels.

Key Terms
منكر ونكير
لقب
الملكين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The names Munkar and Nakir imply that these angels are evil or disapproved.
Correction: The author explicitly states that the names are titles, not terms of blame. Names and essences are not inherently good or evil; moral judgment applies to actions.

Checkpoint
What is the purpose of the names Munkar and Nakir according to the passage?
A) They indicate the angels are disgraced
B) They are titles, not terms of blame
C) They mean 'concealers' of truth
D) They are descriptive of their ugly appearance

Key Takeaway
Belief in the questioning of the grave by Munkar and Nakir is part of Islamic creed, and their names are merely titles not implying blame.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If an angel named 'Denied' (Nakir) came to question you tonight, would your answers bring you peace or terror? What in your life right now would make that difference?
?
The author says names are not inherently good or evil. Yet the names Munkar and Nakir sound frightening. Are you afraid of the grave's questioning? What does that fear reveal about your current state of faith and actions?
?
For believers, the angels are bringers of good news. Do you live in such a way that you genuinely hope for that good news? What one change in your daily routine would reflect that hope starting today?

Author affirms belief in the questioning by Munkar and Nakir and clarifies issues about their names, number, and scope.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic belief in the questioning in the grave by the angels Munkar and Nakir, including the significance of their names and the scope of this questioning.

Core Idea
The grave's questioning by Munkar and Nakir is a reality for every soul, and their names are not insults but titles.

This lesson introduces the foundational belief in the questioning of the dead by two angels, Munkar and Nakir. The author of the Tahawiyyah begins by affirming this belief and clarifying common misconceptions about the angels' names and whether the questioning is limited to those physically buried in graves.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then the translation to grasp the basic affirmation of belief in the questioning.
2

Pay attention to the author's statement that 'Munkar' and 'Nakir' are not derogatory but simply titles.
Names and essences have no inherent moral quality.
3
Observe the discussion on number and alternative names
Note that the common understanding is two angels, but some reports mention three or alternative names for the believer's angels.
4
Consider the scope of the questioning
Understand that the mention of 'grave' is according to the norm; the questioning applies to all deceased regardless of burial.
This addresses a common misunderstanding.
