(و) نؤمن بسؤال الملكين (منكر ونكير) للميت مطلقا، وقيل: للكافر فقط، وتسميتهما بمنكر ونكير ليست على جهة الذم وإنما هي لقب، وليس في الأسماء والذوات قبيح ولا حسن للذات والمتعارف أنهما اثنان، وفي حلية أبي نعيم ثلاثة: منكر ونكير وناكور، وحكى العراقي أن ملكي المؤمن مبشر وبشير كذا ذكره المنلا إلياس. وقوله: (في قبره) جرى على الغالب، وإلا فمن أكلته السباع وأحرقته النار ومن لم يدفن يأتيانه من حيث شاء الله تعالى ويسألانه كما يعلم الله تعالى، وكأن المصنف جرى على ظاهر الحديث؛ ففي الترمذي عن أبي هريرة مرفوعا: «إِذَا قُبِرَ الميت - أو قال: أَحَدُكُمْ - أَتَاهُ مَلَكَانِ أَسْوَدَانِ أَزْرَقَانِ يُقَالُ لِأَحَدِهِمَا: مُنْكَرُ وَالآخَرُ نَكِيرُ، وَيَقُولَانِ: مَا كُنْتَ تَقُولُ فِي هَذَا الرَّجُلِ؟ فَيَقُولُ: مَا كَانَ يَقُولُ فِيهِ هُوَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ وَرَسُولُهُ، أَشْهَدُ أَنْ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ وَأَشْهَدُ أَنَّ مُحَمَّدًا عَبْدُهُ وَرَسُولُهُ، فَيَقُولَانِ: قَدْ كُنَّا نَعْلَمُ أَنَّكَ تَقُولُ هَذَا، ثُمَّ يُفْسَحُ لَهُ فِي قَبْرِهِ سَبْعُونَ ذِرَاعًا فِي سَبْعِينَ، ثُمَّ يُنَوَّرُ لَهُ فِيهِ، ثُمَّ يُقَالُ لَهُ: نَمْ، فَيَقُولُ: حَتَّى أَرْجِعَ إِلَى أَهْلِي فَأُخْبِرَهُم، فَيَقُولَانِ: نَمْ كَتَوْمَةِ الْعَرُوسِ لَا يُوقِظُهُ إِلَّا أَحَبُّ أَهْلِهِ مِنْهَا، فَيَنَامُ حَتَّى يَبْعَثَهُ اللَّهُ مِنْ مَضْجَعِهِ ذَلِكَ. وَإِنْ كَانَ مُنَافِقًا قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ النَّاسَ يَقُولُونَ شَيْئًا فَقُلْتُ مِثْلَهُ لَا أَدْرِي، فَيَقُولَانِ: قَدْ كُنَّا نَعْلَمُ أَنَّكَ تَقُولُ ذَلِكَ، فَيُقَالُ لِلْأَرْضِ الْتَئِمِي عَلَيْهِ فَتَلْتَئِمُ عَلَيْهِ فَتَخْتَلِفُ أَضْلَاعُهُ، فَلَا يَزَالُ فِيهَا مُعَذَّبًا حَتَّى يَبْعَثَهُ اللَّهُ مِنْ مَضْجَعِهِ ذَلِكَ». قال الترمذي: حديث حسن غريب. فيسألانه عن ربه ودينه ونبيه على ما جاءت به الأخبار عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وعن الصحابة أجمعين؛ فإن له حكم المرفوع إليه؛ لأنه لا يقال من قبل الرأي. قال اللقاني: السؤال في القبر عن العقائد فقط؛ يقول الملك للميت: من ربك؟ وما دينك؟ وما كنت تقول في هذا الرجل الذي بعث فيكم؟ وفي رواية: ومن أبوك؟ وما قبلتك؟ وفي أخرى الاقتصار على بعض تلك المذكورات، وجمع باختلاف المسئولين أو بأن بعض الرواة اقتصر وبعضهم أتم. اهـ.
And we believe in the questioning of the two angels (Munkar and Nakir) for the deceased absolutely, and it is said: only for the disbeliever. Their being named Munkar and Nakir is not in a derogatory sense; rather they are titles, and there is no ugliness or beauty in names and essences per se. The common understanding is that they are two, but in Hilyat Abi Nu'aym there are three: Munkar, Nakir, and Nakur. And al-Iraqi reported that the two angels of the believer are Mubashshir and Bashir, as mentioned by al-Mulla Ilyas. And his statement: 'in his grave' is according to the norm, otherwise for one whom beasts have eaten, whom fire has burnt, or who was not buried, they come to him from wherever Allah wills and question him as Allah knows. It seems the author followed the apparent meaning of the hadith. So in al-Tirmidhi from Abu Hurayra marfu'an: 'When the deceased—or one of you—is buried, there come to him two black angels with blue eyes, one called Munkar and the other Nakir. They say: "What did you used to say about this man?" He says: "What he used to say about him: He is the servant of Allah and His Messenger; I testify that there is no god but Allah and I testify that Muhammad is His servant and Messenger." They say: "We knew you would say that." Then his grave is widened for him seventy cubits by seventy, then it is illuminated for him, then it is said to him: "Sleep." He says: "Let me return to my family to inform them." They say: "Sleep like the sleep of a bride, whom none awakens except the most beloved of her family." So he sleeps until Allah resurrects him from that resting place. But if he is a hypocrite, he says: "I heard the people saying something so I said the like of it; I don't know." They say: "We knew you would say that." Then it is said to the earth: "Close in on him," so it closes in on him, and his ribs become interlocked, and he remains in it being punished until Allah resurrects him from that resting place.' Al-Tirmidhi said: a hasan gharib hadith. So they ask him about his Lord, his religion, and his Prophet according to what has come in the reports from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and from the Companions unanimously; for it has the ruling of being marfu' to him, because it is not said from personal opinion. Al-Laqani said: The questioning in the grave is only about creed; the angel says to the deceased: Who is your Lord? What is your religion? What did you used to say about this man who was sent among you? In a narration: And who is your father? What is your direction of prayer? In another narration: they restrict to some of those mentioned, and they are reconciled by the difference of those questioned or by some narrators restricting and others being more complete. End.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage explains the belief in the questioning by the two angels Munkar and Nakir. The author begins by stating that we believe in the questioning for the deceased absolutely, though some say only for the disbeliever. He then clarifies that the names Munkar and Nakir are not derogatory but simply titles, as names and essences have no inherent moral quality. The common knowledge is that there are two angels, but a report mentions three. Al-Iraqi adds that the believer's angels are Mubashshir and Bashir. The author addresses the apparent limitation to those buried in graves, explaining that it generally applies to the buried, but for those not buried (eaten, burnt, etc.), the angels come in the manner Allah wills. He then cites the hadith from Tirmidhi describing the detailed encounter: two black-blue angels question the deceased about the Prophet. The believer responds correctly, leading to easing and light in the grave, while the hypocrite's response leads to the earth constricting. The author notes that this hadith is hasan gharib. He then states that the questioning includes three matters: Lord, religion, and Prophet, based on reports. Al-Laqani specifies that the questioning is only about creed, listing the questions: Who is your Lord? What is your religion? What do you say about this man? Other narrations add father and qibla. The differences are reconciled by varying the questions according to the person or by different narrators' abridgments.

Key Terms
سؤال الملكين
منكر ونكير
عذاب القبر
فتنة القبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that the names Munkar and Nakir are insults or that the questioning only occurs for those physically buried in graves.
Correction: The names are just titles, and the questioning applies to all deceased, regardless of burial.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the scope of the questioning by Munkar and Nakir?
A) Only for disbelievers
B) For all deceased
C) Only for those buried in graves
D) Only for believers

Key Takeaway
Belief in the questioning of the grave is a fundamental part of Islamic creed, and it applies to all souls, with the angels' names being neutral titles.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly live as if you will be questioned by Munkar and Nakir the moment you die? Or do you let worldly distractions make you forget this reality? What would change in your daily actions if you remembered it constantly?
?
The author clarifies that the names Munkar and Nakir are not insults, but titles. How do you react when you hear something unpleasant? Are you quick to judge based on names or appearances? How can you train yourself to see beyond labels and seek the truth?
?
If the angels come even to those not buried, this shows no one escapes the questioning. Are you prepared for that moment? What have you done today to prepare for the first question: 'Who is your Lord?'

The Hadith of Munkar and Nakir and the Details of the Questioning
Author cites the hadith describing the questioning and then details the creedal questions asked.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the detailed description of the grave questioning from the hadith of Tirmidhi and the specific creedal questions asked.

Core Idea
The questioning in the grave tests one's faith with clear answers about Lord, religion, and Prophet.

This lesson presents the authentic hadith that describes the encounter with Munkar and Nakir, detailing the responses of the believer and the hypocrite. It also clarifies the nature of the questions—only about creed—as specified by later scholars.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith text
Read the hadith from Tirmidhi and witness the difference between the believer's and the hypocrite's responses.
Notice the two angels are described as black with blue eyes.
2
Note the consequences
Observe how the believer's grave is widened and illuminated, while the hypocrite's grave constricts and his ribs interlock.
3
Understand the three core questions
Learn that the questioning is about the Lord, the religion, and the Prophet, as stated after the hadith.
4
See how narrations are reconciled
Understand that different narrations may include additional questions or be abbreviated, and these differences are reconciled by context.
Al-Laqani specifies the questions are only about creed.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the questioning involves trivial matters or that the punishment is only symbolic.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith in Tirmidhi, what is the response of a believer when asked about the Prophet?
A) I testify that he is the servant of Allah and His Messenger
B) I heard people saying something so I said the same
C) I don't know
D) He remains silent

Key Takeaway
The grave questioning is a test of true faith, where firm belief in Allah and His Messenger brings peace, while doubt leads to torment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When the angels ask you about 'this man' – Prophet Muhammad – will your answer come from a lifelong conviction or from merely echoing what you heard others say? What one change can you make today to ensure your answer is certain?
?
The hypocrite said 'I don't know' and faced punishment. In your daily life, are there areas where you act like you don't know – where you avoid committing to the truth of this faith? Name one such area and resolve to seek certainty.
?
If you were to die tonight, would your faith be as clear as the believer's testimony – 'ashhadu alla ilaha illallah wa ashhadu anna Muhammadan abduhu wa rasuluh' – or would there be hesitation? What step will you take this week to remove any doubt?

The Universality of the Grave's Questioning
Clarification and hadith on the grave's questioning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the questioning in the grave by Munkar and Nakir applies to every deceased person, regardless of burial status, and that it focuses on the core beliefs.

Core Idea
The grave's questioning is a universal reality for every soul, not only for the buried.

The Tahawiyyah statement mentions 'in his grave,' but Imam Maydani immediately clarifies that this is a general expression; in reality, everyone faces the questioning, even those not buried conventionally. He then supports this with a detailed hadith from al-Tirmidhi describing the exact process and the two angels, Munkar and Nakir, and concludes with the specific questions about faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the English translation. Notice the author's shift from the general rule to the hadith and back to explanation.
The hadith is lengthy but provides vivid details.
2
Focus on the scope clarification
The author begins by noting that 'in his grave' is the common case, but the questioning also reaches those eaten by beasts, burned, or unburied. Understand that Allah's power makes this possible.
This addresses a common misunderstanding.
3
Analyze the hadith details
The hadith describes the two angels, their appearance, the believer's confident answer, the expansion and light, and the hypocrite's hesitation and crushing. Reflect on the consequences of one's beliefs.
Note the phrase 'We knew you would say this' – it indicates knowledge of the heart.
4
Identify the specific questions
After the hadith, the author cites al-Laqqani to list the exact questions: about Lord, religion, Prophet, and in some narrations, father and qiblah. Understand that these are the core beliefs (aqa'id).
5
Reconcile the variations
The passage mentions different narrations with different sets of questions. The author notes that these differences are due to the condition of the one being questioned or the narrator's scope. See that all narrations are authentic and complementary.

وقوله: (في قبره) جرى على الغالب، وإلا فمن أكلته السباع وأحرقته النار ومن لم يدفن يأتيانه من حيث شاء الله تعالى ويسألانه كما يعلم الله تعالى، وكأن المصنف جرى على ظاهر الحديث؛ ففي الترمذي عن أبي هريرة مرفوعا: «إِذَا قُبِرَ الميت - أو قال : أَحَدُكُمْ - أَتَاهُ مَلَكَانِ أَسْوَدَانِ أَزْرَقَانِ يُقَالُ لِأَحَدِهِمَا: مُنْكَرُ وَالآخَرُ نَكِيرُ وَيَقُولَانِ مَا كُنْتَ تَقُولُ فِي هَذَا الرَّجُلِ فَيَقُولُ مَا كَانَ يَقُولُ فِيهِ هُوَ عَبْد الله وَرَسُولِهِ أَشْهَدُ إِلَّا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ وَأَشْهَدُ أَنَّ مُحَمَّدًا عَبْدُهُ وَرَسُولُهُ فَيَقُولَانِ: قَدْ كُنَّا نَعْلَمُ أَنَّكَ تَقُولُ هَذَا ثُمَّ يُفْسَحُ لَهُ فِي قَبْرِهِ سَبْعُونَ ذِرَاعًا فِي سَبْعِينَ ثُمَّ يُنَوِّرُ لَهُ فِيهِ ثُمَّ يُقَالُ لَهُ نَمْ فَيَقُولُ حَتَّى أَرْجِعَ إِلَى أَهْلِي فَأُخْبِرَهُم فَيَقُولَانِ نَمْ كَتَومَةِ العرُوسِ لَا يُوقِظُهَا إِلَّا أَحَبُّ أَهْلِهَا مِنْهَا فَيَنَامُ حَتَّى يَبْعَتَهُ اللَّهُ مِنْ مَضْجَعِهِ ذَلِكَ وَإِنْ كَانَ مُنَافِقًا قَالَ سَمِعْتُ النَّاسَ يَقُولُونَ شَيْئًا فَقُلْتُ مِثْلَهُ لَا أَدْرِي فَيَقُولَانِ قَدْ كُنَّا نَعْلَمُ أَنَّكَ تَقُولُ ذَلِكَ فَيُقَالُ لِلْأَرْضِ التَّيْمِي عَلَيْهِ فَتَلْتَيْمُ عَلَيهِ فَتَخْتَلِفُ أَضْلاعُهُ فَلَا يَزَالُ فِيهَا مُعَذِّبًا حَتَّى يَبْعَثَهُ اللَّهُ مِنْ مَضْجَعِهِ ذَلِكَ» قال الترمذي: حديث حسن غريب. فیسألانه عن ربه ودينه ونبيه على ما جاءت به الأخبار عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وعن الصحابة أجمعين؛ فإن له حكم المرفوع إليه؛ لأنه لا يقال من قبل الرأي، قال اللقاني: السؤال في القبر عن العقائد فقط؛ يقول الملك للميت: من ربك؟ وما دينك؟ وما كنت تقول في هذا الرجل الذي بعث فيكم؟ وفي رواية ومن أبوك؟ وما قبلتك؟ وفي أخرى الاقتصار على بعض تلك المذكورات وجمع باختلاف المسئولين أو بأن بعض الرواة اقتصر وبعضهم أتم. اهـ.
And his statement: 'in his grave' applies to the majority, otherwise for one whom beasts have eaten, fire has burned, or who was not buried, they come to him from wherever Allah wills and question him as Allah knows. It is as if the author followed the apparent meaning of the hadith; for in al-Tirmidhi from Abu Hurayrah raised: 'When the deceased – or he said: one of you – is buried, two black, blue-eyed angels come to him, one called Munkar and the other Nakir. They say: What did you used to say about this man? So he says: What he used to say about him – he is the slave of Allah and His Messenger. I bear witness that there is no god but Allah and I bear witness that Muhammad is His slave and Messenger. So they say: We knew you would say this. Then his grave is expanded seventy cubits by seventy cubits, then it is illuminated for him, then it is said to him: Sleep. He says: Until I return to my family and inform them. They say: Sleep like the sleep of a bride who is woken only by the most beloved of her family. So he sleeps until Allah resurrects him from that resting place. And if he is a hypocrite, he says: I heard the people saying something and I said the same, I do not know. So they say: We knew you would say that. Then it is said to the earth: Crush him. So it crushes him so that his ribs become dislocated. He continues being punished therein until Allah resurrects him from that resting place.' Al-Tirmidhi said: A hasan gharib hadith. So they question him about his Lord, his religion, and his Prophet, according to what has come in the reports from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and from the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them all; for they have the ruling of being raised to him, because it is not said from personal opinion. Al-Laqqani said: The questioning in the grave is only about the beliefs. The angel says to the deceased: Who is your Lord? What is your religion? What did you used to say about this man who was sent among you? In one narration: And who is your father? And what is your qiblah? In another: limiting to some of those mentioned. And they are reconciled by difference in those questioned or that some narrators limited and others completed. End.
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the Tahawiyyah statement about the questioning in the grave. The author first clarifies that the phrase 'in his grave' is generally applied, but the questioning also applies to those not buried in a conventional grave, such as those eaten by beasts or burned, as Allah can make the angels come to them wherever they are. He then presents the hadith from Tirmidhi describing the questioning by Munkar and Nakir, the response of the believer and the hypocrite, and the resulting expansion or crushing. After the hadith, he notes that the questioning concerns the Lord, religion, and Prophet, as reported in authentic narrations. He cites Al-Laqqani, who states that the questioning is only about beliefs, listing the specific questions and mentioning variations in narrations, which are reconciled by attributing differences to the condition of the one questioned or the scope of the narration.

Key Terms
في قبره
منكر ونكير
سؤال القبر
عقائد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only those buried in a grave are questioned by Munkar and Nakir.
Correction: The author clarifies that the questioning applies to all, including those eaten by beasts, burned, or not buried, as the angels come to them from wherever Allah wills.

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what is the scope of the questioning in the grave for those not buried?
A) They are not questioned at all.
B) The angels come to them from wherever Allah wills.
C) They are only questioned on the Day of Judgment.
D) The questioning applies only to Muslims.

Key Takeaway
The questioning in the grave by Munkar and Nakir is a universal reality that every soul will face, and it centers on the fundamental beliefs of Islam.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you are alone and the angels come to question you, what will your answer be? Will you speak with the certainty of the believer or the doubt of the hypocrite? What are you doing right now to ensure your heart is firm on the testimony of faith?
?
The angels already know what you will say before you speak. Does that terrify you or give you hope? If your inner state does not match your outward words, what change must you make today?
?
You will be questioned about your Lord, your religion, and your Prophet. If you were asked this very moment, would you be able to answer with knowledge and conviction? What step will you take today to prepare for that inevitable moment?

The Grave: A Garden of Paradise or a Pit of Hellfire
Explanation of the grave's two possible states based on faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the grave becomes a garden or a pit based on one's steadfastness in faith or doubt, and its significance as the first stage of the Hereafter.

Core Idea
Your grave is shaped by your faith: steadfastness brings a garden, doubt brings a pit.

The Tahawiyyah creed declares a profound truth about the intermediate state after death. This lesson examines the author's explanation that the grave is not a neutral place but reflects the spiritual state of the believer or disbeliever. Through both creedal statement and prophetic hadith, we learn the decisive role of steadfastness in faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the direct language: the grave 'is' a garden or a pit, not 'may be'.
2
Identify the two states and their condition
The passage states the grave is either a garden or a pit. What determines which? Look for the phrase 'بحسب الثبات والارتياب'.
Steadfastness (ثبات) and doubt (ارتياب) are the decisive factors.
3
Understand the hadith's role
The author supports the statement with a hadith from 'Uthman ibn 'Affan. Read the hadith and note how it emphasizes the grave as the first stage of the Hereafter.
The hadith shows the gravity of the grave's state: if saved here, the rest is easier.
4
Reflect on the lesson's core idea
Ask yourself: Why does steadfastness matter so much? How does this teaching affect your understanding of death and the afterlife?
This connects faith directly to post-death experience.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والقبر بعد ذلك على صاحبه روضة من رياض الجنة أو حفرة من حفر النار بحسب الثبات والارتياب أخرج الترمذي والنسائي والحاكم بسند صحيح عن عثمان بن عفان: إِنَّ القَبْرَ أَوَّلُ مَنْزِلٍ مِنْ مَنَازِلِ الْآخِرَةِ فَإِنْ نَجَا مِنْهُ فَمَا بَعْدَهُ أَيْسَرُ مِنْهُ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَنْجُ مِنْهُ فَمَا بَعْدَهُ أَشَدُّ مِنْهُ.
And the grave after that is for its occupant either a garden from the gardens of Paradise or a pit from the pits of Hellfire, according to [his] steadfastness or doubt. Al-Tirmidhi, al-Nasa'i, and al-Hakim narrated with a sound chain from 'Uthman ibn 'Affan: 'Indeed the grave is the first stage of the stages of the Hereafter. If one is saved from it, what comes after it is easier; and if one is not saved from it, what comes after it is more severe.'
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage is a direct explanation of the Tahawiyyah text stating that the grave is either a garden of Paradise or a pit of Hellfire for its occupant. The author clarifies that this depends on the person's steadfastness in faith or doubt (in religion). He then supports this with a hadith from 'Uthman ibn 'Affan, reported by several authorities with a sound chain, which declares the grave as the first stage of the Hereafter. The hadith emphasizes that if a person is saved from the punishment of the grave, the subsequent stages are easier; if not saved, then what follows is even more severe.

Key Terms
روضة
حفرة
الثبات
الارتياب
أول منزل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the grave's state is predetermined regardless of one's belief.
Correction: It actually depends on the person's steadfastness or doubt in faith, as explicitly stated.

Checkpoint
What determines whether the grave becomes a garden of Paradise or a pit of Hellfire according to this passage?
A) The wealth of the deceased.
B) The number of prayers offered.
C) The person's steadfastness or doubt in faith.
D) The manner of burial.

Key Takeaway
The grave becomes a garden or a pit based on one's steadfastness in faith, and it is the first and decisive stage of the Hereafter.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to die tonight and enter your grave, based on your current level of steadfastness or doubt, would it be a garden or a pit for you? Be honest: what is the state of your heart right now regarding the unseen matters?
?
The hadith says that if you are saved from the grave, the rest of the Hereafter is easier; if not, it is more severe. Does this make you fear the grave or motivate you to strengthen your faith? What specific doubt or uncertainty about Allah's promise are you willing to confront today?
?
Imagine standing at the edge of your grave, knowing that your eternal state begins there. What one change in your daily life would you commit to starting right now to ensure your grave becomes a garden of Paradise?

Life in the Grave: Consensus and Disagreement
Doctrinal note on life in the grave and Imam Abu Hanifa's tawaqquf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the orthodox Sunni consensus on life in the grave and the disagreement regarding the return of the soul, including Imam Abu Hanifa’s position of tawaqquf.

Core Idea
The grave holds a real but limited life for experiencing reward and punishment.

This passage clarifies an important point of Islamic eschatology: while the righteous and wicked experience some form of perception in the grave, scholars debate whether the soul returns to the body. Imam Abu Hanifa’s cautious approach reminds us that some matters are left to Allah’s knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the consensus
The passage begins with what Ahl al-Haqq agree upon: Allah creates a type of life in the grave sufficient for experiencing pain and pleasure. Notice the phrase 'نوع حياة' (a type of life) indicating it is not ordinary life.
2
Note the disagreement
Then it says they differed on whether the soul is returned. Understand that this is a point of legitimate scholarly difference.
3
Learn Imam Abu Hanifa’s view
The transmitted view from Imam Abu Hanifa is tawaqquf (suspension of judgment). Reflect on why he might have refrained from taking a definitive stance.
4
Connect to broader theology
Consider why this matters: it affirms the reality of the grave's reward and punishment while acknowledging limits of human knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن أهل الحق اتفقوا على أن الله تعالى يخلق في الميت نوع حياة في القبر قدر ما يتألم ويلتذ، لكن اختلفوا في أنه هل تعاد الروح إليه أم لا؟ والمنقول عن الإمام أبي حنيفة التوقف.
And know that the people of truth (Ahl al-Haqq) have agreed that Allah the Exalted creates in the deceased a type of life in the grave to the extent that he experiences pain and pleasure, but they differed as to whether the soul is returned to him or not. And what is transmitted from Imam Abu Hanifa is suspension of judgment (tawaqquf).
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage is a concise doctrinal note. The author states a point of consensus among Ahl al-Haqq (the people of truth, i.e., the orthodox Sunni scholars): Allah creates a specific kind of life in the deceased in the grave, sufficient for them to experience pain (punishment) and pleasure (reward). Then he notes a disagreement: whether the soul is actually returned to the body at that time. He ends by mentioning the transmitted position of Imam Abu Hanifa, which is tawaqquf (suspension of judgment), meaning he refrained from taking a definitive stance on this particular issue.

Key Terms
نوع حياة
تألم
التذاذ
إعادة الروح
التوقف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That all Muslims believe the soul is definitely returned to the body in the grave.
Correction: In reality, there is a disagreement, and Imam Abu Hanifa suspended judgment, indicating that this matter is not definitively settled.

Checkpoint
What is the transmitted position of Imam Abu Hanifa regarding the return of the soul in the grave?
A) The soul is definitely returned.
B) The soul is not returned.
C) He suspended judgment (tawaqquf).
D) He denied any life in the grave.

Key Takeaway
The orthodox Sunni position affirms a real but limited life in the grave for experiencing reward and punishment, while the return of the soul remains a point of scholarly difference, with Imam Abu Hanifa adopting tawaqquf.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just learned that the grave holds real pleasure and pain. Which specific actions you perform today do you believe will bring you pleasure in the grave tomorrow? Is that belief strong enough to change how you act right now?
?
Imam Abu Hanifa suspended judgment on the return of the soul because the texts were not explicit. Is there an area of your faith where you demand more certainty than Allah has given? Can you accept tawaqquf on matters beyond your knowledge, or does that unsettle you?
?
If you truly believed that right now, in your grave, you could be tasting pleasure or pain based on your deeds this very moment, what would you do differently before you sleep tonight?

The Grave: A Garden or Pit of Hellfire
Commentary on the Tahawiyyah's statement about the grave's reality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic belief about the grave as either a garden of Paradise or a pit of Hellfire, and the scholarly discussion regarding the nature of life in the grave.

Core Idea
The grave is the first stage of the Hereafter, experienced physically through a life created by Allah.

This lesson explores a central tenet of Ahl al-Sunnah: the reality of the grave as a foretaste of Paradise or Hellfire. We will examine a hadith from Uthman ibn Affan and the consensus on Allah creating a type of life in the deceased, while noting the tawaqquf of Imam Abu Hanifah on the return of the soul.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation to understand the literal meaning.
Pay attention to the phrase 'بحسب الثبات والارتياب'.
2
Understand the hadith on the grave
The hadith from Uthman ibn Affan emphasizes the grave as the first stage of the Hereafter. Consider why the author includes this hadith.
3
Analyze the scholarly agreement and difference
The passage states that the people of truth agree that Allah creates a type of life in the deceased to experience pain or pleasure. Then it mentions the difference on whether the soul returns. Note Imam Abu Hanifah's position of tawaqquf.
4
Reflect on the implications
Think about how this belief affects a Muslim's perspective on death and the afterlife.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(والقبر) بعد ذلك على صاحبه (روضة من رياض الجنة أو حفرة من حفر النار) بحسب الثبات والارتياب. أخرج الترمذي والنسائي والحاكم بسند صحيح عن عثمان بن عفان: إن القبر أول منزل من منازل الآخرة، فإن نجا منه فما بعده أيسر منه، وإن لم ينج منه فما بعده أشد منه. واعلم أن أهل الحق اتفقوا على أن الله تعالى يخلق في الميت نوع حياة في القبر قدر ما يتألم ويلتذ، لكن اختلفوا في أنه هل تعاد الروح إليه أم لا؟ والمنقول عن الإمام أبي حنيفة التوقف.
('And the grave') after that for its occupant is ('a garden from the gardens of Paradise or a pit from the pits of Hellfire') according to [his] steadfastness or doubt. At-Tirmidhi, An-Nasa'i, and Al-Hakim narrated with a sound chain from 'Uthman ibn 'Affan: 'Indeed the grave is the first stage of the stages of the Hereafter; if one is saved from it, what comes after it is easier than it, and if one is not saved from it, what comes after it is harder than it.' And know that the people of truth have agreed that Allah the Exalted creates in the deceased a type of life in the grave to the extent that he feels pain and pleasure, but they differed as to whether the soul is returned to him or not. And what is transmitted from Imam Abu Hanifah is that he withheld [from giving a definitive answer].
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage explains the Tahawiyyah's statement regarding the grave. It begins by quoting the Tahawiyyah: 'And the grave after that for its occupant is either a garden from the gardens of Paradise or a pit from the pits of Hellfire, according to [his] steadfastness or doubt.' The commentator then provides a hadith from Uthman ibn Affan to stress the gravity of the grave as the first stage of the Hereafter. He then explains that the people of truth agree that Allah creates a type of life in the deceased to experience pain or pleasure, but there is a difference of opinion on the return of the soul. The transmitted position of Imam Abu Hanifah is that he withheld from a definitive answer (tawaqquf).

Key Terms
القبر
الروضة
الحفرة
التوقف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The grave experience is purely spiritual and does not involve physical sensations.
Correction: The passage affirms that Allah creates a type of life in the deceased to the extent that they feel pain and pleasure, indicating a physical dimension to the grave's experience.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the transmitted position of Imam Abu Hanifah regarding the return of the soul to the deceased in the grave?
A) He affirmed it.
B) He denied it.
C) He withheld from giving a definitive answer (tawaqquf).
D) He considered it metaphorical.

Key Takeaway
The grave is a real and consequential stage of the afterlife, where the deceased experiences a foretaste of Paradise or Hellfire through a life created by Allah, though the return of the soul remains a matter of scholarly caution.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The hadith says if saved from the grave, what comes after is easier. Does this motivate you to prepare for the grave more than for anything else? If not, what is holding you back?
?
The scholars agree that Allah creates a life in the grave to feel pain or pleasure. If you were to experience the grave right now, based on your deeds, would you feel more anticipation or dread? What will you change today?

The Resurrection: Definition and Qur'anic Proofs
Definition of resurrection and citation of Qur'anic verses as proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic definition of resurrection as bodily resurrection with original parts and souls, and the extensive Qur'anic evidence for it.

Core Idea
Resurrection is bodily and proven by numerous clear Qur'anic verses.

This lesson unpacks the first part of the Tahawiyyah's creed on resurrection: what it means and how the Qur'an establishes it beyond doubt. We will see that the resurrection involves the return of both the original physical parts and the soul, and that the Qur'anic verses on this are abundant and unambiguous.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition carefully
Read the Arabic definition of resurrection: it includes the return of all servants with their original parts and the return of souls to them, then gathering for judgment. Note the precision.
The original parts are those that remain from birth to death.
2
Identify the three components
The resurrection involves: (1) returning original body parts, (2) returning souls to them, and (3) driving them to the gathering place. Notice that all three are essential.
3
Review the Qur'anic verses
Read each of the six verses cited. They all affirm bodily resurrection explicitly. The passage says most of these verses cannot be interpreted metaphorically.
Verses include: Ya-Seen 78, Ya-Seen 51, al-Isra' 51, al-Qiyamah 3-4, Qaf 44, al-A'raf 29.
4
Reflect on the number of verses
The passage states that verses on resurrection are nearly as numerous as verses of legal rulings (ayaat al-ahkaam). This shows the importance of the topic.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونؤمن بالبعث) لجميع العباد، ويعيدهم بجميع أجزائهم الأصلية، وهي التي من شأنها البقاء من أول العمر إلى آخره، ويعيد الأرواح إليها ويسوقهم إلى محشرهم لفصل القضاء بينهم، وهذا كله ثابت بالكتاب والسنة أما الكتاب فقد ورد فيه من الآيات الدالة عليه ما يقارب في الكثرة آيات الأحكام، وأكثرها لا يحتمل التأويل؛ مثل قوله تعالى: (قَالَ مَن يُحْيِ الْعِظَمَ وَهِيَ رَمِيمٌ قُلْ يُحْيِيهَا الَّذِى أَنشَأَهَا أَوَّلَ مَرَّة ) [سورة يس آية: ۷۸] وقوله: فَإِذَا هُم مِّنَ الأَجْدَاثِ إِلَى رَبِّهِمْ يَسِلُونَ [سورة يس آية: ٥١] وقوله: فَسَيَقُولُونَ مَن يُعِيدُنَا قُلِ الَّذِي فَطَرَكُمْ أَوَّلَ مَرَّةٍ) [سورة الإسراء آية: ٥١] وقوله: ا تحسب الإنسَنُ أَلَّن تَجْمَعَ عِظَامَهُ بَلَى قَدِرِينَ عَلَى أَن نَسَوَى بَنَانَهُ ﴾ [سورة القيامة آية: ٣) وقوله: ﴿يَوْمَ تَشَقَّى الْأَرْضُ عَنْهُمْ سِرَاعًا ذَلِكَ حَشْرُ عَلَيْنَا يَسِمٌ (سورة ق آية : ٤٤] وقوله: كَمَا بَدَأَكُمْ تَعُودُونَ ﴾ [سورة الأعراف آية: ٢٩]. وأما السنة فقد ورد في ذلك ما يبلغ جملته مبلغ التواتر المعنوي. ولا شك الآن أن الحشر صار من ضروريات الدين؛ فإنكاره كفر بيقين. كذا ذكره اللقاني.
('We believe in the resurrection') of all servants, and He will return them with all their original parts—those which are meant to remain from the beginning of life until its end—and He will return the souls to them and drive them to their gathering-place for the final judgment. All this is established by the Book and the Sunnah. As for the Book, there are in it verses indicating it that are nearly as numerous as the verses of rulings, and most of them do not admit of interpretation; such as His saying: 'Who will give life to bones when they are decayed?' Say: 'He will give them life who produced them the first time...' and His saying: 'Then behold, they will come out of the graves, hastening to their Lord,' and His saying: 'So they will say, "Who will return us?" Say: "He who created you the first time,"' and His saying: 'Does man think that We will not assemble his bones? Yes, We are able to proportion his fingertips,' and His saying: 'On the Day when the earth is split from them in haste—that is a gathering easy for Us,' and His saying: 'As He began you, you will return.' As for the Sunnah, there has come regarding that what in its totality reaches the level of mass transmission (tawatur ma'nawi). There is no doubt now that the resurrection (al-hashr) has become a necessary matter of religion (daruriyyat al-din); denying it is certain disbelief. Thus mentioned al-Laqani.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage comments on the Tahawiyyah's affirmation of resurrection (ba'th). It first defines resurrection as Allah returning all servants with their original parts and returning the souls to them, then gathering them for judgment. It then presents the evidence: the Quran, citing several verses that clearly affirm bodily resurrection without allowing metaphorical interpretation, and the Sunnah, which through multiple chains reaches the level of mass transmission (tawatur ma'nawi). The passage concludes that belief in resurrection is a necessary part of Islam (daruriyyat al-din) and that denying it is clear disbelief, citing al-Laqani.

Sunnah Proof and the Necessity of Belief
Evidence from Sunnah through tawatur and ruling that denial is disbelief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Sunnah confirms resurrection through mass transmission (tawatur) and that denying it is clear disbelief (kufr).

Core Idea
Denial of resurrection is disbelief because it is a necessary matter of religion.

This lesson completes the evidence for resurrection by turning to the Sunnah, which reaches the level of mass transmission, making the belief undeniable. The passage then concludes that resurrection is a necessary part of Islam, and rejecting it is outright disbelief.

Guided Path
1
Read the Sunnah evidence
The passage states that the traditions on resurrection collectively reach tawatur ma'nawi (mass transmission of meaning). This means so many reports exist that certainty is achieved.
Tawatur means multiple independent chains of transmission that cannot be fabricated.
2
Understand the consequence
Because the evidence is so strong, belief in resurrection has become a necessary matter of religion (daruriyyat al-din). This means it is part of the basic, essential beliefs of Islam.
3
Grasp the ruling on denial
Denying resurrection is kufr (disbelief) without any doubt. The passage says 'fainkarahu kufr bi-yaqeen'.
Al-Laqani is cited as the source of this statement.

Belief in the Events of the Day of Judgment
Commentary on Tahawiyyah's list of eschatological events.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific events of the Day of Judgment that Muslims must believe in, as affirmed by the Tahawiyyah and supported by revelation.

Core Idea
The events of the Day of Judgment are literal, not symbolic, and are proven by Quran and Hadith.

The Tahawiyyah creed includes a detailed list of events that will occur on the Day of Judgment. This passage explains the first few: recompense of deeds, presentation, reckoning, and the reading of the book of deeds. It then cites a Quranic verse and the beginning of a prophetic hadith to affirm these realities. Understanding these beliefs is essential for correct eschatological faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the commentary explains each term briefly and then provides scriptural evidence.
The passage is part of a larger commentary; focus on the items explicitly mentioned.
2
Identify the listed events
The passage mentions four events: recompense of deeds, presentation, reckoning, and reading of the book. Note that 'reading of the book' is explained as the book of one's deeds.
Later parts (reward, punishment, bridge, scales) are mentioned in the commentary but not fully detailed here.
3
Examine the Quranic proof
The passage quotes Quran 17:13 about the book spread open. Reflect on how this verse supports the literal reality of the book of deeds.
4
Begin the hadith proof
The hadith begins: 'Indeed Allah will bring the believer near and place His covering over him and conceal him.' This shows divine mercy during judgment.
The hadith is cut off; later parts describe the believer admitting sins and receiving forgiveness.
5
Consider the common misunderstanding
Some might think these events are spiritual symbols. The passage and its sources affirm they are real, physical, or sensory events.
This is a crucial point of Sunni orthodoxy.

Belief in Resurrection and Its Definition
Author lists afterlife beliefs and defines resurrection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the detailed definition of resurrection as the bodily return of all servants with their original parts and souls for judgment.

Core Idea
Resurrection is the bodily return of all servants with their original parts for final judgment.

The author begins by affirming belief in all the major events of the afterlife, then focuses on resurrection. He provides a precise definition that clarifies exactly what we believe about the return of the dead. Let's read the passage and unpack its meaning.

Guided Path
1
Read the creedal statement
Read the opening list of afterlife events and note the sequence: resurrection, recompense, presentation, reckoning, etc.
This list establishes the broad framework of eschatological beliefs.
2
Focus on the definition of resurrection
The author defines resurrection as the return of all servants with their original parts and souls, leading to the gathering for judgment. Identify the key components: original parts, souls, gathering.
Original parts are those that persist from birth to death.
3
Reflect on the significance of 'original parts'
Why does the author specify 'original parts'? This emphasizes the physical, bodily nature of resurrection, countering purely spiritual interpretations.
4
Consider the purpose of resurrection
The ultimate purpose is 'filling the judgment' – the final judgment between all servants.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَنُؤْمِنُ بِالبَعْثِ وَبِجَزَاءِ الأَعْمَالِ يَوْمَ القِيَامَةِ وَالعَرْضِ وَالحِسَابِ وَقِرَاءَةِ الكِتابِ وَالثَّوَابِ وَالعِقَابِ وَالصَّرَاطِ، وَالمِيزَانِ يُوزَنُ بِهِ أَعْمَالُ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ مِنَ الْخَيْرِ وَالشَّرِّ وَالطَّاعَةِ وَالمَعْصِيَةِ. ونؤمن بالبعث) لجميع العباد، ويعيدهم بجميع أجزائهم الأصلية، وهي التي من شأنها البقاء من أول العمر إلى آخره، ويعيد الأرواح إليها ويسوقهم إلى محشرهم لفصل القضاء بينهم، وهذا كله ثابت بالكتاب والسنة أما الكتاب فقد ورد فيه من الآيات الدالة عليه ما يقارب في الكثرة آيات الأحكام، وأكثرها لا يحتمل التأويل؛ مثل قوله تعالى: (قَالَ مَن يُحْيِ الْعِظَمَ وَهِيَ رَمِيمٌ قُلْ يُحْيِيهَا الَّذِى أَنشَأَهَا أَوَّلَ مَرَّة ) [سورة يس آية: ۷۸] وقوله: فَإِذَا هُم مِّنَ الأَجْدَاثِ إِلَى رَبِّهِمْ يَسِلُونَ [سورة يس آية: ٥١] وقوله: فَسَيَقُولُونَ مَن يُعِيدُنَا قُلِ الَّذِي فَطَرَكُمْ أَوَّلَ مَرَّةٍ) [سورة الإسراء آية: ٥١] وقوله: أَيَحْسَبُ الإِنسَانُ أَلَّن تَجْمَعَ عِظَامَهُ بَلَى قَدِرِينَ عَلَى أَن نَسَوَى بَنَانَهُ ﴾ [سورة القيامة آية: ٣) وقوله: ﴿يَوْمَ تَشَقَّى الْأَرْضُ عَنْهُمْ سِرَاعًا ذَلِكَ حَشْرُ عَلَيْنَا يَسِيرٌ (سورة ق آية : ٤٤] وقوله: كَمَا بَدَأَكُمْ تَعُودُونَ ﴾ [سورة الأعراف آية: ٢٩]. وأما السنة فقد ورد في ذلك ما يبلغ جملته مبلغ التواتر المعنوي. ولا شك الآن أن الحشر صار من ضروريات الدين؛ فإنكاره كفر بيقين. كذا ذكره اللقاني (١).
And we believe in resurrection and in the recompense of deeds on the Day of Judgment, and the presentation, and the reckoning, and the reading of the book, and reward, and punishment, and the path, and the scale by which the deeds of the believers are weighed, good and evil, obedience and disobedience. And we believe in resurrection for all servants, and He will return them with all their original parts, which are those that persist from the beginning of life to its end, and He will return the souls to them and drive them to their gathering place for the final judgment between them. All of this is established by the Book and the Sunnah. As for the Book, there are verses indicating it that approach in number the verses of rulings, and most of them cannot be interpreted figuratively; such as His saying: 'He said: Who will give life to bones when they are decayed? Say: He will give them life who produced them the first time' [Surah Ya-Sin, verse 78], and His saying: 'Then behold, from the graves they will hasten to their Lord' [Surah Ya-Sin, verse 51], and His saying: 'And they will say: Who will restore us? Say: He who brought you forth the first time' [Surah Al-Isra, verse 51], and His saying: 'Does man think that We will not assemble his bones? Yes, We are able to proportion even his fingertips' [Surah Al-Qiyamah, verses 3-4], and His saying: 'On the day when the earth will be split open from them, hastening; that is a gathering easy for Us' [Surah Qaf, verse 44], and His saying: 'As He began you, you will return' [Surah Al-A'raf, verse 29]. As for the Sunnah, what has been narrated in that regard reaches the level of mutawatir in meaning. And there is no doubt now that the gathering has become a necessity of religion; denying it is certain disbelief. This is what al-Laqqani mentioned (1).
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof of the belief in resurrection. It begins with the creedal statement containing all the articles of belief in the afterlife, then focuses on resurrection. The author defines resurrection as the return of all servants with their original parts and souls to the gathering place for judgment. He asserts that this is established by both the Qur'an and Sunnah. He notes that the Qur'anic verses on resurrection are nearly as numerous as legal verses and are mostly unambiguous. He provides six specific verses as evidence. For the Sunnah, he states that the hadiths collectively reach the level of tawatur manawi (cumulative certainty). He then declares that belief in resurrection has become a daruriyyat al-din (necessary religious knowledge), such that its denial is unequivocally kufr (disbelief), citing al-Laqqani.

الحشر
القيامة

Correction: The passage affirms that Allah returns the dead with all their original physical parts and reunites souls to bodies.

Checkpoint

A) The bones only
B) The parts that persist from beginning to end of life
C) Only the souls

Key Takeaway
Resurrection involves the bodily return of every person with their original parts and soul for judgment.

?

Proofs of Resurrection and Its Necessity
Author provides proofs from Quran and Sunnah for resurrection and states its status.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that resurrection is proven by abundant Quranic verses and mutawatir hadith, and that denying it is disbelief.

Core Idea
Resurrection is proven by overwhelming evidence and is a necessary belief.

After defining resurrection, the author now proves its truth from the Quran and Sunnah. He cites six clear Quranic verses and states that the hadiths reach the level of tawatur manawi. He concludes that belief in resurrection is a necessary part of Islam, making its denial clear disbelief. Let's examine the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the claim about Quranic verses
Read the author's assertion that verses on resurrection are nearly as numerous as legal verses and mostly unambiguous.
2
Examine the six cited verses
Look at each verse and notice how they answer the skeptics' questions about bringing bones back to life.
These verses are from Surah Ya-Sin, Al-Isra, Al-Qiyamah, Qaf, and Al-A'raf.
3
Understand the Sunnah evidence
The author says the hadiths reach tawatur manawi – a level of mass transmission that yields certainty.
Tawatur manawi means many reports convey the same meaning even if wording differs.
4
Grasp the conclusion
The author declares that resurrection is a daruriyyah (necessity) of religion and denial is kufr.
This is a very strong statement indicating the centrality of this belief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَنُؤْمِنُ بِالبَعْثِ وَبِجَزَاءِ الأَعْمَالِ يَوْمَ القِيَامَةِ وَالعَرْضِ وَالحِسَابِ وَقِرَاءَةِ الكِتابِ وَالثَّوَابِ وَالعِقَابِ وَالصَّرَاطِ، وَالمِيزَانِ يُوزَنُ بِهِ أَعْمَالُ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ مِنَ الْخَيْرِ وَالشَّرِّ وَالطَّاعَةِ وَالمَعْصِيَةِ. ونؤمن بالبعث) لجميع العباد، ويعيدهم بجميع أجزائهم الأصلية، وهي التي من شأنها البقاء من أول العمر إلى آخره، ويعيد الأرواح إليها ويسوقهم إلى محشرهم لفصل القضاء بينهم، وهذا كله ثابت بالكتاب والسنة أما الكتاب فقد ورد فيه من الآيات الدالة عليه ما يقارب في الكثرة آيات الأحكام، وأكثرها لا يحتمل التأويل؛ مثل قوله تعالى: (قَالَ مَن يُحْيِ الْعِظَمَ وَهِيَ رَمِيمٌ قُلْ يُحْيِيهَا الَّذِى أَنشَأَهَا أَوَّلَ مَرَّة ) [سورة يس آية: ۷۸] وقوله: فَإِذَا هُم مِّنَ الأَجْدَاثِ إِلَى رَبِّهِمْ يَسِلُونَ [سورة يس آية: ٥١] وقوله: فَسَيَقُولُونَ مَن يُعِيدُنَا قُلِ الَّذِي فَطَرَكُمْ أَوَّلَ مَرَّةٍ) [سورة الإسراء آية: ٥١] وقوله: أَيَحْسَبُ الإِنسَانُ أَلَّن تَجْمَعَ عِظَامَهُ بَلَى قَدِرِينَ عَلَى أَن نَسَوَى بَنَانَهُ ﴾ [سورة القيامة آية: ٣) وقوله: ﴿يَوْمَ تَشَقَّى الْأَرْضُ عَنْهُمْ سِرَاعًا ذَلِكَ حَشْرُ عَلَيْنَا يَسِيرٌ (سورة ق آية : ٤٤] وقوله: كَمَا بَدَأَكُمْ تَعُودُونَ ﴾ [سورة الأعراف آية: ٢٩]. وأما السنة فقد ورد في ذلك ما يبلغ جملته مبلغ التواتر المعنوي. ولا شك الآن أن الحشر صار من ضروريات الدين؛ فإنكاره كفر بيقين. كذا ذكره اللقاني (١).
And we believe in resurrection and in the recompense of deeds on the Day of Judgment, and the presentation, and the reckoning, and the reading of the book, and reward, and punishment, and the path, and the scale by which the deeds of the believers are weighed, good and evil, obedience and disobedience. And we believe in resurrection for all servants, and He will return them with all their original parts, which are those that persist from the beginning of life to its end, and He will return the souls to them and drive them to their gathering place for the final judgment between them. All of this is established by the Book and the Sunnah. As for the Book, there are verses indicating it that approach in number the verses of rulings, and most of them cannot be interpreted figuratively; such as His saying: 'He said: Who will give life to bones when they are decayed? Say: He will give them life who produced them the first time' [Surah Ya-Sin, verse 78], and His saying: 'Then behold, from the graves they will hasten to their Lord' [Surah Ya-Sin, verse 51], and His saying: 'And they will say: Who will restore us? Say: He who brought you forth the first time' [Surah Al-Isra, verse 51], and His saying: 'Does man think that We will not assemble his bones? Yes, We are able to proportion even his fingertips' [Surah Al-Qiyamah, verses 3-4], and His saying: 'On the day when the earth will be split open from them, hastening; that is a gathering easy for Us' [Surah Qaf, verse 44], and His saying: 'As He began you, you will return' [Surah Al-A'raf, verse 29]. As for the Sunnah, what has been narrated in that regard reaches the level of mutawatir in meaning. And there is no doubt now that the gathering has become a necessity of religion; denying it is certain disbelief. This is what al-Laqqani mentioned (1).
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof of the belief in resurrection. It begins with the creedal statement containing all the articles of belief in the afterlife, then focuses on resurrection. The author defines resurrection as the return of all servants with their original parts and souls to the gathering place for judgment. He asserts that this is established by both the Qur'an and Sunnah. He notes that the Qur'anic verses on resurrection are nearly as numerous as legal verses and are mostly unambiguous. He provides six specific verses as evidence. For the Sunnah, he states that the hadiths collectively reach the level of tawatur manawi (cumulative certainty). He then declares that belief in resurrection has become a daruriyyat al-din (necessary religious knowledge), such that its denial is unequivocally kufr (disbelief), citing al-Laqqani.

Key Terms
التواتر المعنوي
ضروريات الدين
كفر

Correction: The author shows that resurrection is proven by an abundance of clear Quranic verses and mutawatir hadith, making it a certain belief.

Belief in Presentation, Reckoning, and the Book of Deeds
Author affirms belief in presentation, reckoning, reading the book, and cites a hadith contrasting believer and hypocrite.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic belief in the presentation of deeds, the reckoning, and the reading of the book on the Day of Judgment, and how the believer is treated with mercy while the hypocrite is publicly shamed.

Core Idea
On Judgment Day, the believer's sins are concealed and forgiven, while the hypocrite's lies are exposed.

This passage from the Tahawiyyah affirms belief in the recompense of deeds and the specific events of presentation, reckoning, and reading the book. It begins with a Quranic verse describing the book being spread open, and then a profound hadith that contrasts the private mercy shown to the believer with the public humiliation of the hypocrite. Let's read the source and unpack its meaning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to get the overall meaning.
2
Identify the key elements
Notice the three elements: recompense, presentation, reckoning, plus the reading of the book. Then see the hadith's two parts: the believer's treatment and the hypocrite's.
3
Understand the theological implication
Reflect on why the believer's sins are concealed and forgiven, while the hypocrite's are exposed. This shows Allah's mercy and justice.

(و) نؤمن (بجزاء الأعمال يوم القيامة والعرض والحساب وقراءة الكتاب أي كتاب عمله؛ كما قال تعالى: (وَتُخْرِجُ لَهُ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ كِتَابًا يَلْقَهُ مَنشُورًا سورة الإسراء آية: ١٣]، وعنه : (إِنَّ اللهَ يُدْنِي المُؤْمِنَ فَيَضَعُ كَنَفَهُ وَيَسْتُرُهُ فَيَقُولُ أَتَعْرِفُ ذَنْبَ كَذَا فَيَقُولُ نَعَمْ أَيْ رَبِّ حَتَّى إِذَا قَرَّرَهُ بِذُنُوبِهِ وَرَأَى فِي نَفْسِهِ أَنَّهُ قَدْ هَلَكَ قَالَ سَتَرْتُهَا عَلَيْكَ فِي الدُّنْيَا وَأَنَا أَغْفِرُهَا لَكَ اليَومَ فَيُعْطَى كِتَابَ حَسَنَاتِهِ وَأَمَّا الكُفَّارُ وَالمُنَافِقُونَ فَيُنَادَى بِهِم عَلَى رُءُوسِ الخَلَائِقِ هَؤُلَاءِ الَّذِينَ كَذَّبُوا عَلَى رَبِّهِم أَلَا لَعْنَةُ الله عَلَى الظَّالِمِينَ) (١).

He will say: Yes, my Lord. Until when He has confronted him with his sins and he sees in himself that he is destroyed, He will say: I concealed them for you in the world and I forgive them for you today. Then he will be given his book of good deeds. As for the disbelievers and hypocrites, they will be called out before the heads of creation: These are the ones who lied against their Lord; indeed the curse of Allah is upon the wrongdoers.' (1)
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of belief in the recompense of deeds, presentation, reckoning, and reading of the book. It first quotes the Quranic verse about the book of deeds being spread open. Then it cites a hadith describing the treatment of the believer: Allah brings him close, covers him, and asks about his sins; when the believer confesses, Allah reveals that He had concealed those sins in the world and now forgives them, then gives him his book of good deeds. In contrast, the disbelievers and hypocrites are publicly shamed and cursed. This illustrates the mercy for believers and justice for others.

Belief in Reward and Punishment
A creedal affirmation of reward and punishment based on divine promise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that reward and punishment in Islam are based on Allah's promise and threat, ensuring they are just and certain.

Core Idea
Reward and punishment are anchored to Allah's word, not human whims.

This lesson examines a concise creedal statement from Imam Tahawi. The author affirms belief in divine reward for the obedient and punishment for the disobedient, both tied to Allah's explicit promise and threat. This simple yet profound statement establishes the basis for eschatological justice.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then its English translation. Notice the brevity and the direct affirmation.
2
Identify the key components
Identify the four main elements: reward, punishment, obedient, disobedient. Also note the connecting phrase 'according to His promise and threat'.
3
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: why does the author tie reward and punishment specifically to Allah's promise and threat? What does this imply about the nature of divine justice?
This step connects to the core idea.

Source Text

(و) نؤمن بـ (الثواب) للمطيع (والعقاب) للعاصي حسب وعده ووعيده
And we believe in reward for the obedient and punishment for the disobedient according to His promise and threat.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a concise creedal statement affirming belief in divine reward and punishment. It specifies that reward is for the obedient (al-muti‘) and punishment for the disobedient (al-‘asi). Both are according to Allah's promise (wa‘d) and threat (wa‘id), emphasizing that they are not arbitrary but based on His decree.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

Are you willing to let Allah's word alone define what you deserve, even when your own heart disagrees? What would it take for you to submit to that standard completely?

Belief in the Bridge (الصراط)
The author describes the Bridge as a real entity and relates a prophetic parable explaining it as Islam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Bridge (al-Sirat) is a real entity in the afterlife and that the prophetic parable interprets the path as Islam, linking one's worldly faith to successful crossing.

Core Idea
The Bridge is real: your Islam in this world is your path across it.

This lesson presents the Islamic creed regarding al-Sirat, the Bridge over Hell. The author affirms its reality and then relates a profound prophetic parable that identifies the straight path as Islam itself. Through this parable, we learn how our conduct in this world directly determines our crossing on the Day of Judgment.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its literal translation carefully. Notice the concise style and the shift from direct statement to prophetic narration.
2
Identify the three descriptions of the Bridge
The passage describes the Bridge as a bridge over Hell, sharper than a sword, and finer than a hair. Write down these three attributes.
These descriptions emphasize its terrifying precision.
3
Understand the prophetic parable
Visualize the parable: a straight path with two walls, open doors with lowered curtains, a caller at the head urging straightness, and a caller above warning against entering the doors.
This parable is attributed to the Prophet ﷺ via Ghazali and Mullah Ilyas.
4
Learn the interpretation of each element
The author interprets each symbolic element: the path is Islam, the doors are Allah's prohibitions, the curtains are His limits, the caller at the head is the Quran, and the caller above is the inner admonisher.
Use the guided breakdown below to memorize these correspondences.
5
Reflect on the connection between worldly Islam and afterlife crossing
The conclusion states that whoever does not follow Islam in this world will not cross the Bridge in the afterlife. Consider how this challenges a purely metaphorical understanding of the Bridge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(والصراط) أنه حق، وهو جسر ممدود على متن جهنم أَحَدُّ من السيف وأدق من الشعر " كذا في عقيدة الإمام الغزالي (٢) ، قال شارحها العلامة المنلا إلياس قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: ضَرَبَ اللهُ مَثَلًا صِرَاطًا مُسْتَقِيمَا وَعَنْ جَنْبي الصِّرَاطِ سُورَانِ فيهِمَا أَبْوَابٌ مُفَتَّحَةٌ وَعَلَى الأَبْوَابِ سُتُورٌ مُرْخَاةٌ وَعِنْدَ رَأْسِ الصِّرَاطِ دَاعِ يَقُولُ اسْتَقِيمُوا عَلَى الصِّرَاطِ جَمِيعًا وَلَا تَعْوَجُوا - وفي لفظ: يَا أَيُّهَا النَّاسُ ادْخُلُوا الصِّرَاطَ جَمِيعًا وَلَا تَعْوَجُوا وَفَوقَ ذَلِكَ دَاعِ يَدْعُو كُلَّمَا هَمَّ عَبْدٌ أَنْ يَفْتَحَ شَيْئًا مِنْ تِلْكَ الأَبْوَابِ قَالَ وَيْحَكَ لَا تَفْتَحْهُ فَإِنَّكَ إِنْ تُفْتَحْهُ تَلِجْهُ (۳)، ثم فسره فأخبر أن الصراط هو الإسلام، وأن الأبواب المفتحة محارم الله، وأن الستور المرخاة حدود الله، وأن الداعي على رأس الصراط هو القرآن، وأن الداعي من فوقه هو واعظ الله في قلب كل مؤمن؛ فإذا كان الصراط هو الإسلام فمن لا إسلام له لم يدخل الصراط في الدنيا؛ فلا سلكه يوم القيامة إذا صار محسوسا.
And the path: it is true, and it is a bridge stretched over the surface of Hell, sharper than a sword and finer than a hair. As stated in the creed of Imam al-Ghazali (2), its commentator, the scholar Mullah Ilyas, said: The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'Allah made a parable of a straight path, and flanking the path are two walls with open doors, and over the doors are lowered curtains, and at the head of the path is a caller saying: Keep straight on the path, all of you, and do not deviate. In another wording: O people, enter the path all together and do not deviate. And above that is a caller who calls out; whenever a servant intends to open something from those doors, he says: Woe to you, do not open it, for if you open it you will enter it.' (3) Then he interpreted it and informed that the path is Islam, the open doors are the prohibitions of Allah, the lowered curtains are the limits of Allah, the caller at the head of the path is the Qur'an, and the caller above is the admonisher of Allah in the heart of every believer. So if the path is Islam, then whoever has no Islam did not enter the path in this world; thus he will not traverse it on the Day of Judgment when it becomes perceptible.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage defines and explains belief in al-Sirat (the Bridge). It begins by affirming that the Bridge is real (haqq) and describes it as a bridge stretched over Hell, sharper than a sword and finer than a hair, quoting al-Ghazali. Then it relates a prophetic parable: a straight road with walls, open doors with curtains, a caller at the head urging straightness, and a caller above warning against entering the doors. The interpretation is given: the road is Islam, the doors are Allah's prohibitions, the curtains are His limits, the caller at the head is the Qur'an, and the caller above is the inner divine admonisher in every believer's heart. The conclusion is that whoever does not follow Islam in this world (i.e., did not enter the path of Islam) will not cross the Bridge in the afterlife when it becomes a tangible reality.

الجسر

الإسلام

القرآن
واعظ الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think the Bridge is merely a metaphor or symbol, not a real physical entity.
Correction: This passage affirms the Bridge is a true (haqq) reality and describes it in concrete terms (bridge over Hell, sharper than a sword, finer than a hair), emphasizing its physical existence in the afterlife.

B) Islam
C) The prohibitions of Allah

Key Takeaway

The Believer's Forgiveness on the Day of Judgment
Hadith describing the forgiveness of a believer's sins on Judgement Day.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Allah forgives the believer's sins on the Day of Judgment after having concealed them in the world.

Core Idea
God's forgiveness is preceded by concealment in this world.

This hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him) describes the intimate moment when a believer is confronted with his sins. Instead of punishment, the believer experiences God's mercy as his sins are forgiven and he is given his book of good deeds. This lesson explores that scene.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice the dialogue between God and the believer.
The passage is concise; observe every phrase.
2
Identify the key elements
Identify the sin acknowledgment, the believer's despair, and God's response of forgiveness and concealment.
3
Reflect on the concealment
Think about the meaning of God covering sins in the world. How does this relate to His mercy?
This concealment is a form of divine grace.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَيَقُولُ أَتَعْرِفُ ذَنْبَ كَذَا فَيَقُولُ نَعَمْ أَيْ رَبِّ حَتَّى إِذَا قَتَرَهُ بِذُنُوبِهِ وَرَأَى فِي نَفْسِهِ أَنَّهُ قَدْ هَلَكَ قَالَ سَنَرْتُها عَلَيْكَ فِي الدُّنْيَا وَأَنَا أَغْفِرُهَا لَكَ اليَومَ فَيُعْطَى كِتَابَ حَسَنَاتِهِ وَأَمَّا الكُفَّارُ وَالمُنَافِقُونَ فَيُنَادَى بِهِم عَلَى رُءُوسِ الخَلَائِقِ هَؤُلَاءِ الَّذِينَ كَذَّبُوا عَلَى رَبِّهِم أَلَا لَعْنَةُ الله عَلَى الظَّالِمِينَ
He says: 'Do you know such-and-such a sin?' He says: 'Yes, O Lord.' Until when he is weighed down by his sins and sees in himself that he is destroyed, He says: 'I covered it for you in the world and I forgive you for it today.' So he is given his book of good deeds. And as for the disbelievers and the hypocrites, they are proclaimed before the heads of creation: 'These are the ones who lied about their Lord; indeed, the curse of God is upon the wrongdoers.'
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a narration of a hadith (from Bukhari and Muslim) describing the scene of judgment. It first mentions the believer whose sins are reviewed, and when he sees his many sins and fears destruction, God reminds him that He concealed those sins in the world and forgives them today, and then he is given his book of good deeds. In contrast, the disbelievers and hypocrites are publicly shamed before all creation, with the declaration that they lied about their Lord and are cursed. This highlights God's mercy for believers and His justice for disbelievers.

Key Terms
الذنب
الغفران
كتاب الحسنات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that forgiveness on the Day of Judgment only comes after punishment.
Correction: The hadith shows that the believer is forgiven directly after acknowledging his sins, without punishment.

Checkpoint
After the believer acknowledges his sins and feels destroyed, what does God say?
A) 'You are doomed'
B) 'I covered it for you in the world and I forgive you today'
C) 'You will be punished for each sin'
D) 'Your deeds are lost'

Key Takeaway
God forgives the believer's sins on the Day of Judgment because He concealed them in the world.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You know God sees every sin you commit. Why do you still feel safe from exposure? Does this hadith make you reconsider your hope in His concealment—or does it push you to repent before that concealment ends?
?
If God asked you about a sin you hide, would you acknowledge it as the believer did, or would you try to deny it? What does your answer reveal about the state of your faith?
?
The believer felt utterly doomed before forgiveness came. Have you ever felt that weight of your sins? If not, are you truly aware of what you have done? If yes, does this hadith give you real hope—or do you rely on easy forgiveness without genuine remorse?

Hadith describing the public shaming of disbelievers and hypocrites.

Affirming Reward, Punishment, and the Reality of the Sirat
Affirmation of reward, punishment, and the Sirat as a real bridge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the foundational Islamic beliefs in divine reward and punishment according to God's promise, and the reality of the Sirat as a physical bridge over Hellfire.

Core Idea
The Sirat is a real bridge over Hell, sharper than a sword and finer than a hair.

Imam al-Tahawi begins by affirming two essential eschatological truths: that God will reward the obedient and punish the disobedient exactly as He promised and threatened. He then immediately asserts the reality of the Sirat, describing it in vivid terms from the tradition of Imam al-Ghazali. This lesson grounds these beliefs as non-negotiable articles of faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening Arabic passage
Read the lines affirming reward, punishment, and the Sirat. Note the phrasing 'according to His promise and His threat'.
2
Identify the three elements affirmed
The passage affirms (1) reward for the obedient, (2) punishment for the disobedient, and (3) the reality of the Sirat. See how they are connected.
3
Examine the Sirat's description
The Sirat is a bridge over the midst of Hell, sharper than a sword and finer than a hair. Reflect on why these physical descriptions are given.
These descriptions emphasize its difficulty and reality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) نؤمن بـ (الثواب) للمطيع والعقاب للعاصي حسب وعده ووعيده (والصراط) أنه حق، وهو جسر ممدود على متن جهنم أحد من السيف وأدق من الشعر كذا في عقيدة الإمام الغزالي (٢) ، قال شارحها العلامة المنلا إلياس قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: ضَرَبَ اللهُ مَثَلًا صِرَاطًا مُسْتَقِيمَا وَعَنْ جَنْبي الصِّرَاطِ سُورَانِ فيهِمَا أَبْوَابٌ مُفَتَّحَةٌ وَعَلَى الأَبْوَابِ سُتُورٌ مُرْخَاةٌ وَعِنْدَ رَأْسِ الصِّرَاطِ دَاعِ يَقُولُ اسْتَقِيمُوا عَلَى الصِّرَاطِ جَمِيعًا وَلَا تَعْوَجُوا - وفي لفظ: يَا أَيُّهَا النَّاسُ ادْخُلُوا الصِّرَاطَ جَمِيعًا وَلَا تَعْوَجُوا وَفَوقَ ذَلِكَ دَاعِ يَدْعُو كُلَّمَا هَمَّ عَبْدٌ أَنْ يَفْتَحَ شَيْئًا مِنْ تِلْكَ الأَبْوَابِ قَالَ وَيْحَكَ لَا تَفْتَحْهُ فَإِنَّكَ إِنْ تُفْتَحْهُ تَلِجه (۳)، ثم فسره فأخبر أن الصراط هو الإسلام، وأن الأبواب المفتحة محارم الله، وأن الستور المرخاة حدود الله، وأن الداعي على رأس الصراط هو القرآن، وأن الداعي من فوقه هو واعظ الله في قلب كل مؤمن؛ فإذا كان الصراط هو الإسلام فمن لا إسلام له لم يدخل الصراط في الدنيا؛ فلا سلكه يوم القيامة إذا صار محسوسا.
And we believe in reward for the obedient and punishment for the disobedient according to His promise and His threat, and the Path that it is true, and it is a bridge stretched over the middle of Hell, sharper than a sword and finer than a hair. Thus in the creed of Imam al-Ghazali. Its commentator, the scholar al-Mulla Ilyas, said: The Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, said: 'God struck a parable: a straight path, and on the two sides of the path there are two walls with open doors, and on the doors there are lowered curtains, and at the head of the path there is a caller saying: "Keep straight on the path all together and do not deviate." In another wording: "O people, enter the path all together and do not deviate." And above that there is a caller who calls out: whenever a servant intends to open any of those doors, he says: "Woe to you, do not open it, for if you open it you will enter it."' Then he interpreted it and informed that the path is Islam, and that the open doors are the prohibitions of God, and that the lowered curtains are the limits of God, and that the caller at the head of the path is the Quran, and that the caller above him is the admonisher of God in the heart of every believer. So if the path is Islam, then whoever has no Islam did not enter the path in this world, so he will not traverse it on the Day of Resurrection when it becomes perceptible.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage is a statement of faith regarding eschatological realities. The author first affirms belief in reward and punishment according to God's promise and threat. Then he specifically affirms the reality of the Sirat (Bridge), describing it as a bridge stretched over the midst of Hell, sharper than a sword and thinner than a hair, citing Imam al-Ghazali's creed. He then relays a hadith that uses a parable of a straight path with walls, doors, and curtains, and two callers. The commentator al-Mulla Ilyas then interprets the parable: the straight path is Islam, the open doors are God's prohibitions, the lowered curtains are God's limits, the caller at the head of the path is the Quran, and the caller above is the inner divine admonisher in every believer's heart. The key conclusion: since the path is Islam, only those who followed Islam in this world will be able to cross the physical Sirat on the Day of Judgment. This elegantly connects the physical Sirat with the spiritual path of Islam.

Key Terms
الثواب (reward)
العقاب (punishment)
الصراط (the Path/Bridge)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Sirat is purely metaphorical
Correction: The author affirms it as a real physical bridge, citing its description from al-Ghazali's creed.

Checkpoint
What is the Sirat described as?
A) A light on the right path
B) A bridge over Hell, sharper than a sword and finer than a hair
C) A river of mercy
D) A gate to Paradise

Key Takeaway
The Sirat is a real bridge over Hell that believers will cross on the Day of Judgment.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that every hidden action will be rewarded or punished, would you change something you did today? What is that thing?
?
The Sirat is sharper than a sword and finer than a hair—are you living in a way that will allow you to cross it safely? What specific sin are you still clinging to that might weigh you down?
?
Do you actually fear God's punishment as much as you desire His reward? How does your daily routine reflect which one dominates your heart?

The Parable of the Path: Sirat as Islam
Prophetic parable of the straight path and its allegorical interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the prophetic parable of the straight path and its interpretation, showing that the Sirat is Islam and that only those who followed Islam in this world will cross it on the Day of Judgment.

Core Idea
The Sirat is Islam; only those who entered Islam in this world will cross the physical bridge.

The author presents a profound hadith that likens the path of Islam to a straight path with walls, doors, and curtains, and then interprets each element. The commentary by al-Mulla Ilyas reveals that the straight path is Islam itself, the doors are God's prohibitions, and the callers are the Quran and the inner divine admonisher. This lesson connects the physical Sirat of the afterlife to the spiritual path of obedience in this world.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and translation
Read the prophetic parable carefully. Notice the vivid imagery: walls, doors, curtains, and two callers.
2
Understand the interpretation
The commentator explains what each element represents: the path is Islam, the doors are God's prohibitions, the curtains are His limits, the first caller is the Quran, the second is the inner admonisher.
3
Derive the conclusion
Since the path is Islam, only those who have Islam (i.e., entered it in this world) will be able to cross the physical Sirat on the Day of Judgment.
This ties spiritual submission to physical salvation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?

?
If the Sirat is Islam itself, then your daily actions are either keeping you on the path or leading you to one of the open doors. Honestly, which door are you most tempted to open? What concrete step will you take today to close it and return to the path?
