Refuting the Denial of the Sirat's Extreme Description
The author defends the authenticity of the Sirat's extreme description.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the description of the Sirat as finer than hair and sharper than a sword is authentic according to hadith methodology, and how it harmonizes with the varying lights of people.

Core Idea
The Sirat's extreme description is authentic and explains the varied experience of people.

Some have questioned the authenticity of the famous description of the Sirat (the bridge over Hell) as being finer than hair and sharper than a sword. This passage provides a clear refutation based on principles of hadith criticism. It shows that the report, even if transmitted as a mursal of a Companion, is considered connected and thus acceptable. Moreover, a supporting hadith explains that the Sirat appears differently to each person according to their light, reconciling the extreme description with divine justice.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the two main parts: the refutation of al-Qarafi and the supporting hadith.
Pay attention to the term 'mursal of a Companion'.
2
Identify the objection and its refutation
Al-Qarafi claimed no authentic report supports the extreme description. The author rejects this using the principle that a mursal of a Companion is considered a connected hadith.
3
Understand the mursal principle
A mursal hadith is when a narrator says 'the Prophet said' without naming the Companion. But if a Companion says it, it is considered connected and authentic in the view of many scholars.
This is key to the argument.
4
Examine the supporting hadith
The hadith explains that the Sirat appears according to each person's light. For some it widens, for the least it is finer than hair and sharper than a sword. This shows the description is not only authentic but also meaningful.
5
Reflect on the lesson's significance
Realize that this incident combines hadith methodology (accepting mursal of a Companion) and theological understanding (the Sirat's variability) to defend a well-known belief.
This strengthens faith in the transmitted reports.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا وأما ما نقل عن القرافي (١) أنه قال: 'لم يصح في الصراط أنه أدق من الشعر وأحد من السيف شيء' فكلام لا يصح؛ لأن مرسل الصحابي (٢) في حكم الوصل على الصواب، وقد ورد في الخبر المروي أن الصراط يظهر يوم القيامة فيه للأبصار على قدر أنوار الناس فمن الناس من يكون له على الصراط يمشي شعاعه بين يديه وعن يمينه وعن شماله فرسخًا وأكثر وأقل فيتسع الصراط في حقه على قدر نوره فأقلهم نورا هو أخفى من الشعر وأحد من السيف اهـ كلام المنلا إلياس
This — as for what has been transmitted from al-Qarafi that he said: 'Nothing has been authenticated regarding the Path being finer than hair and sharper than a sword' — is a statement that is not correct, because the mursal of a Companion is in the ruling of a connected (report) according to the correct view. And it has come in the transmitted report that the Path appears on the Day of Resurrection to the eyes according to the lights of the people. So among people there is one for whom on the Path his light goes before him and to his right and to his left for a mile or more or less, and the Path widens for him according to his light. So the least of them in light is finer than hair and sharper than a sword. End of the words of al-Mulla Ilyas.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an objection. Al-Qarafi claimed that the description of the Sirat (bridge) as finer than hair and sharper than a sword has no authentic basis. The author rejects this, arguing that the mursal (a hadith where a Companion says 'the Prophet said' without naming the Prophet) of a Companion is considered to have the ruling of a connected hadith, meaning it is acceptable. He then provides supporting evidence: a transmitted report stating that the Sirat will appear on the Day of Resurrection according to the light of each person. For some, the Sirat will be wide, for others narrower; the least in light finds it finer than hair and sharper than a sword. Thus, the extreme description is not only authentic but also explains the variability experienced by different people.

Key Terms
القرافي (al-Qarafi)
مرسل الصحابي (mursal of a Companion)
الوصل (connection)
أنوار الناس (lights of the people)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The description of the Sirat as finer than hair and sharper than a sword has no authentic basis in hadith.
Correction: The author shows that the report is authentic because it is a mursal of a Companion, which is considered connected. Additionally, a supporting hadith explains its meaning.

Checkpoint
Why does the author consider al-Qarafi's objection invalid?
A) Because the report is in the Quran
B) Because a mursal of a Companion is considered connected
C) Because al-Qarafi was not a scholar
D) Because the report is logically necessary

Key Takeaway
The description of the Sirat as finer than hair and sharper than a sword is authentic through the mursal of a Companion and is understood as relative to each person's light.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
On that Day, the Sirat will widen for you according to your light. If your light is minimal, it will be finer than hair and sharper than a sword. Does this truth sink into your heart today? What single action will you take before tonight to increase your light for that crossing?
?
The author defends the authenticity of this description with a methodological argument. But deep down, do you really believe you will cross that bridge? If you did, what would you change about your life starting right now? Name one concrete thing.
?
The least in light will face the most terrifying crossing. Are you certain you are not among them? What evidence from your daily life—your prayers, your charity, your character—actually proves you have light? If the evidence is weak, what will you do about it today?

The Reality of the Scale
Definition and description of the Scale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the description of the Scale (Mizan) as a real physical balance with two pans and a tongue, each pan as vast as the heavens and earth.

Core Idea
The Scale is a real balance with two pans the size of heavens and earth.

The author describes the Scale used to weigh deeds as a literal instrument. He specifies that it has two pans of light and darkness, each vast in size. This makes the reality of the afterlife judgment tangible and emphasizes the grandeur of divine justice.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the detailed description of the Scale.
The passage uses strong terms like 'حقيقي' (real) to assert literalness.
2
Identify the components of the Scale
The Scale has two pans (كفتان) and a tongue (لسان). Each pan is as wide as the heavens and earth. One pan is of light for good deeds, the other of darkness for evil deeds.
The contrast between light and darkness symbolizes good and evil.
3
Reflect on the symbolic meaning
Consider why the pans are described as immense. This highlights the seriousness of weighing deeds and the vastness of divine justice.
The description also counters any metaphorical interpretation of the Scale.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والميزان الذي يوزن به أعمال المؤمنين من الخير والشر والطاعة والمعصية هو ميزان حقيقي بكفتين ولسان كل كفة طباق السموات والأرض كفة من نور والأخرى من ظلام؛ فالنيرة للحسنات والمظلمة للسيئات. واعلم أن من الأخيار من لا يوزن له عمل ولا ينشر له كتاب كأهل البلاء وكذلك من الأشرار، بل يزف الأولون إلى الجنة من غير وزن ولا حساب ويساق الآخرون إلى النار كذلك بدليل قوله تعالى: (حَبِطَتْ أَعْمَلُهُمْ فَلَا نُقِيمُ هُمْ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ وَزَنا) (سورة الكهف آية: ١٠٥). كذا نقله الشيخ علوان، وكأن المصنف خص الوزن لأعمال المؤمنين للإشارة إلى ذلك.
And the Scale by which the deeds of the believers are weighed — good and evil, obedience and disobedience — is a real scale with two pans and a tongue; each pan is as wide as the heavens and the earth; one pan is of light and the other of darkness. So the luminous pan is for good deeds and the dark one for evil deeds. And know that among the righteous there are those whose deeds will not be weighed and whose book will not be unfolded — like the people of affliction — and similarly among the wicked. Rather, the former will be hastened to Paradise without any weighing or reckoning, and the latter will be driven to Hell likewise, based on the saying of the Exalted: 'Their deeds have become worthless, so We will not establish for them on the Day of Resurrection any weight' (Surah al-Kahf, verse 105). Thus transmitted by Shaykh Alwan, and it seems that the author specified the weighing to be for the deeds of the believers to indicate that point.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage is a definition of the Mizan (Scale) and an exception to the general rule. The author begins by stating that the Scale by which the deeds of believers are weighed is a literal scale with two pans and a tongue, each pan as vast as the heavens and the earth — one of light for good deeds, one of darkness for evil deeds. Then he introduces a nuance: there are righteous people, such as those who suffered afflictions (أهل البلاء), whose deeds will not be weighed and whose books will not be unfolded. Instead, they will be rushed directly to Paradise. Similarly, some wicked people will be rushed to Hell without weighing. He supports this with the Quranic verse from Surah al-Kahf indicating that the deeds of disbelievers are worthless and will have no weight. He notes that this is transmitted by Shaykh Alwan, and that the author may have specified that the Scale is for believers' deeds to imply that for a special category, the weighing is not applied.

Key Terms
الميزان
كفتان
لسان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Scale is only a metaphor for justice and not a real physical object.
Correction: The author explicitly states it is 'حقيقي' (real) with physical pans and a tongue.

Checkpoint

A) Gold and silver
B) Light and darkness
C) Fire and water
D) Heaven and earth

Key Takeaway
The Scale is a real instrument with two immense pans of light and darkness to weigh deeds.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the scale has a pan of light and a pan of darkness, which of your deeds are you placing on each? Are you confident the light pan will outweigh the darkness?
?
The scale is real and immense, each pan as wide as the heavens and the earth. Do you live as if your every deed will be weighed on such a scale? What changes if you truly believe that?
?
One pan is for good deeds, the other for evil. How does the reality of this scale affect your choices today? Will you rush to fill the luminous pan before it is too late?

Those Whose Deeds Are Not Weighed
Exception to the general rule of weighing deeds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that some righteous people (like those afflicted) and some wicked people will not have their deeds weighed but will be sent directly to Paradise or Hell.

Core Idea
Affliction can expiate sins so deeds are not weighed.

After describing the Scale, the author introduces an important exception: not everyone’s deeds will be weighed. Some righteous, due to their trials (أهل البلاء), go straight to Paradise without weighing. Similarly, some wicked go directly to Hell. This shows Allah’s mercy and justice in different forms.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the exception
Read the Arabic passage and translation. The author says 'واعلم' (know) to draw attention to a special ruling.
Pay attention to the two groups mentioned: righteous and wicked.
2
Identify the two categories exempted from weighing
First: some righteous, like the people of affliction (أهل البلاء). Second: some wicked. Both are not weighed; they go directly to their destinations.
The righteous go to Paradise without weighing or reckoning; the wicked go to Hell.
3
Analyze the Quranic evidence
The author cites verse 105 of Surah al-Kahf to support that some deeds have no weight. Reflect on how this verse applies to the wicked.
The verse is about disbelievers whose deeds are worthless.
4
Consider the wisdom behind this exception
Think about why Allah would exempt some from weighing. For the righteous, their afflictions purify them so they enter Paradise directly. For the wicked, their disbelief makes their deeds weightless.
This shows that the Scale is not needed for those whose fate is already determined.

The Reality of the Sirat (Bridge)
Refutes al-Qarafi's denial and describes the Sirat's reality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the refutation of al-Qarafi's denial regarding the Sirat and the authentic description of the Sirat as it appears on the Day of Resurrection.

Core Idea
The Sirat is real and its description is authentically established through Prophetic tradition.

In this passage, the author addresses a doubt raised by al-Qarafi, who claimed that nothing authentic establishes the Sirat being finer than a hair and sharper than a sword. The refutation relies on the principle that a mursal narration from a Companion is treated as a connected (musnad) tradition, thus the report describing the Sirat is valid. The description that follows gives a vivid picture of the Sirat's manifestation according to each person's spiritual light.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the two parts: refutation of al-Qarafi and the description of the Sirat.
The passage is continuous; the refutation sets the stage for the description.
2
Understand the refutation of al-Qarafi
Identify the claim of al-Qarafi and the author's response. The key point is that a mursal of a Companion is considered as a connected narration in the correct view.
This is an important principle in hadith sciences.
3
Examine the description of the Sirat
Follow how the Sirat appears according to people's lights. Notice the ray (shu'aa') that walks before, right, and left, and how the Sirat widens accordingly.
The description is literal and emphasizes varying experiences.
4
Reflect on the theological significance
Consider why this description matters: it affirms the reality of the Sirat and that its perception differs based on one's faith and deeds.
This connects to the broader topic of eschatological events.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذا وأما ما نقل عن القرافي أنه قال: "لم يصح في الصراط أنه أدق من الشعر وأحد من السيف شيء" فكلام لا يصح؛ لأن مرسل الصحابي في حكم الوصل على الصواب، وقد ورد في الخبر المروي أن الصراط يظهر يوم القيامة فيه للأبصار على قدر أنوار الناس فمن الناس من يكون له على الصراط يمشي شعاعه بين يديه وعن يمينه وعن شماله فرسخًا وأكثر وأقل فيتسع الصراط في حقه على قدر نوره فأقلهم نورا هو أخفى من الشعر وأحد من السيف اهـ كلام المنلا إلياس
This: as for what was transmitted from al-Qarafi that he said: "Nothing has been authentically established about the Sirat that it is finer than a hair and sharper than a sword" – this statement is not valid; because the mursal of a Companion is in the ruling of connected (musnad) according to the correct view, and it has been reported in the transmitted tradition that the Sirat will appear on the Day of Resurrection, visible to eyes according to the lights of the people. Among the people, there is one for whom on the Sirat his ray walks before him, on his right, and on his left, for a parasang, more or less, and the Sirat widens for him according to his light. The one with the least light is (the Sirat) finer than a hair and sharper than a sword. End of the words of Mulla Ilyas.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage is a refutation and explanation. It begins by refuting a claim from al-Qarafi that the Sirat (bridge) being finer than a hair and sharper than a sword is not authentically established. The author rejects this by stating that a mursal narration from a Companion is considered legally connected (musnad) in the correct view. Then it provides a transmitted report describing the Sirat: on the Day of Resurrection, it appears to sight according to people's light. Some people have a ray (shu'aa') that walks before them, to their right, and to their left for a parasang or more or less. The Sirat widens for that person proportionally to their light. The person with the least light finds it finer than a hair and sharper than a sword. The passage ends by attributing this explanation to Mulla Ilyas.

Key Terms
الصراط
مرسل الصحابي
الوصول
الشعاع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The description of the Sirat (finer than hair, sharper than sword) is not authentically established in hadith.
Correction: The author shows that the mursal narration from a Companion is considered connected and thus authentic, and the description is preserved in transmitted tradition.

Checkpoint

A) It is rejected
B) It is in the ruling of a connected (musnad) narration
C) It is weaker than a mursal from a Tabi'i
D) It is only accepted in matters of reward and punishment

Key Takeaway
The Sirat is a real bridge on the Day of Resurrection, authentically described in hadith, and its experience varies with a person's spiritual light.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The Companions transmitted this tradition with care; do you trust their message enough to live your life in preparation for this reality, or do you postpone repentance?
?
The Sirat widens for those with more light — what specific action will you commit to this week to earn more light from Allah, even if it costs you comfort or pride?

The Reality of the Mizan (Balance)
Definition and description of the real balance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Mizan is a real physical balance with two pans and a tongue, one of light and one of darkness.

Core Idea
The Mizan is a real balance, not a metaphor.

Sanusi clarifies that the balance used on the Day of Judgment is not symbolic but a real created object. He describes its physical characteristics: two pans as vast as the heavens and earth, one made of light for good deeds and one of darkness for evil deeds. This lesson lays the foundation for understanding how deeds are weighed.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the opening sentence describing the Mizan. Note the key terms: ميزان حقيقي, كفتان, لسان.
The Arabic is concise but descriptive.
2
Identify the characteristics
List the features: real (حقيقي), two pans (كفتان), a tongue (لسان), each pan is vast (طباق السموات والأرض), one of light (نور) for good deeds (الحسنات), one of darkness (ظلام) for evil deeds (السيئات).
3
Understand the significance
Ask why the author specifies that the balance is real. This guards against interpreting it metaphorically. The vivid description emphasizes the tangible reality of the Hereafter.
This connects to the core idea.

And the balance (mizan) with which the deeds of the believers are weighed – good and evil, obedience and disobedience – is a real balance with two pans and a tongue; each pan is as vast as the heavens and the earth: one pan of light and the other of darkness. Commentary
This passage defines and describes the Mizan (balance). It states that the balance used to weigh the deeds of believers is a real (haqiqi) balance, with two pans and a tongue. Each pan is as vast as the layers of the heavens and earth: one pan is made of light for good deeds, the other of darkness for evil deeds. Then the author adds an important point: some righteous people, such as those who endured severe affliction in the world, will not have their deeds weighed or their books spread, and similarly some wicked people will not be weighed. Instead, the righteous are taken directly to Paradise without any weighing or accounting, and the wicked are driven directly to Hell, based on Quranic evidence from Surah al-Kahf verse 105, which indicates that the deeds of disbelievers are rendered worthless, so no weight is established for them. The author notes that the statement 'weighing the deeds of the believers' might be specific to those who are not from this exceptional category.

?

Exceptions to the Weighing of Deeds
Explanation of who is not weighed and why.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that not all people will have their deeds weighed on the Mizan; some are exempt based on Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
Some are weighed, others are sent straight without weighing.

After describing the balance, Sanusi introduces an important nuance: not everyone's deeds are weighed. Some righteous people, such as those who suffered severe affliction, bypass the scales entirely, as do some wicked people. This is supported by a Quranic verse. This lesson clarifies the exceptions to the general rule of weighing deeds.

Guided Path
1
Read the exception passage
Read from 'واعلم أن من الأخيار' to the end. Identify the two categories: some righteous (أهل البلاء) and some wicked.
Notice the phrase 'لا يوزن له عمل'.
2
Understand the fate of the exceptions
The righteous are 'يزفون إلى الجنة' (conveyed to Paradise) without weighing or account; the wicked are 'يساقون إلى النار' (driven to Hell) without weighing.
3
Check the Quranic evidence
The author quotes Surah al-Kahf 105: 'فَلَا نُقِيمُ لَهُمْ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ وَزْنًا' (We will not establish for them any weight). Understand how this verse supports the exception.
The verse originally refers to disbelievers, but the author applies it to show that some will not have their deeds weighed.
4
Note the author's remark
The author speculates that specifying weighing for believers indicates that the exception is for those who are not from the exceptional category.
This is a subtle point about the scope of the verse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(والميزان الذي يوزن به أعمال المؤمنين من الخير والشر والطاعة والمعصية) هو ميزان حقيقي بكفتين ولسان كل كفة طباق السموات والأرض كفة من نور والأخرى من ظلام؛ فالنيرة للحسنات والمظلمة للسيئات. واعلم أن من الأخيار من لا يوزن له عمل ولا ينشر له كتاب كأهل البلاء وكذلك من الأشرار، بل يزف الأولون إلى الجنة من غير وزن ولا حساب ويساق الآخرون إلى النار كذلك بدليل قوله تعالى: (حَبِطَتْ أَعْمَلُهُمْ فَلَا نُقِيمُ هُمْ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ وَزَنا ) (سورة الكهف آية: ١٠٥). كذا نقله الشيخ علوان، وكأن المصنف خص الوزن لأعمال المؤمنين للإشارة إلى ذلك.
And the balance (mizan) with which the deeds of the believers are weighed – good and evil, obedience and disobedience – is a real balance with two pans and a tongue; each pan is as vast as the heavens and the earth: one pan of light and the other of darkness. The luminous one is for good deeds and the dark one for evil deeds. And know that among the righteous there is one whose deed is not weighed and whose book is not unfolded, like the people of affliction, and similarly among the wicked. Rather, the former are conveyed to Paradise without weighing or accounting, and the latter are driven to Hell likewise, as evidence of Allah's statement: (Their deeds have become worthless, so We will not establish for them on the Day of Resurrection any weight) (Surah al-Kahf, verse 105). Thus narrated Shaykh Alwan, and it seems that the author specified weighing for the deeds of believers to indicate that.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage defines and describes the Mizan (balance). It states that the balance used to weigh the deeds of believers is a real (haqiqi) balance, with two pans and a tongue. Each pan is as vast as the layers of the heavens and earth: one pan is made of light for good deeds, the other of darkness for evil deeds. Then the author adds an important point: some righteous people, such as those who endured severe affliction in the world, will not have their deeds weighed or their books spread, and similarly some wicked people will not be weighed. Instead, the righteous are taken directly to Paradise without any weighing or accounting, and the wicked are driven directly to Hell, based on Quranic evidence from Surah al-Kahf verse 105, which indicates that the deeds of disbelievers are rendered worthless, so no weight is established for them. The author notes that the statement 'weighing the deeds of the believers' might be specific to those who are not from this exceptional category.

Key Terms
أهل البلاء
يزف
يساق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Everyone's deeds will be weighed on the Mizan without exception.
Correction: Some righteous and wicked are exempt; they go directly to Paradise or Hell.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who are among those whose deeds are not weighed?
A) All believers
B) People of affliction (أهل البلاء)
C) All sinners
D) Only prophets

Key Takeaway
Some people are exempt from the weighing of deeds and are sent directly to their final abode.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you living as if your deeds will be weighed in detail, or do you assume you are among the exempt? What specific affliction have you faced that makes you hope for direct entry, and how does that affect your current actions?
?
If you were to be among the people of affliction, would your deeds now be worthy of direct Paradise? What is the one deed you are holding onto that would be worthless on that Day?
?
The passage says some wicked are also sent directly without weighing. Does that comfort or terrify you? What does it reveal about Allah's justice that some are not even given a chance to present their deeds?

Paradise and Hell Are Created Now
Affirms creation of Paradise and Hell now, with proof and refutation of Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the evidence that Paradise and Hell were created before the Day of Judgment, and the refutation of the Mu'tazila who claimed otherwise.

Core Idea
Paradise and Hell were created now, not just on Judgment Day.

The Tahawiyyah affirms that Paradise and Hell are already created. This lesson examines the proof from the story of Adam and the Qur'anic verses that describe them as 'prepared' for the righteous and disbelievers. We will also see how the author answers an objection from another verse.

Guided Path
1
Read the creedal statement
Read the opening sentence: 'And Paradise and Hell are created...' This establishes the topic.
Notice that the statement also mentions they do not perish, but the focus here is on creation.
2
Understand the Mu'tazila position
The Mu'tazila claimed Paradise and Hell will be created on the Day of Recompense, not before. The author directly contradicts them.
3
Examine the first proof: Adam and Eve
The author cites the story of Adam and Eve dwelling in Paradise as evidence that Paradise existed before the Day of Judgment.
This is a strong narrative proof.
4
Examine the second proof: Qur'anic verses
Verses like 'Prepared for the righteous' (3:133) and 'Prepared for the disbelievers' (3:131) indicate Paradise and Hell are already prepared.
The word 'prepared' (أعدت) implies prior existence.
5
Consider the objection and answer
An objection from Quran 28:83 is raised, but the author answers that the verse can refer to the present state and continuity, and the story of Adam remains uncontradicted.
This shows how objections are addressed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالجَنَّةُ وَالنَّارُ مَخْلُوقَتَانِ لَا يَفْنَيَانِ وَلَا يَبِيدَانِ، وَإِنَّ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى خَلَقَ الجَنَّةَ وَالنَّارَ وَخَلَقَ لَهُمَا أَهْلًا؛ فَمَنْ شَاءَ إِلَى الْجَنَّةِ أَدْخَلَهُ فَضْلًا مِنْهُ وَمَنْ شَاءَ مِنْهُمْ إِلَى النَّارِ أَدْخَلَهُ عَدْلًا مِنْهُ، وَكُلٌّ يَعْمَلُ مَا قَدْ فُرِغَ مِنْهُ وَصَائِرٌ إِلَى مَا خُلِقَ لَهُ، وَالخَيْرُ وَالشَّرُّ مُقَدَّرَانِ عَلَى العِبَادِ. (و) نقول: (الجنة والنار مخلوقتان الآن خلافا للمعتزلة أنهما يخلقان يوم الجزاء. لنا قصة آدم وحواء وإسكانهما الجنة، والآيات الظاهرة في إعدادهما مثل: (أُعِدَّتْ لِلْمُتَّقِينَ) [سورة آل عمران آية ١٣٣] ومثل: (أُعِدَّتْ لِلْكَفِرِينَ) [سورة آل عمران آية ١٣١]. فإن عورض بمثل قوله تعالى: (تِلْكَ الدَّارُ الْآخِرَةُ نَجْعَلُهَا لِلَّذِينَ لَا يُرِيدُونَ عُلُوًّا فِي الْأَرْضِ وَلَا فَسَادًا) [سورة القصص آية ٨٣]، قلنا: يحتمل الحال والاستمرار، ولو سلم فقصة آدم تبقى سالمة عن المعارضة. ولا يفنيان هما ولا أهلها ولا يبيدان سرمدا تكرارًا للتأكيد أي لا يطرأ عليهما عدم مستمر؛ لقوله تعالى في حق الفريقين: (خَالِدِينَ فِيهَا أَبَدًا) [سورة النساء آية ٥٧]، فما قيل: إنهما يهلكان ولو لحظة تحقيقا لقوله تعالى: (كُلُّ شَيْءٍ هَالِكٌ إِلَّا وَجْهَهُ) [سورة القصص آية ٨٨] فلا ينافي البقاء بهذا المعنى، على أنك قد عرفت ألا دلالة في الآية على الفناء، وذهبت الجهمية إلى أنهما يفنيان ويفني أهلهما، وهو قول باطل مخالف للكتاب والسنة والإجماع ليس عليه شبهة فضلا عن حجة.
And Paradise and Hell are created, they do not perish nor cease to exist. And indeed Allah most High created Paradise and Hell and created for them inhabitants; so whomever He wills, He admits to Paradise out of His bounty, and whomever He wills of them, He admits to Hell out of His justice. And each one does what has been decreed for him, and each is headed to what he was created for. And good and evil are predestined for the servants. And we say: Paradise and Hell are created now, contrary to the Mu'tazila who say they will be created on the Day of Recompense. Our proof is the story of Adam and Eve and their dwelling in Paradise, and the apparent verses concerning their preparation, like (Prepared for the righteous) [Surah Al Imran verse 133] and like (Prepared for the disbelievers) [Surah Al Imran verse 131]. If it is objected with like His statement: (That is the abode of the Hereafter – We assign it for those who do not desire exaltedness in the earth nor corruption) [Surah al-Qasas verse 83], we say: it can refer to the present state and continuity, and even if conceded, the story of Adam remains free from objection. And they do not perish, neither they nor their inhabitants, nor do they cease to exist eternally, as a repetition for emphasis, i.e., non-existence does not occur to them continuously; due to His statement concerning the two groups: (Abiding therein forever) [Surah an-Nisa verse 57]. So what is said that they will be destroyed even for a moment as a realization of His statement: (Everything is perishing except His Face) [Surah al-Qasas verse 88] does not contradict perpetual existence in this sense, especially since you already know that there is no evidence in the verse for annihilation. The Jahmiyya went to the view that they will perish and their inhabitants will perish, and it is a false statement, contrary to the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus, having no doubt, let alone proof.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal statement and proof. It begins by quoting the Tahawiyyah creed: Paradise and Hell are created (makhluqatan), they do not perish (la yafnayan) nor cease to exist (la yabidan). Then it explains that Allah created them and their inhabitants. People are admitted to Paradise by His bounty and to Hell by His justice. Then the commentary addresses two deviations: First, against the Mu'tazila who claim Paradise and Hell will be created only on the Day of Judgment. The proof is the story of Adam and Eve dwelling in Paradise (showing Paradise existed then) and verses stating 'prepared for the righteous' etc. A possible objection from Quran 28:83 is answered: it can refer to present or continuous state, and even if it meant only in the afterlife, the story of Adam remains as counter-evidence. Second, against the Jahmiyya who claim Paradise and Hell will eventually perish. The proof is the Quranic statement of 'eternal abiding' (khalidina fiha abada) for both groups. The objection from 'everything perishing except His Face' is refuted: it does not imply permanent destruction but rather a passing change, and in any case, there is no evidence for annihilation. The Jahmiyya view is condemned as false, contradicting Quran, Sunnah, and consensus.

Key Terms
الجنة
النار
مخلوقة
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Paradise and Hell will only be created on the Day of Judgment.
Correction: They are created now, as proven by the story of Adam and the Qur'anic description of them as 'prepared'.

Checkpoint
What proof does the author provide against the Mu'tazila view that Paradise and Hell will be created on the Day of Judgment?
A) The story of Adam and Eve dwelling in Paradise
B) The statement that everything perishes except Allah's Face
C) Consensus of the Salaf
D) Rational argument

Key Takeaway
Paradise and Hell were created by Allah before the Day of Judgment, as evidenced by the story of Adam and explicit Qur'anic verses.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Paradise and Hell are already created and waiting, how does that change the way you view your daily choices? What is one decision you will make today with this reality in mind?
?
The Mu'tazila denied the current existence of Paradise and Hell because of a rational objection. Are there any aspects of Islamic belief where you are tempted to prioritize your own reasoning over clear texts? How will you humble yourself before Allah's words?
?
Adam and Eve were physically placed in Paradise before the Day of Judgment. Does your longing for Paradise feel that real and immediate? What can you do today to increase that certainty and desire in your heart?

Paradise and Hell Are Eternal and Never Perish
Affirms eternity of Paradise, Hell, and their inhabitants; refutes Jahmiyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the evidence that Paradise, Hell, and their inhabitants are eternal and never cease to exist, and the refutation of the Jahmiyya who claimed they will perish.

Core Idea
Paradise and Hell are eternal, never perishing.

Having established that Paradise and Hell are created, the Tahawiyyah now affirms that they will never perish. This lesson examines the proof from the Qur'anic promise of eternal abiding for both groups and refutes the false claim of the Jahmiyya that they will be annihilated based on a misinterpretation of a verse.

Guided Path
1
Read the statement of eternity
Read: 'And they do not perish, neither they nor their inhabitants, nor do they cease to exist eternally.' This is the second key claim.
The repetition emphasizes perpetuity.
2
Identify the proof from Quran
The author cites Quran 4:57 which says both groups will abide 'forever' (أبداً). This proves eternal existence.
3
Consider the objection from 'everything perishes'
Some use Quran 28:88 ('Everything is perishing except His Face') to argue Paradise and Hell will perish. The author refutes this.
Note the distinction between passing away and annihilation.
4
Understand the refutation of Jahmiyya
The Jahmiyya claim Paradise and Hell and their inhabitants will perish. The author declares this false, contrary to Quran, Sunnah, and consensus.
The author states it has no doubt, let alone proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The Creation of Paradise and Hell: Evidence and Refutation
Maydani asserts Paradise and Hell are created now and refutes the Mu'tazila view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni position that Paradise and Hell are already created and how the Mu'tazila view is refuted using textual evidence and reasoned response.

Core Idea
Paradise and Hell exist now, not only on Judgment Day.

This passage from Maydani tackles a key theological debate concerning the present existence of Paradise and Hell. It presents the Sunni belief that both are already created, supported by the story of Adam and Eve and clear Quranic verses. The author also anticipates and refutes a potential objection, strengthening the case.

Guided Path
1
Read the Passage
Start by reading the Arabic text and its English translation to get an overview of the argument.
Notice the direct language: 'والجنة والنار مخلوقتان الآن'.
2
Identify the Evidence
Find the two pieces of evidence: the historical precedent of Adam and Eve in Paradise, and the Quranic verses using the word 'أعدت' (prepared).
These show that Paradise and Hell were prepared for their inhabitants before the Day of Judgment.
3
Examine the Objection and Reply
Look at the objection based on the verse 'تلك الدار الآخرة' and how Maydani responds by offering alternative interpretations and pointing out that the Adam story remains unchallenged.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْجَنَّةُ وَالنَّارُ مَخْلُوقَتَانِ. (و) نَقُولُ: (الْجَنَّةُ وَالنَّارُ مَخْلُوقَتَانِ الْآنَ خِلَافًا لِلْمُعْتَزِلَةِ أَنَّهُمَا يُخْلَقَانِ يَوْمَ الْجَزَاءِ. لَنَا قِصَّةُ آدَمَ وَحَوَّاءَ وَإِسْكَانُهُمَا الْجَنَّةَ، وَالْآيَاتُ الظَّاهِرَةُ فِي إِعْدَادِهِمَا مِثْلُ: أُعِدَّتْ لِلْمُتَّقِينَ [سورة آل عمران آية: ١٣٣] وَمِثْلُ: أُعِدَّتْ لِلْكَافِرِينَ [سورة آل عمران آية: ١٣١]. فَإِنْ عُورِضَ بِمِثْلِ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: تِلْكَ الدَّارُ الْآخِرَةُ نَجْعَلُهَا لِلَّذِينَ لَا يُرِيدُونَ عُلُوًّا فِي الْأَرْضِ وَلَا فَسَادًا [سورة القصص آية: ٨٣]، قُلْنَا: يَحْتَمِلُ الْحَالَ وَالِاسْتِمْرَارَ، وَلَوْ سُلِّمَ فَقِصَّةُ آدَمَ تَبْقَى سَالِمَةً عَنِ الْمُعَارَضَةِ. كَذَا فِي شَرْحِ الْعَقَائِدِ (١).
And Paradise and Hell are created. And we say: Paradise and Hell are created now, contrary to the Mu'tazila that they will be created on the Day of Recompense. Our evidence is the story of Adam and Eve and their dwelling in Paradise, and the apparent verses about their preparation, such as: 'Prepared for the righteous' [Surah Al Imran 133], and such as: 'Prepared for the disbelievers' [Surah Al Imran 131]. If it is objected by a similar verse such as His statement: 'That is the final abode; We assign it to those who do not desire exaltation in the earth nor corruption' [Surah Al-Qasas 83], we say: It may refer to the present time or to continuity, and even if conceded, the story of Adam remains free from opposition. Thus in Sharh al-Aqa'id (1).
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the creation of Paradise and Hell now, combined with a refutation of the Mu'tazila. It begins by stating the position: Paradise and Hell are already created. Then it provides two proofs: the historical event of Adam and Eve dwelling in Paradise, and Quranic verses that describe both abodes as having been prepared. The author then addresses a potential objection: the verse 'That is the final abode' might suggest they will be created only in the hereafter. The answer is twofold: first, the verse can refer to the present or to continuity; second, even if taken as future, the story of Adam is a stronger evidence that remains uncontradicted. The passage thus defends the Sunni view against the Mu'tazila who claimed that Paradise and Hell will be created on the Day of Judgment.

Key Terms
الجنة
النار
المعتزلة
خلق
الإعداد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Paradise and Hell are not yet created and will only come into existence on the Day of Judgment.
Correction: The Quran and the story of Adam show they are already created and prepared for their inhabitants.

Checkpoint

A) Adam and Eve dwelling in Paradise
B) The verse 'Everything perishes'

Key Takeaway
Paradise and Hell are created now, as established by the dwelling of Adam in Paradise and the Quranic descriptions of their preparation.

?
The story of Adam shows that Paradise was real enough for him to dwell in. Are you seeking to dwell in that same Paradise, or are you content with the temporary gardens of this world? What is one concrete step you will take this week to orient your life toward the Hereafter?

Eternal Nature of Paradise and Hell
Maydani affirms Paradise and Hell are eternal and refutes the Jahmiyya view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Paradise and Hell are eternal and never cease to exist, based on Quranic evidence and scholarly consensus.

Core Idea
Paradise and Hell are eternal - neither they nor their inhabitants will ever perish.

This lesson establishes a core belief of Sunni Islam: the eternal duration of Paradise and Hell. Maydani presents the doctrinal affirmation, supports it with a clear Quranic proof, addresses a potential objection from another verse, and decisively refutes the Jahmiyya deviation. As you read, pay attention to how the author uses repetition for emphasis and how he defends the eternity of the abodes against apparent scriptural challenges.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the English translation. Let the author's confident tone set the stage for the doctrine.
Notice the repeated phrase for emphasis: 'لا يفنيان ولا يبيدان'.
2
Identify the main claim and its proof
Locate the assertion that Paradise and Hell never perish. What Quranic verse does the author cite to support this?
The verse 'خالدين فيها أبدا' (Abiding therein forever) is the primary evidence.
3
Examine the objection and its answer
Find the objection: some say Paradise and Hell will be destroyed even for a moment because of the verse 'كل شيء هالك إلا وجهه'. How does Maydani respond? He says it doesn't negate eternal subsistence and that the verse does not indicate annihilation.
4
Understand the refutation of the Jahmiyya
The Jahmiyya claimed both abodes and inhabitants perish. Maydani calls this a false statement contrary to Quran, Sunnah, and consensus, with no evidence.
This shows the gravity of the issue: it's not a minor opinion but a heretical deviation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْجَنَّةُ وَالنَّارُ لَا يَفْنَيَانِ وَلَا يَبِيدَانِ. (و) (لَا يَفْنَيَانِ) هُمَا وَلَا أَهْلُهَا (وَلَا يَبِيدَانِ) سَرْمَدًا تَكْرَارًا لِلتَّأْكِيدِ أَيْ لَا يَطْرَأُ عَلَيْهِمَا عَدَمٌ مُسْتَمِرٌّ؛ لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى فِي حَقِّ الْفَرِيقَيْنِ: (خَالِدِينَ فِيهَا أَبَدًا) [سورة النساء آية: ٥٧]، فَمَا قِيلَ: إِنَّهُمَا يَهْلَكَانِ وَلَوْ لَحْظَةً تَحْقِيقًا لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى: (كُلُّ شَيْءٍ هَالِكٌ إِلَّا وَجْهَهُ) [سورة القصص آية: ٨٨] فَلَا يُنَافِي الْبَقَاءَ بِهَذَا الْمَعْنَى، عَلَى أَنَّكَ قَدْ عَرَفْتَ أَلَا دَلَالَةَ فِي الْآيَةِ عَلَى الْفَنَاءِ، وَذَهَبَتِ الْجَهْمِيَّةُ إِلَى أَنَّهُمَا يَفْنَيَانِ وَيَفْنَى أَهْلُهُمَا، وَهُوَ قَوْلٌ بَاطِلٌ مُخَالِفٌ لِلْكِتَابِ وَالسُّنَّةِ وَالْإِجْمَاعِ لَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ شُبْهَةٌ فَضْلًا عَنْ حُجَّةٍ. كَذَا فِي شَرْحِ الْعَقَائِدِ (٢).
And Paradise and Hell do not perish and do not cease to exist. And (they do not perish) neither they nor their inhabitants, and (do not cease to exist) eternally, as a repetition for emphasis, meaning that perpetual non-existence does not befall them; because of the statement of Allah regarding the two groups: 'Abiding therein forever' [Surah An-Nisa 57]. So what is said that they will be destroyed, even for a moment, in realization of His statement: 'Everything is perishing except His Face' [Surah Al-Qasas 88], does not negate subsistence in this sense, especially since you have come to know that there is no indication in the verse of annihilation. And the Jahmiyya held that they perish and their inhabitants perish, and it is a false statement contrary to the Book, the Sunnah, and consensus, having no semblance of evidence, let alone a proof. Thus in Sharh al-Aqa'id (2).
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the eternal nature of Paradise and Hell. It begins with the assertion that they never perish or cease. The author explains that the phrasing is repeated for emphasis: neither the abodes nor their inhabitants will ever undergo permanent annihilation. The proof is from the Quranic verse promising eternity to both groups. Then an objection is considered: the verse 'Everything is perishing' might imply that Paradise and Hell will also perish at least momentarily. The author answers that this does not contradict eternal subsistence because the verse refers to the annihilation of all created things except God's essence, and Paradise and Hell are of a different nature; moreover, the verse does not explicitly indicate their annihilation. The author then refutes the Jahmiyya who claimed that Paradise and Hell will perish altogether, calling their view baseless and contrary to scripture, consensus, and reason.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that the verse 'Everything is perishing except His Face' proves that Paradise and Hell will also be destroyed, even if momentarily.
Correction: The author explains this verse does not negate eternal subsistence and does not indicate annihilation of the abodes. It refers to the perishing of all worldly things, not the afterlife.

Key Takeaway
Paradise and Hell are eternal; this is proven by the Quran and supported by consensus, and any claim that they will perish is a false innovation.

Benefit of Supplication and Charity for the Dead
Proof that the living's supplication and charity benefit the dead, refuting the Mu'tazilite denial.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Ahl al-Sunnah believe that the living's supplication and charity benefit the dead, and how this refutes the Mu'tazilite denial.

Core Idea
Intercession and charity for the dead are effective because Allah accepts them.

This lesson addresses a deeply comforting doctrine: that our prayers and charitable acts can reach our deceased loved ones. The Mu'tazilites denied this, arguing each soul is isolated. Here, Imam al-Tahawi presents the Sunni evidence from hadith and practice.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Let the author's own arguments and proofs come through.
Notice the structure: claim, objection, evidence, then general principle.
2
Identify the main claim and the Mu'tazilite objection
Find the statement that the living's supplication and charity benefit the dead. Then locate the Mu'tazilite counter-argument about the decree being unchangeable and each soul being recompensed only for its own deeds.
The Mu'tazilite argument is summarized briefly; the author refutes it with evidence.
3
Examine the two hadiths as proofs
Look at the hadith about a hundred Muslims interceding for a deceased person and the hadith of Sa'd ibn 'Ubadah about digging a well for his mother. Explain how each directly contradicts the Mu'tazilite position.
The first shows intercession is accepted; the second shows charity (water) benefits the dead.
4
Reflect on the general principle of answered supplication
The passage ends by affirming that Allah answers prayers in general, citing Quran and hadith. Consider how this principle underlies the specific benefit for the dead.
This reinforces that supplicating for the dead is part of the broader promise of answered prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَفي دُعَاءِ الأَحْيَاءِ لِلأَمْوَاتِ وَصَدَقَتِهِمْ مَنْفَعَةٌ لِلأَمْوَاتِ، وَاللَّهُ تَعَالَى يَسْتَجِيبُ الدَّعَوَاتِ وَيَقْضِي الحَاجَاتِ. (و) نقول : ( في دعاء الأحياء للأموات وصدقتهم عنهم (منفعة للأموات خلافًا للمعتزلة تمسكًا بأن القضاء لا يتبدل وكل نفس مرهونة بما كسبت والمرء مجزي بعمله لا بعمل غيره. ولنا ما روي في الصحاح من الدعاء للأموات خصوصا في صلاة الجنازة وقد توارثه السلف؛ فلو لم يكن للأموات نفع فيه لما كان له معنى، وقال عليه الصلاة والسلام: «مَا مِنْ ميّتٍ تُصَلِّي عَلَيهِ أُمَّةٌ مِنَ المُسْلِمِينَ يَبْلُغُونَ مَائَةً كُلُّهم يَشْفَعُونَ لَهُ إِلَّا شُفُعُوا فِيهِ. وعن سعد بن عبادة أنه قال: يا رسول الله إن أم سعد ماتت فأي صدقة أفضل؟ قال: «الماءُ» فحفر بثرًا وقال: هذه لأم سعد، والأحاديث والآثار في هذا الباب أكثر من أن تحصى. كذا في شرح العقائد. (والله تعالى يستجيب الدعوات ويقضي الحاجات)؛ لقوله تعالى: ادْعُونِي أسْتَجِبْ لَكُمْ [سورة غافر آية: ٦٠]، ولقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: يُسْتَجَابُ لِلْعَبْدِ مَا لَمْ يَدْعُ بِإِثْمِ أَوْ قَطِيعَةِ رَحِمِ مَا لَمْ يَسْتَعْجِلُ يَقُولُ دَعَوْتُ فَلَمْ يُسْتَجَبْ لي، ولقوله : إِنَّ رَبَّكُم حَبِيٌّ كَرِيمٌ يَسْتَحْيِي مِنْ عَبْدِهِ إِذَا رَفَعَ يَدَيهِ إِلَيْهِ أَنْ يَرُدَّهُمَا صِفْرًا
And in the supplication of the living for the dead and their charity, there is benefit for the dead. And Allah the Exalted answers prayers and fulfills needs. And we say: In the supplication of the living for the dead and their charity on their behalf, there is benefit for the dead, contrary to the Mu'tazilites, who cling [to the argument] that the decree does not change and that every soul is pledged for what it earned and a person is recompensed for his own deeds, not for the deeds of others. Our evidence is what has been reported in the authentic collections of supplication for the dead, especially in the funeral prayer, and the Salaf transmitted it; if there were no benefit for the dead in it, it would have no meaning. And he (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no deceased person over whom a community of Muslims numbering a hundred prays, all interceding for him, but their intercession is accepted for him.' And from Sa'd ibn 'Ubadah that he said: O Messenger of Allah, my mother Umm Sa'd has died, so which charity is best? He replied: 'Water.' So he dug a well and said: This is for Umm Sa'd. The hadiths and traditions on this topic are too numerous to count. This is as stated in Sharh al-'Aqa'id. And Allah the Exalted answers prayers and fulfills needs, due to His saying: 'Call upon Me, I will respond to you' [Surah Ghafir 40:60], and due to his (peace be upon him) saying: 'The servant is answered as long as he does not supplicate for sin or severing family ties and does not hasten, saying: I supplicated but I was not answered.' And due to his saying: 'Indeed your Lord is Loving and Generous; He is shy from His servant when he raises his hands to Him to send them back empty.'
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage defends the Ahl al-Sunnah doctrine that supplications and charitable acts performed by the living can benefit the deceased. It begins by stating the core belief: the living's prayers and charity bring benefit to the dead, and Allah answers prayers. The author then contrasts this with the Mu'tazilite position, which argues that divine decrees are immutable and that each soul is only responsible for its own deeds, so the actions of others cannot affect it. The proof against this is multifaceted: first, the continuous practice of the Salaf (early generations) of praying for the dead, especially in the funeral prayer, implies benefit; otherwise such practice would be meaningless. Second, two key hadiths are cited: (1) the Prophet's saying that if a hundred Muslims intercede for a deceased person, their intercession is accepted; (2) the hadith of Sa'd ibn 'Ubadah, where the Prophet recommended providing water as charity for his deceased mother. The author then reaffirms that Allah answers supplications in general, citing the Qur'anic verse 'Call upon Me, I will respond to you' and two hadiths: one about the conditions for acceptance (avoiding sin and haste) and another describing Allah's generosity and shyness to leave a supplicant empty-handed. The passage thus establishes the theological foundation for practices like praying for the dead and giving charity on their behalf.

دعاء
صدقة
الأموات
المعتزلة
الشفاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The dead cannot benefit from the actions of the living because each soul is only responsible for its own deeds and the divine decree is unchangeable.
Correction: The Mu'tazilite argument is refuted by authentic hadiths and the practice of the Salaf, showing that Allah accepts intercession and charity on behalf of the dead. Allah's decree allows for such benefit, and His response to supplication is a means by which the dead can receive reward.

Checkpoint

A) They say it is forbidden to pray for the dead
B) They argue that Allah does not change His decree and each soul is only recompensed for its own deeds
C) They claim the dead are unaware and thus cannot benefit
D) They deny the existence of an afterlife

Key Takeaway
Supplication and charity from the living benefit the deceased, as established by the Qur'an, Sunnah, and consensus of the Salaf.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
When you face a difficulty, do you turn to Allah with the same certainty that He will answer as the Prophet taught, or do you let doubts about the effectiveness of supplication linger?
?
The Prophet said Allah is shy to return empty hands; do you live with that confidence in your prayers, or do you hesitate to ask because you feel unworthy? What would it take for you to approach Allah with that boldness?

Conditions for Answered Supplication
Maydani enumerates conditions for answered supplication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three conditions for a supplication to be answered: sincerity of intention, purity of inner self, and presence of heart.

Core Idea
Sincere, heart-centered certainty is the key to answered supplication.

In this passage, Maydani outlines the spiritual prerequisites for du'a to be effective. Drawing from the hadith of the Prophet ﷺ, he emphasizes that mere words are not enough; the heart must be fully present and certain. This lesson explores those conditions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on conditions
Read the Arabic and translation focusing on the first part up to the hadith.
2
Identify the three conditions
Look for the three conditions listed: sincerity of intention (صدق النية), purity of inner self (خلوص الطوية), and presence of heart (حضور القلب).
3
Reflect on the hadith
Notice the hadith: 'Call upon Allah while being certain of the response...' How does this emphasize the role of certainty?
The hadith is from Tirmidhi and others.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن العمدة في ذلك صدق النية وخلوص الطوية وحضور القلب لقوله : ادْعُوا اللَّهَ وَأَنتُم مُوقِنُونَ بِالْإِجَابَةِ وَاعْلَمُوا أَنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى لَا يَسْتَجِيبُ الدُّعَاءَ مِنْ قَلْبِ غَافِلٍ. واختلف المشايخ في أنه هل يجوز أن يقال: يستجاب دعاء الكافرين؟ فمنعه الجمهور لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا دُعَاءُ الْكَافِرِينَ إِلَّا فِي ضَلَالٍ﴾ [سورة الرعد آية: ١٤]، ولأنه لا يدعو الله لأنه لا يعرفه؛ لأنه وإن أقر به فلما وصفه بما لا يليق به فقد نقض إقراره، وما روي في الحديث: «إِنَّ دَعْوَةَ المَظْلُومِ وَإِنْ كَانَ كَافِرًا تُسْتَجَابُ» محمول على كفران النعمة. وجوزه بعضهم لقوله تعالى حكاية عن إبليس: ﴿رَبِّ فَأَنْظِرْنِي﴾ [سورة الحجر آية: ٣٦]؛ فقال الله: ﴿فَإِنَّكَ مِنَ الْمُنْظَرِينَ﴾ [سورة الحجر آية: ٣٧]؛ هذه إجابة، وإليه ذهب أبو القاسم الحكيم وأبو نصر الدبوسي؛ قال الصدر الشهيد: وبه يفتى. كذا في شرح العقائد.
And know that the foundation in that is sincerity of intention, purity of inner self, and presence of heart, due to his saying: 'Call upon Allah while being certain of the response, and know that Allah does not answer the supplication from a heedless heart.' And the scholars disagreed about whether it is permissible to say: 'The supplication of disbelievers is answered.' The majority forbade it due to His saying: 'And the supplication of the disbelievers is only in error' [Surah al-Ra'd, verse 14], and because he does not supplicate Allah since he does not know Him; for even if he acknowledges Him, when he describes Him with what is not befitting, he has nullified his acknowledgment. And what is related in the hadith: 'Indeed, the supplication of the oppressed, even if he is a disbeliever, is answered' is interpreted as [referring to] ingratitude for blessings. And some permitted it due to His saying, narrating about Iblis: 'My Lord, then give me respite' [Surah al-Hijr, verse 36]; so Allah said: 'Then indeed you are of those given respite' [Surah al-Hijr, verse 37]; this is a response. And this view was held by Abu al-Qasim al-Hakim and Abu Nasr al-Dabusi. Al-Sadr al-Shahid said: 'And with it is the fatwa.' As in Sharh al-Aqa'id.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage is a combination of a directive and a legal discussion. First, the author states the key conditions for a supplication to be answered: sincerity of intention (ṣidq al-niyya), purity of inner self (khuṣūṣ al-ṭawiyya), and presence of heart (ḥuḍūr al-qalb). He supports this with a prophetic hadith quoting the Prophet ﷺ: 'Call upon Allah while being certain of the response, and know that Allah does not answer the supplication from a heedless heart.' This establishes that mere verbal invocation is insufficient; the heart must be engaged and certain.

Then the author moves to a scholastic disagreement (ikhtilāf al-mashāyikh): Is it permissible to say that the supplication of disbelievers (duʿāʾ al-kāfirīn) is answered? The majority (al-jumhūr) forbade saying so. Their evidence includes the Quranic verse in Surah al-Ra'd (13:14) that the supplication of disbelievers is only in error (ḍalāl). They reason that a disbeliever does not truly supplicate Allah because he does not know Him; even if he acknowledges His existence, he describes Him with inappropriate attributes, thus negating his acknowledgment. As for the hadith that the supplication of the oppressed, even if he is a disbeliever, is answered—they interpret it as referring to ingratitude for blessings (kufrān al-niʿma), not disbelief in God.

Conversely, some scholars allowed saying that a disbeliever's supplication may be answered. They cite the story of Iblis in Surah al-Hijr (15:36-37), where Iblis asked for respite and Allah granted it, calling that a response (ijāba). Among those who held this view were Abu al-Qasim al-Hakim and Abu Nasr al-Dabusi. The author then notes that al-Sadr al-Shahid stated that the fatwa follows this permissive view, as recorded in Sharh al-Aqa'id. Thus, the passage presents both sides but indicates that the preferred legal opinion is the permissive one.

Key Terms
دعاء
صدق النية
حضور القلب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A supplication is answered just by reciting words without focus.
Correction: The hadith explicitly states that Allah does not answer supplication from a heedless heart.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in the passage, what is required for a supplication to be answered?
A) Loud voice
B) Certainty of response
C) Many repetitions
D) Group gathering

Key Takeaway
Sincerity, inner purity, and heartfelt certainty are essential for a supplication to be answered.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you make du'a, do you truly believe that Allah will respond, or are your words merely a habit? What would change if you prayed with absolute certainty?
?
Think of a du'a you have been making for a long time. Has your heart become weary? How can you revive the presence of your heart, knowing that Allah does not answer from a heedless heart?
?
Are there supplications where your intention is mixed with showing off or wanting people to see you as pious? How can you purify your intention for Allah alone?

intermediate

The Ruling on Disbelievers' Supplication
Maydani presents the scholarly disagreement on whether disbelievers' supplication is answered.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly disagreement on whether the supplication of a disbeliever can be answered, and the evidence for each position.

Core Idea
Disbelievers' supplication is considered invalid by the majority, but some scholars permit it based on the story of Iblis.

After discussing conditions for answered supplication, Maydani addresses a debated question: Can the supplication of a disbeliever be answered? He presents the majority view forbidding saying so, and the minority view allowing it, concluding with the fatwa followed in practice.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the disagreement
Read the Arabic and translation from 'واختلف المشايخ' to the end.
2
Identify the two opinions
Note the majority opinion (منعه الجمهور) and the minority opinion (جوزه بعضهم). Also note the evidence each side uses.
3
Understand the hadith interpretation
The hadith about the oppressed disbeliever is interpreted differently. See how it is explained away by the majority.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage ends with al-Sadr al-Shahid stating that the fatwa follows the permissive view. What does this mean for practice?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن العمدة في ذلك صدق النية وخلوص الطوية وحضور القلب لقوله : ادْعُوا اللَّهَ وَأَنتُم مُوقِنُونَ بِالْإِجَابَةِ وَاعْلَمُوا أَنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى لَا يَسْتَجِيبُ الدُّعَاءَ مِنْ قَلْبِ غَافِلٍ. واختلف المشايخ في أنه هل يجوز أن يقال: يستجاب دعاء الكافرين؟ فمنعه الجمهور لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا دُعَاءُ الْكَافِرِينَ إِلَّا فِي ضَلَالٍ﴾ [سورة الرعد آية: ١٤]، ولأنه لا يدعو الله لأنه لا يعرفه؛ لأنه وإن أقر به فلما وصفه بما لا يليق به فقد نقض إقراره، وما روي في الحديث: «إِنَّ دَعْوَةَ المَظْلُومِ وَإِنْ كَانَ كَافِرًا تُسْتَجَابُ» محمول على كفران النعمة. وجوزه بعضهم لقوله تعالى حكاية عن إبليس: ﴿رَبِّ فَأَنْظِرْنِي﴾ [سورة الحجر آية: ٣٦]؛ فقال الله: ﴿فَإِنَّكَ مِنَ الْمُنْظَرِينَ﴾ [سورة الحجر آية: ٣٧]؛ هذه إجابة، وإليه ذهب أبو القاسم الحكيم وأبو نصر الدبوسي؛ قال الصدر الشهيد: وبه يفتى. كذا في شرح العقائد.
And know that the foundation in that is sincerity of intention, purity of inner self, and presence of heart, due to his saying: 'Call upon Allah while being certain of the response, and know that Allah does not answer the supplication from a heedless heart.' And the scholars disagreed about whether it is permissible to say: 'The supplication of disbelievers is answered.' The majority forbade it due to His saying: 'And the supplication of the disbelievers is only in error' [Surah al-Ra'd, verse 14], and because he does not supplicate Allah since he does not know Him; for even if he acknowledges Him, when he describes Him with what is not befitting, he has nullified his acknowledgment. And what is related in the hadith: 'Indeed, the supplication of the oppressed, even if he is a disbeliever, is answered' is interpreted as [referring to] ingratitude for blessings. And some permitted it due to His saying, narrating about Iblis: 'My Lord, then give me respite' [Surah al-Hijr, verse 36]; so Allah said: 'Then indeed you are of those given respite' [Surah al-Hijr, verse 37]; this is a response. And this view was held by Abu al-Qasim al-Hakim and Abu Nasr al-Dabusi. Al-Sadr al-Shahid said: 'And with it is the fatwa.' As in Sharh al-Aqa'id.
Source pages p. 181

Commentary
This passage is a combination of a directive and a legal discussion. First, the author states the key conditions for a supplication to be answered: sincerity of intention (ṣidq al-niyya), purity of inner self (khuṣūṣ al-ṭawiyya), and presence of heart (ḥuḍūr al-qalb). He supports this with a prophetic hadith quoting the Prophet ﷺ: 'Call upon Allah while being certain of the response, and know that Allah does not answer the supplication from a heedless heart.' This establishes that mere verbal invocation is insufficient; the heart must be engaged and certain.

Then the author moves to a scholastic disagreement (ikhtilāf al-mashāyikh): Is it permissible to say that the supplication of disbelievers (duʿāʾ al-kāfirīn) is answered? The majority (al-jumhūr) forbade saying so. Their evidence includes the Quranic verse in Surah al-Ra'd (13:14) that the supplication of disbelievers is only in error (ḍalāl). They reason that a disbeliever does not truly supplicate Allah because he does not know Him; even if he acknowledges His existence, he describes Him with inappropriate attributes, thus negating his acknowledgment. As for the hadith that the supplication of the oppressed, even if he is a disbeliever, is answered—they interpret it as referring to ingratitude for blessings (kufrān al-niʿma), not disbelief in God.

Conversely, some scholars allowed saying that a disbeliever's supplication may be answered. They cite the story of Iblis in Surah al-Hijr (15:36-37), where Iblis asked for respite and Allah granted it, calling that a response (ijāba). Among those who held this view were Abu al-Qasim al-Hakim and Abu Nasr al-Dabusi. The author then notes that al-Sadr al-Shahid stated that the fatwa follows this permissive view, as recorded in Sharh al-Aqa'id. Thus, the passage presents both sides but indicates that the preferred legal opinion is the permissive one.

Key Terms
كافر
استجابة
جمهور
إبليس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If a disbeliever's supplication is answered, that means Allah approves of his disbelief.
Correction: The passage shows that even Iblis was granted respite without approval; answering does not imply approval.

Checkpoint
What evidence do the majority (الجمهور) use to forbid saying that a disbeliever's supplication is answered?
A) Hadith of the Prophet
B) Quran verse 13:14
C) Story of Iblis
D) Consensus of the Sahaba

Key Takeaway
The majority view forbids saying that a disbeliever's supplication is answered, but the preferred fatwa permits it based on the story of Iblis.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the story of Iblis asking for respite and Allah granting it, do you ever catch yourself making similar bargains with Allah — asking for something while knowing you intend to persist in something He has forbidden? This lesson forces you to ask: what is the state of your heart when you make du'a? Are you truly acknowledging Allah as He deserves, or do you approach Him carelessly, expecting an answer while you remain in disobedience? Examine the sincerity of your own prayers.
?
The majority argued that a disbeliever's supplication is not truly directed to Allah because he does not know Him. Consider your own knowledge of Allah. Are you asking with deep ma'rifa (knowledge), or are you just reciting words? Is your du'a a real conversation with the One you know intimately, or is it a wish list thrown to a vague deity? This lesson should make you confront: how well do you really know the One you are calling upon?
?
If Allah can answer the supplication of Iblis — the one who defied Him openly — what does that mean for you, a believer? Does it make you more hopeful or more fearful? But here is the real question: are you taking advantage of Allah's generosity while living in a way that would put you in the ranks of those who don't truly acknowledge Him? Reflect on a specific area where you have been asking Allah for change but have not changed yourself. What will you do today to align your actions with your du'a?

Scriptural Evidence for Loving the Companions
Lists Quranic verses and a hadith urging love for the companions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scriptural basis for the obligation to love the Companions of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him), as established in the Quran and hadith.

Core Idea
Loving the Companions is loving the Prophet, and harming them is harming Allah.

This passage compiles Quranic verses and a prophetic hadith that collectively establish the duty to love the Companions. The evidence ranges from descriptions of their virtues to warnings against harming them, showing that their status is divinely ordained. As we read through these texts, notice how each one reinforces the same central message: the Companions are to be honored and loved.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get a sense of the flow. Then read the translation. Note that the author begins with Quranic verses, then cites a hadith.
The passage uses the phrase 'شيء كثير' (many things) to indicate abundance of evidence.
2
Identify the three Quranic verses cited
Locate the three verses: Surah al-Fath (48:29), Surah al-Ma'idah (5:54), and Surah al-Hashr (59:8). Each highlights different virtues of the Companions.
Surah al-Hashr verse is cited partially; the full verse praises the emigrants.
3
Analyze the hadith from al-Tirmidhi
Read the hadith carefully. Notice the chain of causation: loving Companions = love for Prophet; hating them = hatred for Prophet; harming them = harming Allah. This escalates the seriousness.
The hadith is from 'Abdullah ibn Mughaffal and is considered hasan by some scholars.
4
Reflect on the theological implications
Consider how these texts establish love for the Companions as a religious duty. The hadith explicitly links harming them to harming Allah, which implies a severe warning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد ورد في الحث على حبهم من الآيات القرآنية والأحاديث النبوية شيء كثير كقوله تعالى: (مُحَمَّدٌ رَسُولُ اللهِ وَالَّذِينَ مَعَهُ أَشِدَّاهُ عَلَى الْكُفَّارِ رُحَمَاهُ بَيْنَهُمْ تَرَنهُمْ رُكَّعًا سُجَّدًا يَبْتَغُونَ فَضْلًا مِّنَ اللَّهِ وَرِضْوَانًا .... إلى وأَجْرًا عظِيمًا) [سورة الفتح آية: (۲۹)، وقوله تعالى: (فَسَوْفَ يَأْتِي اللَّهُ بِقَوْمٍ تُحِهُمْ وَيُحِبُّونَهُ أَذِلَّةٍ عَلَى الْمُؤْمِنِينَ أَعِزَّةٍ عَلَى الْكَفِرِينَ مُجْتَهِدُونَ فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ وَلَا تَخَافُونَ لَوْمَةَ لأيمية ... الآية (سورة المائدة آية: ٥٤)، وقوله: لِلْفُقَرَاءِ الْمُهَجِرِينَ)... إلى قوله: هُمُ الصَّدِقُونَ ﴾ [سورة الحشر آية: (۸)، وإلى غير ذلك من الآيات، وروى الترمذي عن عبدالله بن مغفل قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «الله اللهَ فِي أَصْحَابِ لَا تَتَّخِذُوهُم فَرَضًا بَعْدِي فَمَنْ أَحَبَّهُمْ فَبِحُبِّي أَحَبَّهُمْ وَمَنْ أَبْغَضَهُم فَيُغْضِي أَبْغَضَهُمْ وَمَنْ آذَاهُم فَقَدْ آذَانِ وَمَنْ آذَانِ فَقَدْ آذَى اللهَ وَمَنْ آذَى اللهَ يُوشِكُ أَنْ يَأْخُذَهُ) (١)
And indeed there has come in urging love for them from the Quranic verses and prophetic hadiths many things, such as His statement (Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah, and those who are with him are severe against the disbelievers, merciful among themselves; you see them bowing and prostrating, seeking bounty from Allah and [His] pleasure ... to a great reward) [Surah al-Fath, verse 29], and His statement (Soon Allah will bring a people whom He loves and they love Him, humble towards the believers, stern towards the disbelievers, striving in the way of Allah and not fearing the blame of any blamer ...) [Surah al-Ma'idah, verse 54], and His statement (For the poor emigrants ... to His statement: they are the truthful) [Surah al-Hashr, verse 8], and other verses. And al-Tirmidhi narrated from 'Abdullah ibn Mughaffal that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'Fear Allah regarding my companions; do not take them as targets after me. Whoever loves them loves them out of love for me; whoever hates them hates them out of hatred for me; whoever harms them has harmed Allah; whoever harms Allah, He is about to seize him.' (1)
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage is a compilation of scriptural evidence for the obligation to love the companions of the Prophet. The author first cites several Quranic verses: Surah al-Fath 48:29 describes the qualities of the companions; Surah al-Ma'idah 5:54 mentions a future people beloved to Allah, often interpreted as the companions; Surah al-Hashr 59:8 praises the poor emigrants. Then a hadith from al-Tirmidhi from 'Abdullah ibn Mughaffal is quoted, wherein the Prophet commands fear of Allah regarding his companions and warns against taking them as targets. The hadith emphasizes that love for the companions is love for the Prophet, and hatred for them is hatred for him, and harming them is harming Allah. This establishes that loving the Sahaba is a religious duty.

Key Terms

آيات
أحاديث
آذى الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think loving the Companions is optional or merely recommended.
Correction: The hadith shows it is directly linked to love for the Prophet and even Allah, making it obligatory to love them and forbidden to harm them.

Checkpoint
What does the hadith from al-Tirmidhi say about those who harm the companions?
A) They will be forgiven if they repent.
B) They have harmed Allah.
C) They are still believers.
D) They will be punished only if they die unrepentant.

Key Takeaway
Loving the Companions is an integral part of faith, as it is directly linked to love for the Prophet and Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a negative comment about a Companion, do you feel a protective love rise in your heart, or do you find yourself indifferent? This lesson reminds you that your reaction reveals your connection to the Prophet. Will you commit to guarding your heart against any trace of dislike for them starting today?
?
The hadith says: 'Whoever harms them has harmed Allah.' Think of a time you spoke carelessly about a Companion or allowed a doubt about them to linger. How can you seek forgiveness and rectify your attitude now?
?
Do you love the Companions with the same intensity that the Prophet demanded? Or is your love merely intellectual? This lesson calls you to actively love them—would you be willing to defend their honor in a conversation? Why or why not?
