The Interpretive Methodology for Disputes Among Companions
The author states the principle of silence and quotes Ibn Daqiq's method for handling reports of disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the principle of remaining silent about disputes among the Companions and the proper method of interpreting authentic reports about them.

Core Idea
Silence and good interpretation protect the Companions' honor.

This lesson covers the foundational approach to conflicts reported among the Sahaba. The author advocates silence regarding what occurred, because those events stemmed from ijtihad. He then presents Ibn Daqiq al-'Id's principle: false reports are ignored, authentic ones are interpreted favorably, because Allah's prior praise takes precedence over later doubtful reports.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once carefully, then the translation. Let the author's words establish the framework before analysis.
Notice the sequence: silence → ijtihad → Ibn Daqiq's quote.
2
Understand the principle of silence
The author states 'we remain silent' about what occurred. Why? Because those events were the result of ijtihad. This implies that the Companions are not blameworthy even if they erred.
Ijtihad means independent reasoning; it is a valid basis for action.
3
Examine Ibn Daqiq's categorization
Ibn Daqiq divides reports into false (ignored) and authentic (interpreted favorably). Identify this division in the text.
Authentic reports must be given a good interpretation (ta'wil hasan).
4
Connect to the Quranic praise
The rationale: Allah's prior praise of the Companions (e.g., 'pleased with them') is certain and takes precedence over later uncertain reports.
This is a key principle in resolving apparent contradictions.
5
Grasp why doubtful reports don't override certainty
The passage concludes that doubtful or imaginary accounts cannot nullify what is certain and known about the Companions' virtue.
This protects their reputation from baseless allegations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ونسكت عن ذكر ما وقع بينهم فإنه الذي أدى إليه اجتهادهم، قال ابن دقيق العيد في عقيدته: وما نقل فيما بينهم واختلفوا فيه فمنه باطل وكذب فلا يلتفت إليه، وما كان صحيحا أولناه تأويلا حسنا؛ لأن الثناء عليهم من الله تعالى سابق وما نقل من الكلام اللاحق محتمل للتأويل، والمشكوك والموهوم لا يبطل المحقق والمعلوم اهـ. وبغير الحق لا نذكرهم؛ ففي صحيح الإمام مسلم: «لَا تَسُبُّوا أَصْحَابِي فَوَالَّذِي نَفْسِي بِيَدِهِ لَوْ أَنْفَقَ أَحَدُكُمْ مِثْلَ أُحُدٍ ذَهَبًا مَا بَلَغَ مُدَّ أَحَدِهِمْ وَلَا نَصِيفَهُ»، وعن ابن عباس: لا تسبوا أصحاب محمد فلمقام أحدهم ساعة يعني مع النبي - خير من عمل أحدكم أربعين سنة، وفي رواية عمره. ونرى حبهم دينا وإيمانا وإحسانا و نرى بغضهم كفرًا وشقاقا ونفاقا وطغيانا؛ حيث كان حبهم من حبه وبغضهم من بغضه مع شهادته لهم بالخيرية.
And we remain silent about mentioning what occurred among them, for it was that which their ijtihad led to. Ibn Daqiq al-'Id said in his creed: 'What has been transmitted regarding what happened among them and they differed about—some of it is false and a lie, so no attention is paid to it. And what is authentic, we interpret it in a good way, because the commendation of them from Allah, the Most High, is prior, and what has been transmitted of later speech is subject to interpretation. And what is doubtful and imaginary does not nullify what is certain and known.' End quote. And we do not mention them except with the truth. For in Sahih Muslim: 'Do not curse my Companions, for by the One in Whose hand is my soul, if one of you were to spend the equivalent of Mount Uhud in gold, it would not reach the measure of a handful of one of them, nor even half of that.' And from Ibn 'Abbas: 'Do not curse the Companions of Muhammad, for the station of one of them for an hour—meaning with the Prophet—is better than the deeds of one of you for forty years.' And in another narration: 'his lifetime.' And we consider love for them to be religion, faith, and righteousness, and we consider hatred for them to be disbelief, dissension, hypocrisy, and transgression, because love for them is from love for him and hatred for them is from hatred for him, while he testified to their goodness.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage provides the methodological principle for handling reports of disputes among the Companions. The author begins by stating that we remain silent about what happened between them, because those events were the result of their ijtihad (independent reasoning). He then quotes Ibn Daqiq al-'Id's creed: reports about the Companions' conflicts are either false and should be ignored, or authentic but subject to favorable interpretation. The reason is that Allah's prior praise of them (in the Quran) establishes their virtue, and later reports (al-kalam al-lahiq) that seem negative are open to interpretation. Doubtful or imaginary accounts cannot overturn certain knowledge of their goodness. The author then cites a hadith from Sahih Muslim prohibiting cursing the Companions and extolling their immense merit: even spending gold like Mount Uhud cannot match the reward of a Companion's moment with the Prophet. A saying of Ibn 'Abbas reinforces this: the Companions' brief company with the Prophet surpasses forty years of worship by later Muslims. In the final sentence, the author makes a strong doctrinal statement: love for the Companions is a part of religion (din), faith (iman), and righteousness (ihsan), while hatred for them is disbelief (kufr), dissension (shiqaq), hypocrisy (nifaq), and transgression (tughyan). This is because the Prophet himself testified to their goodness, so loving them follows from loving him, and hating them follows from hating him.

Key Terms
الاجتهاد
التأويل
الثناء السابق
الكلام اللاحق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All reports of disputes among the Sahaba must be accepted literally and used to determine fault.
Correction: The author asserts that authentic reports should be interpreted favorably, and false ones ignored, due to the primacy of divine praise.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Daqiq, what should be done with authentic reports of disputes among the Companions?
A) Accept them literally
B) Interpret them favorably
C) Reject them entirely
D) Use them to criticize

Key Takeaway
Authentic reports of Companions' disputes must be interpreted favorably, honoring Allah's prior praise of them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a story that casts a Companion in a negative light, do you immediately feel a sense of doubt about their character? What does this lesson demand you do instead, and what will you actually do the next time you encounter such a report?
?
Allah’s prior praise of the Companions is certain and settled. Is there any area of your faith where you allow doubtful reports or whispers to shake what you know to be true from the Qur’an and Sunnah? How will you apply Ibn Daqiq’s principle of ‘doubt cannot nullify certainty’ to your own heart?
?
The lesson teaches silence and good interpretation to protect honor. Think of a person you know (or a group) whose honor is established. Are you quick to believe negative accounts about them? What would it mean for you to adopt the same ‘good interpretation’ attitude toward them as you do for the Companions? Commit to one specific change.

The Ruling on Loving and Hating the Companions
The author cites hadith and a companion's saying to demonstrate the virtue of the Sahaba, then gives the ruling on loving/hating them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that loving the Companions is part of faith and hating them is a sign of hypocrisy and disbelief.

Core Idea
Loving the Sahaba is religion; hating them is kufr.

After establishing the proper stance toward disputes, the author moves to a stronger doctrinal point: our attitude toward the Companions defines our faith. Citing hadith and a saying of Ibn 'Abbas, he shows their immense virtue. Then he declares that loving them is an act of faith, while hating them is disbelief, because the Prophet testified to their goodness.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and Ibn 'Abbas's statement
Read the hadith from Sahih Muslim that prohibits cursing the Companions and highlights their unmatched virtue. Then read Ibn 'Abbas's comparison.
Notice the hyperbolic comparison to emphasize their status.
2
Understand the prohibition of cursing
The hadith explicitly says 'Do not curse my Companions.' This is a clear prohibition. The reason given is their immense merit.
Cursing includes any form of insult or vilification.
3
Grasp the incomparable virtue of the Sahaba
The hadith states that even spending gold like Mount Uhud cannot match a handful given by a Companion. Ibn 'Abbas says an hour with the Prophet is better than forty years of worship.
This shows the unique honor of being a Companion.
4
Internalize the theological ruling
The author concludes: love for them = din, iman, ihsan; hatred for them = kufr, shiqaq, nifaq, tughyan. This is because the Prophet testified to their goodness.
Hatred of the Sahaba is a sign of hypocrisy and disbelief.

Source Text

ونسكت عن ذكر ما وقع بينهم فإنه الذي أدى إليه اجتهادهم، قال ابن دقيق العيد في عقيدته: وما نقل فيما بينهم واختلفوا فيه فمنه باطل وكذب فلا يلتفت إليه، وما كان صحيحا أولناه تأويلا حسنا؛ لأن الثناء عليهم من الله تعالى سابق وما نقل من الكلام اللاحق محتمل للتأويل، والمشكوك والموهوم لا يبطل المحقق والمعلوم اهـ. وبغير الحق لا نذكرهم؛ ففي صحيح الإمام مسلم: «لَا تَسُبُّوا أَصْحَابِي فَوَالَّذِي نَفْسِي بِيَدِهِ لَوْ أَنْفَقَ أَحَدُكُمْ مِثْلَ أُحُدٍ ذَهَبًا مَا بَلَغَ مُدَّ أَحَدِهِمْ وَلَا نَصِيفَهُ»، وعن ابن عباس: لا تسبوا أصحاب محمد فلمقام أحدهم ساعة يعني مع النبي - خير من عمل أحدكم أربعين سنة، وفي رواية عمره. ونرى حبهم دينا وإيمانا وإحسانا و نرى بغضهم كفرًا وشقاقا ونفاقا وطغيانا؛ حيث كان حبهم من حبه وبغضهم من بغضه مع شهادته لهم بالخيرية.
And we remain silent about mentioning what occurred among them, for it was that which their ijtihad led to. Ibn Daqiq al-'Id said in his creed: 'What has been transmitted regarding what happened among them and they differed about—some of it is false and a lie, so no attention is paid to it. And what is authentic, we interpret it in a good way, because the commendation of them from Allah, the Most High, is prior, and what has been transmitted of later speech is subject to interpretation. And what is doubtful and imaginary does not nullify what is certain and known.' End quote. And we do not mention them except with the truth. For in Sahih Muslim: 'Do not curse my Companions, for by the One in Whose hand is my soul, if one of you were to spend the equivalent of Mount Uhud in gold, it would not reach the measure of a handful of one of them, nor even half of that.' And from Ibn 'Abbas: 'Do not curse the Companions of Muhammad, for the station of one of them for an hour—meaning with the Prophet—is better than the deeds of one of you for forty years.' And in another narration: 'his lifetime.' And we consider love for them to be religion, faith, and righteousness, and we consider hatred for them to be disbelief, dissension, hypocrisy, and transgression, because love for them is from love for him and hatred for them is from hatred for him, while he testified to their goodness.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage provides the methodological principle for handling reports of disputes among the Companions. The author begins by stating that we remain silent about what happened between them, because those events were the result of their ijtihad (independent reasoning). He then quotes Ibn Daqiq al-'Id's creed: reports about the Companions' conflicts are either false and should be ignored, or authentic but subject to favorable interpretation. The reason is that Allah's prior praise of them (in the Quran) establishes their virtue, and later reports (al-kalam al-lahiq) that seem negative are open to interpretation. Doubtful or imaginary accounts cannot overturn certain knowledge of their goodness. The author then cites a hadith from Sahih Muslim prohibiting cursing the Companions and extolling their immense merit: even spending gold like Mount Uhud cannot match the reward of a Companion's moment with the Prophet. A saying of Ibn 'Abbas reinforces this: the Companions' brief company with the Prophet surpasses forty years of worship by later Muslims. In the final sentence, the author makes a strong doctrinal statement: love for the Companions is a part of religion (din), faith (iman), and righteousness (ihsan), while hatred for them is disbelief (kufr), dissension (shiqaq), hypocrisy (nifaq), and transgression (tughyan). This is because the Prophet himself testified to their goodness, so loving them follows from loving him, and hating them follows from hating him.

Key Terms
سب الصحابة
حب الصحابة
بغض الصحابة
الشهادة بالخيرية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: It is acceptable to criticize or curse some Companions based on their actions in disputes.
Correction: The hadith prohibits cursing any Companion, and their virtue outweighs any sin, so hatred is classified as disbelief.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith in Sahih Muslim, what is the comparison made regarding spending gold?
A) The Prophet's reward is greater
B) A Companion's charity outweighs that of later Muslims
C) Spending like Uhud cannot match a handful from a Companion
D) Only the Sahaba can give charity

Key Takeaway
Loving the Companions is a sign of faith, while hating them is a sign of hypocrisy and disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of the Companions, do you feel genuine love and gratitude, or have you allowed even a trace of resentment or indifference to settle in your heart? How does this lesson expose that hidden attitude?
?
If loving the Companions is a direct reflection of your love for the Prophet, what does your inner state toward the Sahaba say about the sincerity of your claim to love him? Will you seek to purify that love today?
?
The Prophet testified to the goodness of every Companion. Do you fully accept his testimony without exception, or do you secretly hold personal judgments that contradict it? What step will you take to align your heart with his testimony?

The Superiority of Prophets over Awliya'
Imam al-Tahawi states that no wali is better than a prophet, and the commentator explains the reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic doctrine that prophets are superior to awliya', the reasons for this superiority, and the refutation of the deviant opinion that a wali could be better than a prophet.

Core Idea
One prophet is better than all awliya' combined.

Imam al-Tahawi makes a clear declaration in his creed: no wali (saint) is equal to a prophet, let alone superior. This lesson unpacks that statement, explaining why prophets hold a unique rank and why any claim that a wali could surpass a prophet is rejected as disbelief.

Guided Path
1
Read the original statement
Begin by reading the Arabic passage from Imam al-Tahawi's creed. Notice the direct and unambiguous language: 'We do not prefer any wali over any prophet, and we say: one prophet is better than all awliya'.'
The statement also affirms belief in the karamat (miracles) of awliya' as reported by trustworthy narrators.
2
Understand the reasoning
The commentator gives the reasons: prophets are ma'sumun (protected from sin), secure from a bad end, honored with revelation and witnessing angels, and tasked with conveying divine rulings after attaining the perfections of awliya'.
This explains why prophets are inherently superior.
3
Reflect on the refutation
The passage explicitly refutes the Karramiyya sect's claim that a wali could be better than a prophet, labeling it as disbelief and misguidance.
This shows the gravity of deviating from this doctrine.
4
Consider the nuance
The commentator notes that there may be hesitation about whether the rank of prophethood or walaya is higher, but emphasizes that a prophet combines both ranks and is definitely superior to any non-prophet wali.
This nuance prevents confusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في الأولياء] وَلَا نُفَضِّلُ أَحَدًا مِنَ الْأَوْلِيَاءِ عَلَى أَحَدٍ مِنَ الأَنْبِيَاءِ، وَنَقُولُ: نَبِيٌّ وَاحِدٌ أَفْضَلُ مِنْ جَمِيعِ الأَوْلِيَاءِ، وَنُؤْمِنُ بِمَا جَاءَ مِنْ كَرَامَاتِهِمْ وَصَحَ عَنِ الثَّقَاتِ مِنْ رُوَايَتِهِمْ. ) ولا نفضل أحدا من الأولياء) ( على أحد من الأنبياء صلوات الله تعالى عليهم (ونقول نبي واحد أفضل من جميع الأولياء)؛ لأن الأنبياء معصومون مأمونون عن خوف الخاتمة، مكرمون بالوحي ومشاهدة الملك، ومأمورون بتبليغ الأحكام والإرشاد للأنام بعد الاتصاف بكمالات الأولياء؛ فما نقل عن بعض الكرامية من جواز كون الولي أفضل من النبي كفر وضلال نعم قد يقع تردد في أن مرتبة النبوة أفضل أم مرتبة الولاية بعد القطع بأن النبي متصف بالمرتبتين وأنه أفضل من الولي الذي ليس بنبي. كذا في شرح العقائد.
And we do not prefer anyone from the awliya' over anyone from the prophets, and we say: one prophet is better than all the awliya'. And we believe in what has come of their karamat and what has been authenticated from trustworthy narrators of their narrations. (And we do not prefer anyone of the awliya') (over anyone of the prophets, peace and blessings of Allah be upon them) (and we say one prophet is better than all the awliya'); because the prophets are protected (ma'sumun), secure from fear of the end, honored with revelation and witnessing the angel, and commanded to convey the rulings and guide the people after being described with the perfections of the awliya'; thus what has been reported from some of the Karramiyya that a wali may be better than a prophet is disbelief and misguidance. Yes, there may be hesitation regarding whether the rank of prophethood is better or the rank of walaya, after being certain that the prophet is described with both ranks and that he is better than the wali who is not a prophet. Thus in Sharh al-Aqa'id.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the Tahawiyyah statement regarding the status of awliya' compared to prophets. The commentator begins by repeating the matn: 'We do not prefer any wali over any prophet, and we say one prophet is better than all awliya'.' Then he provides the rationale: prophets are ma'sumun (protected from sin), secure from a bad end, honored with revelation and the sight of angels, and tasked with conveying divine rulings and guiding creation after they themselves have attained the perfections of awliya'. The commentator then refutes the claim of some Karramiyya sect that a wali could be superior to a prophet, labeling it as kufr and dalal. He notes that there may be hesitation regarding whether prophethood or walaya is the higher rank, but there is no doubt that a prophet combines both ranks and is superior to any non-prophet wali. He concludes the section with a reference to Sharh al-Aqa'id.

Key Terms

أنبياء
معصومون
كرامة
كرامية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that a wali (saint) can be superior to a prophet in rank.
Correction: This passage clearly states that one prophet is better than all awliya', and any claim otherwise is disbelief and misguidance.

Checkpoint

A) Because they are more numerous
B) Because they are protected from sin and receive revelation
C) Because they perform more miracles
D) Because they are from the lineage of Quraysh

Key Takeaway
Prophets are superior to awliya' because they are ma'sumun, receive revelation, and are tasked with conveying divine guidance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You may revere certain awliya' for their karamat, but do you revere the Prophet (peace be upon him) as the one who brought the revelation? In your daily life, whose example do you actually follow more: a saint you admire or the Prophet's sunnah? Be honest.
?

?
The prophets are ma'sumun, secure from fear of the end. Are you secure in your end? If not, why are you not clinging to the teachings of the prophets as your only hope? What practical step will you take today to strengthen your connection to the prophetic way?

Belief in the Signs of the Hour
Al-Tahawi defines belief in the signs of the Hour and enumerates key signs from prophetic hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that belief in the signs of the Hour is an integral part of Islamic creed, based on authentic prophetic reports, and you will be familiar with the major signs mentioned in the hadith.

Core Idea
The signs of the Hour are real events we must believe in because the Prophet informed us.

Imam al-Tahawi includes belief in the signs of the Hour as part of the creed of Ahl al-Sunnah. These signs are specific events that will occur before the Day of Judgment, reported by the Prophet. This lesson presents the foundational belief and then lists the major signs as evidence that our faith is based on revelation, not speculation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the full translation. Let the author's rhythm and the hadith come through.
2
Identify the two parts
Notice that the passage has two main sections: the declaration of belief with four examples, and the hadith listing ten signs.
3
Understand the basis for belief
The commentator states these are 'possible matters reported by the Truthful One'—the Prophet. Reflect on why this makes belief obligatory.
It's a matter of trusting revelation.
4
Recognize the scope of belief
The commentator directs seekders to specialized books for details, showing that the core belief is in the general occurrence, not every detail.
5
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question and try the activity to solidify learning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَنُؤْمِنُ بِأَشْرَاطِ السَّاعَةِ وَمِنْهَا: خُرُوجُ الدَّجَّالِ وَنُزُولُ عِيسَى عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ مِنَ السَّمَاءِ، وَطُلُوعُ الشَّمْسِ مِنْ مَغْرِبِهَا وَخُرُوجُ دَابَّةِ الْأَرْضِ مِنْ مَوْضِعِهَا. ( ونؤمن بأشراط الساعة)؛ أي علاماتها؛ (ومنها: خروج الدجال ونزول عيسى عليه السلام من السماء وطلوع الشمس من مغربها وخروج دابة الأرض من موضعها؛ لأنها أمور ممكنة أخبر عنها الصادق قال حذيفة بن أسيد الغفاري اطلع علينا النبي ونحن نتذاكر فقال: «مَا تَذَاكَرُونَ؟» قالوا: نذكر الساعة، قال: «إِنَّهَا لَنْ تَقُومَ حَتَّى تَرَوْا قَبْلَهَا عَشْرَ آياتٍ؛ فذكر الدخان والدجال والدابة وطلوع الشمس من مغربها ونزول عيسى بن مريم ويأجوج ومأجوج وثلاث خسوفات خسف بالمشرق وخسف بالمغرب، وخسف بجزيرة العرب وآخر ذلك نار تخرج من اليمن تطرد الناس إلى محشر هم) ، والأحاديث الصحاح في هذه الأشراط كثيرة جدا، وقد روي أحاديث وآثار في تفاصيلها وكيفياتها؛ فليطلب من كتب التفسير والسير والتواريخ كذا في شرح العقائد (۳).
And we believe in the signs of the Hour, and among them are: the emergence of the Dajjal, the descent of Jesus (peace be upon him) from the sky, the rising of the sun from its west, and the emergence of the Beast of the Earth from its place. (And we believe in the signs of the Hour) i.e., its markers; (and among them: the emergence of the Dajjal, the descent of Jesus (peace be upon him) from the sky, the rising of the sun from its west, and the emergence of the Beast of the Earth from its place) because they are possible matters reported by the Truthful One. Hudhayfa ibn Usayd al-Ghifari said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) came out to us while we were discussing and said: 'What are you discussing?' They said: We are mentioning the Hour. He said: 'It will not come until you see before it ten signs.' Then he mentioned the smoke, the Dajjal, the Beast, the rising of the sun from its west, the descent of Jesus son of Mary, Gog and Magog, three sinkings: a sinking in the east, a sinking in the west, and a sinking in the Arabian Peninsula, and the last of that is a fire that comes out from Yemen driving the people to their gathering place. And the authentic hadiths concerning these signs are very many, and hadiths and reports have been narrated concerning their details and modalities; so let one seek them from the books of exegesis, biography, and history, as stated in Sharh al-ʿAqāʾid (3).
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof-text section. It begins with the original text of Imam al-Tahawi: 'And we believe in the signs of the Hour, and among them are: the emergence of the Dajjal, the descent of Jesus (peace be upon him) from the sky, the rising of the sun from its west, and the emergence of the Beast of the Earth from its place.' The commentator then explains that 'signs' means markers, and these four are mentioned as examples. He gives the reason for belief: they are possible matters reported by the Truthful One, i.e., the Prophet (peace be upon him). Then he cites the hadith of Hudhayfa ibn Usayd al-Ghifari in which the Prophet enumerated ten major signs: the smoke, the Dajjal, the Beast, the rising of the sun from the west, the descent of Jesus, Gog and Magog, three sinkings (east, west, Arabian Peninsula), and a fire from Yemen that drives people to the gathering place. The commentator notes that authentic hadiths on these signs are abundant, and details can be found in books of tafsir, sirah, and history. Thus, the passage establishes the obligation of believing in the signs of the Hour based on divine revelation and authentic prophetic reports.

نزول عيسى عليه السلام
طلوع الشمس من مغربها
دابة الأرض

الخسوفات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One must know every detail about the signs of the Hour to be a believer.
Correction: The passage shows that belief in the signs as reported is sufficient; details are additional knowledge that can be sought from books.

Checkpoint

D) Twelve

Key Takeaway
Believing in the signs of the Hour is an article of faith based on authentic prophetic reports; the major signs are known from the hadith and include the Dajjal, descent of Jesus, sun rising from the west, the Beast, Gog and Magog, three sinkings, and a fire.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Seeing Allah and the Method of Tafwid
Imam Tahawi affirms the vision of Allah without modality and explains the method of tafwid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Islamic belief in seeing Allah in the afterlife without modality and the method of tafwid (consigning ambiguous matters to Allah).

Core Idea
Believers will see Allah in Paradise, but we affirm without specifying how.

Imam Tahawi affirms a key belief of Ahl al-Sunnah: the vision of Allah for believers in Paradise. However, he immediately adds two vital restrictions: without encompassing (ihata) and without modality (kayfiyya). Moreover, he teaches us the correct approach to such texts: to accept them as they are and consign their true meaning to Allah, a method known as tafwid.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get the rhythm. Then read the translation. Notice the key terms: الرؤية, الكيفية, الإحاطة, التسليم, التأويل.
Pay attention to the Qur'anic proof and the concluding statement about submission.
2
Identify the two restrictions on ru'ya
Find the two conditions Imam Tahawi places on seeing Allah: without encompassing (إحاطة) and without modality (كيفية). Understand why these restrictions matter.
This guards against anthropomorphism (tashbih) and denial (ta'til).
3
Understand the methodology of tafwid
Read the part about 'لا ندخل في ذلك متأولين...' and note how we should not interpret based on opinion or desire. The correct approach is to submit and refer knowledge to Allah.
This is the method of tafwid: consigning the true meaning to Allah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالرُّؤْيَةُ حَقٌّ لِأَهْلِ الْجَنَّةِ بِغَيْرِ إِحَاطَةٍ وَلَا كَيْفِيَّةٍ كَمَا نَطَقَ بِهِ كِتَابُ رَبِّنَا حَيْثُ قَالَ: وُجُوهٌ يَوْمَئِذٍ نَاضِرَةٌ إِلَى رَبِّهَا نَاظِرَةٌ [سورة القيامة آية: ٢٢-٢٣] وَتَفْسِيرُهُ عَلَى مَا أَرَادَهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى وَعَلِمَهُ، وَكُلُّ مَا جَاءَ فِي ذَلِكَ مِنَ الحَدِيثِ الصَّحِيحِ عَنْ رَسُولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَعَنْ أَصْحَابِهِ رُضْوَانُ اللهِ عَلَيْهِمْ أَجْمَعِينَ فَهُوَ كَمَا قَالَ، وَمَعْنَاهُ وَتَفْسِيرُهُ عَلَى مَا أَرَادَ، لَا نَدْخُلُ فِي ذَلِكَ مُتَأَوِّلِينَ بِآرَائِنَا وَلَا مُتَوَهِّمِينَ بِأَهْوَائِنَا؛ فَإِنَّهُ مَا سَلِمَ فِي دِينِهِ إِلَّا مَنْ سَلَّمَ لِلَّهِ تَعَالَى وَلِرَسُولِهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَرَدَّ عِلْمَ مَا اشْتَبَهَ عَلَيْهِ إِلَى عَالِمِهِ.
And the vision (ru'ya) is true for the people of Paradise, without encompassing and without modality, as the Book of our Lord has spoken where He said: 'Faces on that day are radiant, looking at their Lord' [Surah Al-Qiyamah, verses 22-23]. And its interpretation is as Allah intended and knows. And everything that has come in that regard from authentic hadith of the Messenger of Allah and his Companions, may Allah be pleased with them all, is as they said, and its meaning and interpretation is as He intended. We do not enter into that by interpreting with our opinions nor by speculating with our desires. For nothing saves one in his religion except one who submits to Allah and His Messenger and refers the knowledge of what is ambiguous to its Knower.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage affirms the reality of seeing Allah (ru'ya) for the people of Paradise, but with two restrictions: بدون إحاطة (without encompassing) and لا كيفية (without modality). The proof is the Qur'anic verse: 'وجوه يومئذ ناضرة إلى ربها ناظرة' (Faces on that day are radiant, looking at their Lord). Then Imam Tahawi explains the correct approach to such texts: their interpretation is as Allah intended and knows. All authentic hadith on this topic are to be accepted as they came, without delving into interpretation (تأويل) based on personal opinion or speculation (تأويل بآرائنا ولا متوهمين بأهوائنا). He concludes that salvation lies in submitting to Allah and His Messenger and referring ambiguous matters back to the One who knows them (عالمها). This is the method of tafwid (consigning the meaning to Allah).

Key Terms
الرؤية
الكيفية
الإحاطة
التسليم
التأويل
التفويض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some deny the vision of Allah (ru'ya) or interpret it metaphorically, claiming it is impossible or that it implies corporeality.
Correction: This passage affirms ru'ya as true for believers, but without modality or encompassing, thus avoiding both denial and anthropomorphism.

Checkpoint
How does the passage say we should understand the hadith about seeing Allah?
A) Interpret them metaphorically.
B) Accept them as they are and refer their meaning to Allah.
C) Only accept Qur'an, not hadith.
D) Deny them because they are unclear.

Key Takeaway
Seeing Allah in Paradise is true, but we only affirm it as Allah and His Messenger described, without interpretation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a divine attribute like ru'ya that you cannot fully comprehend, does your heart immediately surrender with 'Allah knows best,' or does it try to rationalize and explain it away? What does your reaction reveal about your trust in Allah's words?
?
The passage says safety lies in submission (taslim). Is there any area of your faith where you struggle to submit, where you prefer to rely on your own reasoning? Will you today commit to referring that matter back to its Knower and abandon speculation?
?
Imagine standing before Allah on the Day of Judgment being asked about your beliefs regarding His attributes. Would you be able to say, 'I affirmed what You and Your Messenger said, without interpretation and without desire'? What changes do you need to make now to ensure that answer is true?

Faith in Seeing Allah Requires Tafwid
Tahawi rules on valid faith in ru'ya and defines its correct approach.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the correct belief in seeing Allah (ru'ya) requires abandoning interpretation and practicing tafwid (submission).

Core Idea
True faith in seeing Allah means not interpreting it — only submitting.

Imam Tahawi now addresses a critical aspect of belief in the vision of Allah: how to avoid falling into error. Many assume that to protect God's transcendence, they must interpret the ru'ya metaphorically. But Tahawi teaches the opposite: the correct 'interpretation' is to abandon interpretation and submit. This is the path of all prophets.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the strong negation at the beginning and the paradoxical statement that the interpretation is to abandon interpretation.
Pay attention to the key terms: الرؤية, التأويل, التسليم.
2
Identify the condition for valid faith
The passage states that faith in ru'ya is not valid for those who rely on imagination (وهم) or interpretation (تأويل) based on human understanding. Ask yourself why these are invalid.
This is the main point: faith requires submission, not mental grasping.
3
Understand the 'interpretation' of divine attributes
Tahawi says that the correct تأويل of ru'ya and all divine attributes is to abandon تأويل and adhere to التسليم. This is the Salafi position of tafwid.
This is the core of the lesson: the 'interpretation' is non-interpretation.
4
Connect to the prophets' way
The passage ends by affirming that this principle is the religion of all messengers and the laws of all prophets. This shows it is the universal, original teaching.
This grounds the lesson in the broader Islamic tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَصِحُّ الإِيمَانُ بِالرُّؤْيَةِ لِأَهْلِ دَارِ السَّلَامِ لِمَنِ اعْتَبَرَهَا مِنْهُمْ بِوَهْمٍ أَوْ تَأَوَّلَهَا بِفَهْمٍ، إِذْ كَانَ تَأْوِيلُ الرُّؤْيَةِ وَتَأْوِيلُ كُلِّ مَعْنًى يُضَافُ إِلَى الرُّبُوبِيَّةِ تَرْكَ التَّأْوِيلِ وَلُزُومَ التَّسْلِيمِ وَعَلَيْهِ دِينُ الْمُرْسَلِينَ وَشَرَائِعُ النَّبِيِّينَ.
And faith in the vision (ru'ya) for the people of the Abode of Peace (Paradise) is not valid for those who consider it through imagination or interpret it through understanding, since the interpretation of the vision and the interpretation of every meaning attributed to Lordship is to abandon interpretation and adhere to submission. And upon that is the religion of the messengers and the laws of the prophets.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage reinforces the correct belief regarding seeing Allah. Imam Tahawi states that faith in the ru'ya is not valid (لا يصح الإيمان بالرؤية) if one tries to conceptualize it through imagination (بوهْم) or interpret it through human understanding (تأولها بفهم). Rather, the proper interpretation (تأويل) of ru'ya and all divine attributes is to abandon interpretation (ترك التأويل) and adhere to submission (لزوم التسليم). This is the religion of all messengers (دين المرسلين) and the laws of all prophets (شرائع النبيين). This is a clear statement of the methodology of the Salaf: tafwid (consigning the meaning to Allah) without ta'til (denial) or tashbih (anthropomorphism).

Key Terms
الرؤية
التأويل
التسليم
التفويض
دين المرسلين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One must interpret the ru'ya metaphorically to avoid comparing Allah to creation.
Correction: The passage says the correct 'interpretation' is to abandon interpretation and submit, not to engage in metaphorical reinterpretation.

Checkpoint
What does the passage say is the correct 'interpretation' of the vision of Allah?
A) To interpret it metaphorically.
B) To abandon interpretation and submit.
C) To visualize it in one's mind.
D) To deny it.

Key Takeaway
True faith in seeing Allah requires abandoning all human interpretation and submitting to the divine text, following the way of all prophets.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about seeing Allah in the afterlife, do you find yourself forming mental images or trying to understand 'how' it will happen? This lesson says such imagination invalidates faith. Will you repent from that and submit to the unknown, trusting that His promise is true without needing to picture it?
?
In your daily recitation of the Quran, when you come across verses about Allah's hand, face, or other attributes, what is your immediate inner reaction? Do you feel the need to quickly explain them away with 'metaphor'? This lesson says the correct approach is to abandon interpretation and submit. How will you train your heart to do that from now on?
?
This passage says that the way of all prophets is to submit without interpretation. Is there any area of your faith where you are relying on your own reasoning or intellectual comfort rather than pure submission? What is one specific belief you will actively surrender to Allah today, even if you don't fully understand it?

The Reality of the Pool and Intercession
Affirms the reality of the Hawd and Shafa'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Ahl al-Sunnah affirms the reality of the Hawd (Pool) granted to the Prophet and the Shafa'ah (intercession) stored for the Ummah.

Core Idea
The Pool and Intercession are real blessings stored for the Prophet's Ummah.

The text begins by affirming two key eschatological realities: the Hawd (Pool) that Allah will provide for the Prophet's Ummah on the Day of Judgment, and the Shafa'ah (Intercession) that Allah has reserved. Both are confirmed in transmitted reports and are part of the beliefs of Ahl al-Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage affirming the Pool
Read the first sentence carefully, noting that it says the Hawd is true and that Allah honored the Prophet with it.
2
Read the passage affirming Intercession
Read the second part about Shafa'ah, noting it is stored as reported.
3
Reflect on the term 'true'
The text uses 'حق' for both, meaning they are real, not metaphorical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالحَوْضُ الَّذِي أَكْرَمَهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى بِهِ غِيَانًا لِأُمَّتِهِ حَقٌّ، وَالشَّفَاعَةُ الَّتِي ادَّخَرَهَا اللهُ لَمْ كَمَا رُوِي فِي الأَخْبَارِ، وَالمِيثَاقُ الَّذِي أَخَذَهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى مِنْ آدَمَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَذُرِّيَّتِهِ حَقٌّ. وَقَدْ عَلِمَ اللهُ تَعَالَى فِيمَا لَمْ يَزَلْ عَدَدَ مَنْ يَدْخُلُ الجَنَّةَ وَيَدْخُلُ النَّارَ جُمْلَةٌ وَاحِدَةً لَا يُزَادُ فِي ذَلِكَ العَدَدِ وَلَا يُنْقَصُ مِنْهُ، وَكَذَلِكَ أَفْعَالَهُمْ فِيمَا عَلِمَ مِنْهُمْ أَنَّهُمْ يَفْعَلُونَهُ، وَكُلٌ مُيَسَّرُ مَا خُلِقَ لَهُ. وَالأَعْمَالُ بِالخَوَانِمِ، وَالسَّعِيدُ مَنْ سَعِدَ بِقَضَاءِ اللَّه تَعَالَى وَالشَّفِيُّ مَنْ شَقِي بِقَضَاءِ الله تَعَالَى.
And the Pool which Allah Most High honored him with as a provision for his Ummah is true, and the intercession which Allah stored away for us as reported in the traditions is true, and the covenant which Allah Most High took from Adam, peace be upon him, and his offspring is true. And Allah Most High has always known the number of those who will enter Paradise and those who will enter Hell as one totality, nothing is added to that number nor subtracted from it. Similarly, their actions are as He knew from them that they would do. And everyone is facilitated to that for which he was created. And deeds are according to their endings. And the fortunate is the one who is fortunate by the decree of Allah Most High, and the wretched is the one who is wretched by the decree of Allah Most High.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage affirms several key beliefs of Ahl al-Sunnah. First, the reality of the Hawd (the Pool) that Allah will grant the Prophet as a provision for his Ummah on the Day of Judgment. Second, the reality of intercession (Shafa'ah) that Allah has stored for the Prophet as narrated in reports. Third, the reality of the covenant (Meethaq) taken from Adam and his descendants. Then it affirms that Allah's knowledge of who enters Paradise and Hell is eternal and unchanging; the number is fixed and does not increase or decrease. Likewise, He knows their actions before they do them. Then it states the principle that everyone is facilitated to what he was created for. Then it mentions that deeds are judged by their endings, and that one's felicity or misery is by Allah's decree.

Key Terms
الحوض
الشفاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the passage say about the Pool (الْحَوْض)?
A) It is a metaphor for knowledge.
B) It is true and a provision for the Ummah.
C) It is only for the Prophet.
D) It is not mentioned.

Key Takeaway
The Pool and Intercession are real blessings that Allah has prepared for the Prophet's Ummah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think of the Prophet’s Pool, do you feel a genuine longing to drink from it? What are you doing today to ensure you will be among those who are given that drink?
?
If intercession is a stored mercy from Allah, are you living in a way that relies on it while also striving to obey? How does this truth change the way you view your sins and your hope in Allah's mercy?

The Covenant Taken from Adam and His Offspring
Affirms the reality of the primordial covenant.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the belief in the covenant (Meethaq) that Allah took from Adam and all humans in pre-existence.

Core Idea
The covenant with Allah is a real, binding testament from all souls.

The next affirmation in the passage is the covenant (Meethaq) that Allah took from Adam and his descendants. This refers to the primordial covenant where all souls testified to Allah's lordship, as mentioned in the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Read the Meethaq sentence
Read the sentence about the covenant, noting that it is taken from Adam and his offspring.
2
Relate to Quranic verse

3
Understand its significance
This covenant is a proof (hujjah) against mankind on the Day of Judgment.

Source Text

Divine Foreknowledge of the Count of Inhabitants of Paradise and Hell
Affirms Allah's eternal knowledge of the exact number in Paradise and Hell.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's knowledge of who will enter Paradise and Hell is eternal, complete, and unchanging.

Core Idea
Allah knows eternally the exact number of people in Paradise and Hell, and no change occurs.

The passage then turns to the subject of divine foreknowledge (qadar). It states that Allah has always known the precise number of those who will enter Paradise and Hell, and that number is fixed. This establishes that divine knowledge is not acquired over time but is eternal and unchanging.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on divine foreknowledge
Read the sentence starting from 'وَقَدْ عَلِمَ اللهُ' to understand that Allah's knowledge is eternal.
2
Note the fixity of the number
The text says the number is one totality, not increased or decreased.
3
Reflect on the implications
This does not mean compulsion; it is simply knowledge of what will occur.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالحَوْضُ الَّذِي أَكْرَمَهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى بِهِ غِيَانًا لِأُمَّتِهِ حَقٌّ، وَالشَّفَاعَةُ الَّتِي ادَّخَرَهَا اللهُ لَمْ كَمَا رُوِي فِي الأَخْبَارِ، وَالمِيثَاقُ الَّذِي أَخَذَهُ اللهُ تَعَالَى مِنْ آدَمَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ وَذُرِّيَّتِهِ حَقٌّ. وَقَدْ عَلِمَ اللهُ تَعَالَى فِيمَا لَمْ يَزَلْ عَدَدَ مَنْ يَدْخُلُ الجَنَّةَ وَيَدْخُلُ النَّارَ جُمْلَةٌ وَاحِدَةً لَا يُزَادُ فِي ذَلِكَ العَدَدِ وَلَا يُنْقَصُ مِنْهُ، وَكَذَلِكَ أَفْعَالَهُمْ فِيمَا عَلِمَ مِنْهُمْ أَنَّهُمْ يَفْعَلُونَهُ، وَكُلٌ مُيَسَّرُ مَا خُلِقَ لَهُ. وَالأَعْمَالُ بِالخَوَانِمِ، وَالسَّعِيدُ مَنْ سَعِدَ بِقَضَاءِ اللَّه تَعَالَى وَالشَّفِيُّ مَنْ شَقِي بِقَضَاءِ الله تَعَالَى.

And Allah Most High has always known the number of those who will enter Paradise and those who will enter Hell as one totality, nothing is added to that number nor subtracted from it. Similarly, their actions are as He knew from them that they would do. And everyone is facilitated to that for which he was created. And deeds are according to their endings. And the fortunate is the one who is fortunate by the decree of Allah Most High, and the wretched is the one who is wretched by the decree of Allah Most High.

Commentary
This passage affirms several key beliefs of Ahl al-Sunnah. First, the reality of the Hawd (the Pool) that Allah will grant the Prophet as a provision for his Ummah on the Day of Judgment. Second, the reality of intercession (Shafa'ah) that Allah has stored for the Prophet as narrated in reports. Third, the reality of the covenant (Meethaq) taken from Adam and his descendants. القضاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Allah's foreknowledge compels people to commit sins, leaving no free will.
Correction: Foreknowledge is simply knowledge, not compulsion. People act by their own choice, but Allah knows what they will choose.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, does the number of people in Paradise and Hell change?
A) Yes, it increases with good deeds
B) No, it is fixed and unchangeable
C) It changes only for Hell
D) It is unknown

Key Takeaway
Allah's eternal knowledge fixes the count of people in Paradise and Hell, yet human actions are real.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah already knows your final destination, does that make you more diligent in your actions today or more complacent? Examine your current striving—are you living as if your name is among the fixed number of Paradise? Commit now to one action today that proves you are serious.
?
The passage says no number is added or subtracted. Do you truly believe that your fate is sealed by divine knowledge, yet your choices matter? Pause and consider: does this thought fill you with awe or anxiety? What does your reaction reveal about your trust in Allah's justice?
?
Allah knows every action you will ever do before you do it. How does that change the way you approach your next decision, even a small one? Will you act as if you are being watched, or will you forget? Make a concrete intention right now to be conscious of Allah's knowledge in your next interaction.
